life s handicap. 
be story of mine own people. 
by rudyard kipling. 

to e. k. r. from r. k. c. m. g. 
preface. 
in northern india stand a monastery call the chubara of dhunni bhagat. no one remember who or what dhunni bhagat have be. he have live his life make a little money and spend it all a every good hindu should do on a work of piety the chubara. that be full of brick cell gaily paint with the figure of god and king and elephant where wear out priest could sit and meditate on the latter end of thing. the path be brick pave and the naked foot of thousand have wear them into gutter. clump of mango sprout from between the brick. great pipal tree overhang the well windlass that whine all day. and host of parrot tear through the tree. crow and squirrel be tame in that place for they know that never a priest would touch them. 
the wander mendicant charm seller and holy vagabond for a hundred mile round use to make the chubara their place of call and rest. mahomedan sikh and hindu mix equally under the tree. they be old men and when man ha come to the turnstile of night all the creed in the world seem to him wonderfully alike and colourless. 
gobind the one eye tell me this. he be a holy man who live on an island in the middle of a river and feed the fish with little bread pellet twice a day. in flood time when swell corps strand themselves at the foot of the island gobind would cause them to be piously burn for the sake of the honour of mankind and have regard to his own account with god hereafter. but when two third of the island be tear away in a spate gobind come across the river to dhunni bhagat s chubara he and his brass drink vessel with the well cord round the neck his short arm rest crutch stud with brass nail his roll of bed his big pipe his umbrella and his tall sugar loaf hat with the nod peacock feather in it. he wrap himself up in his patch quilt make of every colour and material in the world sit down in a sunny corner of the very quiet chubara and rest his arm on his short handle crutch wait for death. the people bring him food and little clump of marigold flower and he give his bless in return. he be nearly blind and his face be seam and line and wrinkle beyond belief for he have live in his time which be before the english come within five hundred mile of dhunni bhagat s chubara. 
when we grow to know each other well gobind would tell me tale in a voice most like the rumble of heavy gun over a wooden bridge. his tale be true but not one in twenty could be print in an english book because the english do not think a native do. they brood over matter that a native would dismiss till a fit occasion. and what they would not think twice about a native will brood over till a fit occasion. then native and english stare at each other hopelessly across great gulf of miscomprehension. 
and what say gobind one sunday even be your honour craft and by what manner of mean earn you your daily bread. 
i be say i a kerani one who write with a pen upon paper not be in the service of the government. 
then what do you write. say gobind. come near for i cannot see your countenance and the light fail. 
i write of all matter that lie within my understand and of many that do not. but chiefly i write of life and death and men and woman and love and fate accord to the measure of my ability tell the tale through the mouth of one two or more people. then by the favour of god the tale be sell and money accrue to me that i may keep alive. 
even so say gobind. that be the work of the bazar story teller. but he speak straight to men and woman and doe not write anything at all. only when the tale ha arouse expectation and calamity be about to befall the virtuous he stop suddenly and demand payment ere he continue the narration. be it so in your craft my son. 
i have hear of such thing when a tale be of great length and be sell a a cucumber in small piece. 
ay i be once a famed teller of story when i be beg on the road between koshin and etra. before the last pilgrimage that ever i take to orissa. i tell many tale and hear many more at the rest house in the even when we be merry at the end of the march. it be in my heart that grow men be but a little child in the matter of tale and the old tale be the most beloved. 
with your people that be truth say i. but in regard to our people they desire new tale and when all be write they rise up and declare that the tale be good tell in such and such a manner and doubt either the truth or the invention thereof. 
but what folly be theirs. say gobind throw out his knot hand. a tale that be tell be a true tale a long a the tell last. and of their talk upon it you know how bilas khan that be the prince of tale teller say to one who mock him in the great rest house on the jhelum road. go on my brother and finish that i have begin and he who mock take up the tale but have neither voice nor manner for the task come to a standstill and the pilgrim at supper make him eat abuse and stick half that night. 
nay but with our people money have pass it be their right. a we should turn against a shoeseller in regard to shoe if those wear out. if ever i make a book you shall see and judge. 
and the parrot say to the fall tree wait brother till i fetch a prop. say gobind with a grim chuckle. god ha give me eighty year and it may be some over. i cannot look for more than day grant by day and a a favour at this tide. be swift. 
in what manner be it best to set about the task. say i o chief of those who string pearl with their tongue. 
how do i know. yet he think for a little how should i not know. god ha make very many head but there be only one heart in all the world among your people or my people. they be child in the matter of tale. 
but none be so terrible a the little one if a man misplace a word or in a second tell vary event by so much a one small devil. 
ay i also have tell tale to the little one but do thou this his old eye fell on the gaudy painting of the wall the blue and red dome and the flame of the poinsettia beyond. tell them first of those thing that thou hast see and they have see together. thus their knowledge will piece out thy imperfection. tell them of what thou alone hast see then what thou hast hear and since they be child tell them of battle and king horse devil elephant and angel but omit not to tell them of love and suchlike. all the earth be full of tale to him who listen and doe not drive away the poor from his door. the poor be the best of tale teller. for they must lay their ear to the grind every night. 
after this conversation the idea grow in my head and gobind be press in his inquiry a to the health of the book. 
late when we have be part for month it happen that i be to go away and far off and i come to bid gobind good bye. 
it be farewell between u now for i go a very long journey i say. 
and i also. a long one than thou. but what of the book. say he. 
it will be bear in due season if it be so ordain. 
i would i could see it say the old man huddle beneath his quilt. but that will not be. i die three day hence in the night a little before the dawn. the term of my year be accomplish. 
in nine case out of ten a native make no miscalculation a to the day of his death. he ha the foreknowledge of the beast in this respect. 
then thou wilt depart in peace and it be good talk for thou hast say that life be no delight to thee. 
but it be a pity that our book be not bear. how shall i know that there be any record of my name. 
because i promise in the forepart of the book precede everything else that it shall be write gobind sadhu of the island in the river and await god in dhunni bhagat s chubara first speak of the book say i. 
and give counsel an old man s counsel. gobind son of gobind of the chumi village in the karaon tehsil in the district of mooltan. will that be write also. 
that will be write also. 
and the book will go across the black water to the house of your people and all the sahib will know of me who be eighty year old. 
all who read the book shall know. i cannot promise for the rest. 
that be good talk. call aloud to all who be in the monastery and i will tell them this thing. 
they troop up faquir sadhu sunnyasis byragis nihangs and mullah priest of all faith and every degree of raggedness and gobind lean upon his crutch speak so that they be visibly fill with envy and a white haired senior bid gobind think of his latter end instead of transitory repute in the mouth of stranger. then gobind give me his bless and i come away. 
these tale have be collect from all place and all sort of people from priest in the chubara from ala yar the carver jiwun singh the carpenter nameless men on steamer and train round the world woman spin outside their cottage in the twilight officer and gentleman now dead and bury and a few but these be the very best my father give me. the great part of them have be publish in magazine and newspaper to whose editor i be indebted. but some be new on this side of the water and some have not see the light before. 
the most remarkable story be of course those which do not appear for obvious reason.

the lang men o larut [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
the chief engineer s sleep suit be of yellow strip with blue and his speech be the speech of aberdeen. they sluice the deck under him and he hop on to the ornamental capstan a black pipe between his teeth though the hour be not seven of the morn. 
do you ever hear o the lang men o larut. he ask when the man from orizava have finish a story of an aboriginal giant discover in the wild of brazil. there be never story yet pass the lip of teller but the man from orizava could cap it. 
no we never do we respond with one voice. the man from orizava watch the chief keenly a a possible rival. 
i m not tell the story for the sake of talk merely say the chief but a a warn against bet unless you bet on a perrfect certainty. the lang men o larut be just a certainty. i have have talk wi them. now larut you will understand be a dependency or it may be an outlying possession o the island o penang and there they will get you tin and manganese an it mayhap mica and all manner o meenerals. larut be a great place. 
but what about the population. say the man from orizava. 
the population say the chief slowly be few but enorrmous. you must understand that exceptin the tin mine there be no special inducement to european to reside in larut. the climate be warm and remarkably like the climate o calcutta. and in regard to calcutta it cannot have escape your obsairvation that. 
calcutta isn t larut. and we ve only just come from it protest the man from orizava. there s a meteorological department in calcutta too. 
ay but there s no meteorological department in larut. each man be a law to himself. some drink whisky and some drink brandipanee and some drink cocktail vara bad for the coat o the stomach be a cocktail and some drink sangaree so i have be credibly inform. but one and all they sweat like the pack of piston head on a fourrteen day voyage with the screw race half her time. but a i be say the population o larut be five all tell of english that be to say scotch an i m scotch ye know say the chief. 
the man from orizava light another cigarette and wait patiently. it be hopeless to hurry the chief engineer. 
i be not pretend to account for the population o larut be lay down accord to such fabulous dimension. o the five white men engage upon the extraction o tin ore and mercantile pursuit there be three o the son o anak. wait while i remember. lammitter be the first by two inch a giant in the land an a terreefic man to cross in his way. from heel to head he be six foot nine inch and proportionately build across and through the thickness of his body. six good foot nine inch an overbearin man. next to him and i have forget his precise business be sandy vowle. and he be six foot seven but lean and lathy and it be more in the elasteecity of his neck that the height lay than in any honesty o bone and sinew. five foot and a few odd inch may have be his real height. the remainder come out when he hold up his head and six foot seven he be upon the door sill. i take his measure in chalk standin on a chair. and next to him but a proportionately make man ruddy and of a fair countenance be jock coan that they call the fir cone. he be but six foot five and a child beside lammitter and vowle. when the three walk out together they make a scunner run through the colony o larut. the malay run round them a though they have be the giant tree in the yosemite valley these three lang men o larut. it be perfectly ridiculous a lusus naturae that one little place should have contain maybe the three tall ordinar men upon the face o the earth. 
obsairve now the order o thing. for it lead to the fine big drink in larut and six sore head the morn that endure for a week. i be against immoderate liquor but the event to follow be a justification. you must understand that many coast steamer call at larut wi stranger o the mercantile profession. in the spring time when the young cocoanut be ripen and the tree o the forest be put forth their leaf there come an american man to larut and he be six foot three or it may have be four in his stocking. he come on business from sacramento but he stay for pleasure wi the lang men o larut. le than a half o the population be ordinar in their girth and stature ye will understand howson and nailor merchant five foot nine or thereabouts. he have business with those two and he stand above them from the six foot threedom o his height till they go to drink. in the course o conversation he say a tall men will thing about his height and the trouble of it to him. that be his pride o the flesh. 
a the long man in the island he say but there they take him up and ask if he be sure. 
i say i be the long man in the island he say and on that i ll bet my substance. 
they lay down the bed plate of a big drink then and there and put it aside while they call jock coan from his house near by among the firefly wink. 
how s a wi you. say jock and come in by the side o the sacramento profligate two inch or it may have be one tall than he. 
you re long say the man open his eye. but i be long. an they send a whistle through the night an howkit out sandy vowle from his bite bungalow and he come in an stand by the side o jock an the pair just fillit the room to the ceiling cloth. 
the sacramento man be a euchre player and a most profane sweerer. you hold both bower he say but the joker be with me. 
fair an softly say nailor. jock whaur s lang lammitter. 
here say that man put his leg through the window and come in like an anaconda o the desert furlong by furlong one foot in penang and one in batavia and a hand in north borneo it may be. 
be you suit. say nailor when the hind end o lang lammitter be slide through the sill an the head of lammitter be lose in the smoke away above. 
the american man take out his card and put it on the table. esdras b. long be my name america be my nation frisco be my rest place but this here beat creation say he. boy giant side show giant i mind to slide out of my bet if i have be overtop on the strength of the riddle on this paste board. i would have do it if you have top me even by three inch but when it come to foot yard mile i be not the man to shirk the big drink that ever make the traveller joy palm blush with virginal indignation or the orang outang and the perambulate dyak howl with envy. set them up and continue till the final conclusion. 
o mon i tell you twas an awful sight to see those four giant thresh about the house and the island and tearin down the pillar thereof an throw palm tree broadcast and currling their long leg round the hill o larut. an awfu sight. i be there. i do not mean to tell you but it s out now. i be not overcome for i e en sit me down under the piece o the table at four the morn an meditate upon the strangeness of thing. 
losh yon s the breakfast bell. 
reingelder and the german flag [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
han breitmann paddle across the deck in his pink pyjama a cup of tea in one hand and a cheroot in the other when the steamer be swelter down the coast on her way to singapur. he drink beer all day and all night and play a game call scairt with three compatriot. 
i haf wash say he in a voice of thunder but dere be no use wash on these hell sea. look at me i be still all wet and schweatin. it be d tea dot make me so. boy bring me bilsener on ice. 
you will die if you drink beer before breakfast say one man. beer be the bad thing in the world for. 
ya i know d liver. i haf no liver und i shall not die. at least i will not die obon dese benny sdeamers dot haf no beer fit to trink. if i should haf die i will haf don so a hoondert dime before now in shermany in new york in japon in assam und all over d inside ban of south amerique. also in shamaica should i hat die or in siam but i be here. und d be my orchits dot i have drafelled all the vorld round to find. 
he point towards the wheel where in two rough wooden box lay a mass of shrivel vegetation suppose by all the ship to represent assam orchid of fabulous value. 
now orchid do not grow in the main street of town and han breitmann have go far to get his. there be nothing that he have not collect that year from king crab to white kangaroo. 
lisden now say he after he have be speak for not much more than ten minute without a pause. lisden und i will dell you a sdory to show how bad und bad it be to go gollectin und belief vot anoder fool haf say. dis be in uraguay which be in amerique north or sout you would not know und i be hoontin orchits und aferydings else dot i could back in my kanasters dot be drafelling sbecimen gaces. dere va den mit me anoder man reingelder dot va his name und he va hoontin also but only coral snake joost uraguay coral snake aferykind you could imagine. i dell you a coral snake be a peauty all red und white like coral dot ha be gestrung in band upon d neck of a girl. dere be one snake howefer dot we who gollect know ash d sherman flag pecause id be red und plack und white joost like a sausage mit druffles. reingelder he be naturalist goot man goot trinker good a me. by gott say reingelder i will get a sherman flag snake or i will die. und we toorned all uraguay upside behint all pecause of dot sherman flag. 
von day when we be in none know where shwingin in our hummock among d wood oop come a natif woman mit a sherman flag in a bickle bottle my bickle bottle und we both fell from our hummock flat ubon our pot what you call stomach mit shoy at dis thing. now i be gollectin orchits also und i know dot d idee of life to reingelder va dis sherman flag. derefore i bicked myselfs oop und i say reingelder dot be your find. heart s true friend dou art a goot man say reingelder und mit dot he obens d bickle bottle und d natif woman she shqueals. herr gott. it will bite. i say pecause in uraguay a man must be careful of d insect reingelder shpifligate her in d alcohol und den she will be all right. nein say reingelder i will d shnake alife examine. dere be no fear. d coral shnakes be mitout shting apparatus brofided. boot i look at her het und she va d het of a boison shnake d true viper cranium narrow und contract. it be not goot say i she may bite und den we be tree hoondert mile from aferywheres. broduce d alcohol und bickle him alife. reingelder he have him in his hand grawlin und grawlin a slow a a woorm und dwice a guiet. nonsense say reingelder. yates haf say dot not von of d coral shnakes haf d sack of boison. yates va d crate authorite ubon d reptilia of sout amerique. he haf write a book. you do not know of course but he va a crate authorite. 
i gum my eye upon d sherman flag grawlin und grawlin in reingelder s fist und d het va not d het of innocence. mein gott i say. it be you dot will get d sack d sack from dis life here pelow. 
den you may haf d shnake say reingelder pattin it ubon her het. see now i will show you vat yates haf write. 
uud mit dot he go indo his dent unt brung out his big book of yates. d sherman flag grawlin in his fist. yates haf say say reingelder und he throw oben d book in d fork of his fist und read d passage proofin conglusivement dot nefer coral shnake bite va boison. den he shut d book mit a bang und dot shqueeze d sherman flag und she nip once und dwice. 
d liddle fool he haf bite me say reingelder. 
dese thing be before we know apout d permanganat potash injection. i be discomfordable. 
die oop d arm reingelder say i und trink whisky ontil you can no more trink. 
trink ten tousand tevils. i will go to dinner say reingelder und he put her afay und it va very red mit emotion. 
we lifed upon soup horse flesh und bean for dinner but before we va eat d soup reingelder he haf hold of his arm und cry it be genumben to d clavicle. i be a dead man. und yates he haf lie in brint. 
i dell you it va most sad for d symbtoms dot come va all dose of strychnine. he va double into big knot und den undoubled und den redouble mooch bad dan pefore und he froth. i va mit him say reingelder dost dou know me. but he himself d inward gonsciousness part be peyond knowledge und so i know he va not in bain. den he wrop himself oop in von dremendous knot und den he die all alone mit me in uraguay. i be sorry for i lofed reingelder und i puried him und den i take d coral shnake dot sherman flag so bad und dreacherous und i bickled him alife. 
so i get him. und so i lose reingelder. 
the wander jew [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
if you go once round the world in an easterly direction you gain one day say the men of science to john hay. in after year john hay go east west north and south transact business make love and beget a family a have do many men and the scientific information above record lay neglect in the deep of his mind with a thousand other matter of equal importance. 
when a rich relative die he find himself wealthy beyond any reasonable expectation that he have entertain in his previous career which have be a chequer and evil one. indeed long before the legacy come to him there exist in the brain of john hay a little cloud a momentary obscuration of think that come and go almost before he could realize that there be any solution of continuity. so do the bat flit round the eaves of a house to show that the darkness be fall. he enter upon great possession in money land and house. but behind his delight stand a ghost that cry out that his enjoyment of these thing should not be of long duration. it be the ghost of the rich relative who have be permit to return to earth to torture his nephew into the grave. wherefore under the spur of this constant reminder john hay always preserve the air of heavy business like stolidity that hide the shadow on his mind turn investment house and land into sovereign rich round red english sovereign each one worth twenty shilling. land may become valueless and house fly heavenward on the wing of red flame but till the day of judgment a sovereign will always be a sovereign that be to say a king of pleasure. 
possess of his sovereign john hay would fain have spend them one by one on such coarse amusement a his soul love. but he be haunt by the instant fear of death. for the ghost of his relative stand in the hall of his house close to the hat rack shout up the stairway that life be short that there be no hope of increase of day and that the undertaker be already rough out his nephew s coffin. john hay be generally alone in the house and even when he have company his friend could not hear the clamorous uncle. the shadow inside his brain grow large and black. his fear of death be drive john hay mad. 
then from the deep of his mind where he have stow away all his discard information rise to light the scientific fact of the easterly journey. on the next occasion that his uncle shout up the stairway urge him to make haste and live a shrill voice cry who go round the world once easterly gain one day. 
his grow diffidence and distrust of mankind make john hay unwilling to give this precious message of hope to his friend. they might take it up and analyse it. he be sure it be true but it would pain him acutely be rough hand to examine it too closely. to him alone of all the toil generation of mankind have the secret of immortality be vouchsafe. it would be impious against all the design of the creator to set mankind hurry eastward. besides this would crowd the steamer inconveniently and john hay wish of all thing to be alone. if he could get round the world in two month some one of whom he have read he could not remember the name have cover the passage in eighty day he would gain a clear day. and by steadily continue to do it for thirty year would gain one hundred and eighty day or nearly the half of a year. it would not be much but in course of time a civilisation advance and the euphrates valley railway be open he could improve the pace. 
arm with many sovereign john hay in the thirty fifth year of his age set forth on his travel two voice bear him company from dover a he sail to calais. fortune favour him. the euphrates valley railway be newly open and he be the first man who take ticket direct from calais to calcutta thirteen day in the train. thirteen day in the train be not good for the nerve. but he cover the world and return to calais from america in twelve day over the two month and start afresh with four and twenty hour of precious time to his credit. three year pass and john hay religiously go round this earth seek for more time wherein to enjoy the remainder of his sovereign. he become know on many line a the man who want to go on. when people ask him what he be and what he do he answer. 
i m the person who intend to live and i be try to do it now. 
his day be divide between watch the white wake spin behind the stern of the swift steamer or the brown earth flash past the window of the fast train. and he note in a pocket book every minute that he have rail or screw out of remorseless eternity. 
this be good than pray for long life quoth john hay a he turn his face eastward for his twentieth trip. the year have do more for him than he dare to hope. 
by the extension of the brahmaputra valley line to meet the newly develop china midland the calais railway ticket hold good via karachi and calcutta to hongkong. the round trip could be manage in a fraction over forty seven day and fill with fatal exultation john hay tell the secret of his longevity to his only friend the house keeper of his room in london. he speak and pass. but the woman be one of resource and immediately take counsel with the lawyer who have first inform john hay of his golden legacy. very many sovereign still remain and another hay long to spend them on thing more sensible than railway ticket and steamer accommodation. 
the chase be long for when a man be journey literally for the dear life he doe not tarry upon the road. round the world hay sweep anew and overtake the weary doctor who have be send out to look for him in madras. it be there that he find the reward of his toil and the assurance of a bless immortality. in half an hour the doctor watch always the parch lip the shake hand and the eye that turn eternally to the east win john hay to rest in a little house close to the madras surf. all that hay need do be to hang by rope from the roof of the room and let the round earth swing free beneath him. this be good than steamer or train for he gain a day in a day and be thus the equal of the undying sun. the other hay would pay his expense throughout eternity. 
it be true that we cannot yet take ticket from calais to hongkong though that will come about in fifteen year. but men say that if you wander along the southern coast of india you shall find in a neatly whitewash little bungalow sit in a chair swing from the roof over a sheet of thin steel which he know so well destroy the attraction of the earth an old and wear man who for ever face the rise sun a stop watch in his hand race against eternity. he cannot drink he doe not smoke and his live expense amount to perhaps twenty five rupee a month but he be john hay the immortal. without he hear the thunder of the wheel world with which he be careful to explain he ha no connection whatever. but if you say that it be only the noise of the surf he will cry bitterly for the shadow on his brain be pass away a the brain cease to work and he doubt sometimes whether the doctor speak the truth. 
why doe not the sun always remain over my head. ask john hay. 
through the fire [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
the policeman ride through the himalayan forest under the moss drape oak and his orderly trot after him. 
it s an ugly business bhere singh say the policeman. where be they. 
it be a very ugly business say bhere singh. and a for them they be doubtless now fry in a hot fire than be ever make of spruce branch. 
let u hope not say the policeman for allow for the difference between race and race it s the story of francesca da rimini bhere singh. 
bhere singh know nothing about francesca da rimini so he hold his peace until they come to the charcoal burner clear where the die flame say whit whit whit a they flutter and whisper over the white ash. it must have be a great fire when at full height. men have see it at donga pa across the valley wink and blaze through the night and say that the charcoal burner of kodru be get drink. but it be only suket singh sepoy of the load punjab native infantry and athira a woman burn burn burn. 
this be how thing befall. and the policeman s diary will bear me out. 
athira be the wife of madu who be a charcoal burner one eye and of a malignant disposition. a week after their marriage he beat athira with a heavy stick. a month late suket singh sepoy come that way to the cool hill on leave from his regiment and electrify the villager of kodru with tale of service and glory under the government and the honour in which he suket singh be hold by the colonel sahib bahadur. and desdemona listen to othello a desdemonas have do all the world over and a she listen she love. 
i ve a wife of my own say suket singh though that be no matter when you come to think of it. i be also due to return to my regiment after a time and i cannot be a deserter i who intend to be havildar. there be no himalayan version of i could not love thee dear a much love i not honour more. but suket singh come near to make one. 
never mind say athira stay with me and if madu try to beat me you beat him. 
very good say suket singh. and he beat madu severely to the delight of all the charcoal burner of kodru. 
that be enough say suket singh a he roll madu down the hillside. now we shall have peace. but madu crawl up the grass slope again and hover round his hut with angry eye. 
he ll kill me dead say athira to suket singh. you must take me away. 
there ll be a trouble in the line. my wife will pull out my beard. but never mind say suket singh i will take you. 
there be loud trouble in the line and suket singh s beard be pull and suket singh s wife go to live with her mother and take away the child. that s all right say athira. and suket singh say yes that s all right. 
so there be only madu leave in the hut that look across the valley to donga pa. and since the begin of time no one ha have any sympathy for husband so unfortunate a madu. 
he go to juseen daze the wizard man who keep the talk monkey s head. 
get me back my wife say madu. 
i can t say juseen daze until you have make the sutlej in the valley run up the donga pa. 
no riddle say madu and he shake his hatchet above juseen daze s white head. 
give all your money to the headman of the village say juseen daze. and they will hold a communal council and the council will send a message that your wife must come back. 
so madu give up all his worldly wealth amount to twenty seven rupee eight anna three pice and a silver chain to the council of kodru. and it fell a juseen daze foretell. 
they send athira s brother down into suket singh s regiment to call athira home. suket singh kick him once round the line and then hand him over to the havildar who beat him with a belt. 
come back yell athira s brother. 
where to. say athira. 
to madu say he. 
never say she. 
then juseen daze will send a curse and you will wither away like a bark tree in the springtime say athira s brother. athira sleep over these thing. 
next morning she have rheumatism. i be begin to wither away like a bark tree in the springtime she say. that be the curse of juseen daze. 
and she really begin to wither away because her heart be dry up with fear and those who believe in curse die from curse. suket singh too be afraid because he love athira good than his very life. two month pass and athira s brother stand outside the regimental line again and yelp aha. you be wither away. come back. 
i will come back say athira. 
say rather that we will come back say suket singh. 
ai. but when. say athira s brother. 
upon a day very early in the morning say suket singh. and he tramp off to apply to the colonel sahib bahadur for one week s leave. 
i be wither away like a bark tree in the spring moan athira. 
you will be good soon say suket singh. and he tell her what be in his heart and the two laugh together softly for they love each other. but athira grow good from that hour. 
they go away together travel third class by train a the regulation provide and then in a cart to the low hill and on foot to the high one. athira sniff the scent of the pine of her own hill the wet himalayan hill. it be good to be alive say athira. 
hah. say suket singh. where be the kodru road and where be the forest ranger s house. 
it cost forty rupee twelve year ago say the forest ranger hand the gun. 
here be twenty say suket singh and you must give me the best bullet. 
it be very good to be alive say athira wistfully sniff the scent of the pine mould. and they wait till the night have fall upon kodru and the donga pa. madu have stack the dry wood for the next day s charcoal burn on the spur above his house. it be courteous in madu to save u this trouble say suket singh a he stumble on the pile which be twelve foot square and four high. we must wait till the moon rise. 
when the moon rise athira kneel upon the pile. if it be only a government snide say suket singh ruefully squint down the wire bind barrel of the forest ranger s gun. 
be quick say athira. and suket singh be quick. but athira be quick no long. then he light the pile at the four corner and climb on to it re load the gun. 
the little flame begin to peer up between the big log atop of the brushwood. the government should teach u to pull the trigger with our toe say suket singh grimly to the moon. that be the last public observation of sepoy suket singh. 
upon a day early in the morning madu come to the pyre and shriek very grievously and run away to catch the policeman who be on tour in the district. 
the base bear ha ruin four rupee worth of charcoal wood madu gasp. he ha also kill my wife and he ha leave a letter which i cannot read tie to a pine bough. 
in the stiff formal hand teach in the regimental school sepoy suket singh have write. 
let u be burn together if anything remain over for we have make the necessary prayer. we have also curse madu and malak the brother of athira both evil men. send my service to the colonel sahib bahadur. 
the policeman look long and curiously at the marriage bed of red and white ash on which lay dull black the barrel of the ranger s gun. he drive his spur heel absently into a half char log and the chatter spark fly upwards. most extraordinary people say the policeman. 
whe w whew ouiou say the little flame. 
the policeman enter the dry bone of the case for the punjab government doe not approve of romance in his diary. 
but who will pay me those four rupee. say madu. 
the finance of the god [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
the even meal be end in dhunni bhagat s chubara and the old priest be smoke or count their bead. a little naked child patter in with it mouth wide open a handful of marigold flower in one hand and a lump of conserve tobacco in the other. it try to kneel and make obeisance to gobind but it be so fat that it fell forward on it shave head and roll on it side kick and gasp while the marigold tumble one way and the tobacco the other. gobind laugh set it up again and bless the marigold flower a he receive the tobacco. 
from my father say the child. he ha the fever and cannot come. wilt thou pray for him father. 
surely little. but the smoke be on the grind and the night chill be in the air and it be not good to go abroad naked in the autumn. 
i have no clothe say the child and all to day i have be carry cow dung cake to the bazar. it be very hot and i be very tire. it shiver a little for the twilight be cool. 
gobind lift an arm under his vast tattered quilt of many colour and make an invite little nest by his side. the child creep in and gobind fill his brass stud leather waterpipe with the new tobacco. when i come to the chubara the shave head with the tuft atop and the beady black eye look out of the fold of the quilt a a squirrel look out from his nest and gobind be smile while the child play with his beard. 
i would have say something friendly but remember in time that if the child fell ill afterwards i should be credit with the evil eye and that be a horrible possession. 
sit thou still thumbling i say a it make to get up and run away. where be thy slate and why ha the teacher let such an evil character loose on the street when there be no police to protect u weakling. in which ward dost thou try to break thy neck with fly kite from the house top. 
nay sahib nay say the child burrow it face into gobind s beard and twist uneasily. there be a holiday to day among the school and i do not always fly kite. i play k li kit like the rest. 
cricket be the national game among the schoolboy of the punjab from the naked hedge school child who use an old kerosene tin for wicket to the b. a. s of the university who compete for the championship belt. 
thou play kerlikit. thou art half the height of the bat. i say. 
the child nod resolutely. yea i do play. perlayball ow at. run run run. i know it all. 
but thou must not forget with all this to pray to the god accord to custom say gobind who do not altogether approve of cricket and western innovation. 
i do not forget say the child in a hush voice. 
also to give reverence to thy teacher and gobind s voice soften to abstain from pull holy men by the beard little badling. eh eh eh. 
the child s face be altogether hide in the great white beard and it begin to whimper till gobind soothe it a child be soothe all the world over with the promise of a story. 
i do not think to frighten thee senseless little one. look up. be i angry. be be be. shall i weep too and of our tear make a great pond and drown u both and then thy father will never get well lack thee to pull his beard. peace peace and i will tell thee of the god. thou hast hear many tale. 
very many father. 
now this be a new one which thou hast not hear. long and long ago when the god walk with men a they do to day but that we have not faith to see shiv the great of god and parbati his wife be walk in the garden of a temple. 
which temple. that in the nandgaon ward. say the child. 
nay very far away. maybe at trimbak or hurdwar whither thou must make pilgrimage when thou art a man. now there be sit in the garden under the jujube tree a mendicant that have worship shiv for forty year and he live on the offering of the pious and meditate holiness night and day. 
oh father be it thou. say the child look up with large eye. 
nay i have say it be long ago and moreover this mendicant be marry. 
do they put him on a horse with flower on his head and forbid him to go to sleep all night long. thus they do to me when they make my wed say the child who have be marry a few month before. 
and what didst thou do. say i. 
i weep and they call me evil name and then i smite her and we weep together. 
thus do not the mendicant say gobind. for he be a holy man and very poor. parbati perceive him sit naked by the temple step where all go up and down and she say to shiv what shall men think of the god when the god thus scorn their worshipper. for forty year yonder man ha pray to u and yet there be only a few grain of rice and some break cowry before him after all. men s heart will be harden by this thing. and shiv say it shall be look to and so he call to the temple which be the temple of his son ganesh of the elephant head say son there be a mendicant without who be very poor. what wilt thou do for him. then that great elephant head one awake in the dark and answer in three day if it be thy will he shall have one lakh of rupee. then shiv and parbati go away. 
but there be a money lender in the garden hide among the marigold the child look at the ball of crumple blossom in it hand ay among the yellow marigold and he hear the god talk. he be a covetous man and of a black heart and he desire that lakh of rupee for himself. so he go to the mendicant and say o brother how much do the pious give thee daily. the mendicant say i cannot tell. sometimes a little rice sometimes a little pulse and a few cowry and it ha be pickle mango and dry fish. 
that be good say the child smack it lip. 
then say the money lender because i have long watch thee and learn to love thee and thy patience i will give thee now five rupee for all thy earn of the three day to come. there be only a bond to sign on the matter. but the mendicant say thou art mad. in two month i do not receive the worth of five rupee and he tell the thing to his wife that even. she be a woman say when do money lender ever make a bad bargain. the wolf run through the corn for the sake of the fat deer. our fate be in the hand of the god. pledge it not even for three day. 
so the mendicant return to the money lender and would not sell. then that wicked man sit all day before him offer more and more for those three day earn. first ten fifty and a hundred rupee. and then for he do not know when the god would pour down their gift rupee by the thousand till he have offer half a lakh of rupee. upon this sum the mendicant s wife shift her counsel and the mendicant sign the bond and the money be pay in silver. great white bullock bring it by the cartload. but save only all that money the mendicant receive nothing from the god at all and the heart of the money lender be uneasy on account of expectation. therefore at noon of the third day the money lender go into the temple to spy upon the council of the god and to learn in what manner that gift might arrive. even a he be make his prayer a crack between the stone of the floor gap and close catch him by the heel. then he hear the god walk in the temple in the darkness of the column and shiv call to his son ganesh say son what hast thou do in regard to the lakh of rupee for the mendicant. and ganesh wake for the money lender hear the dry rustle of his trunk uncoil and he answer father one half of the money ha be pay and the debtor for the other half i hold here fast by the heel. 
the child bubble with laughter. and the moneylender pay the mendicant. it say. 
surely for he whom the god hold by the heel must pay to the uttermost. the money be pay at even all silver in great cart and thus ganesh do his work. 
nathu. ohe nathu. 
a woman be call in the dusk by the door of the courtyard. 
the child begin to wriggle. that be my mother it say. 
go then little answer gobind. but stay a moment. 
he rip a generous yard from his patchwork quilt put it over the child s shoulder and the child run away. 
the amir s homily [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
his royal highness abdur rahman amir of afghanistan g. c. s. i. and trust ally of her imperial majesty the queen of england and empress of india be a gentleman for whom all right think people should have a profound regard. like most other ruler he govern not a he would but a he can and the mantle of his authority cover the most turbulent race under the star. to the afghan neither life property law nor kingship be sacred when his own lust prompt him to rebel. he be a thief by instinct a murderer by heredity and train and frankly and bestially immoral by all three. none the le he ha his own crook notion of honour and his character be fascinate to study. on occasion he will fight without reason give till he be hack in piece. on other occasion he will refuse to show fight till he be drive into a corner. herein he be a unaccountable a the gray wolf who be his blood brother. 
and these men his highness rule by the only weapon that they understand the fear of death which among some oriental be the begin of wisdom. some say that the amir s authority reach no farther than a rifle bullet can range. but a none be quite certain when their king may be in their midst and a he alone hold every one of the thread of government his respect be increase among men. gholam hyder the commander in chief of the afghan army be fear reasonably for he can impale. all kabul city fear the governor of kabul who ha power of life and death through all the ward. but the amir of afghanistan though outlying tribe pretend otherwise when his back be turn be dread beyond chief and governor together. his word be red law. by the gust of his passion fall the leaf of man s life and his favour be terrible. he ha suffer many thing and be a hunt fugitive before he come to the throne and he understand all the class of his people. by the custom of the east any man or woman have a complaint to make or an enemy against whom to be avenge ha the right of speak face to face with the king at the daily public audience. this be personal government a it be in the day of harun al raschid of bless memory whose time exist still and will exist long after the english have pass away. 
the privilege of open speech be of course exercise at certain personal risk. the king may be please and raise the speaker to honour for that very bluntness of speech which three minute late bring a too imitative petitioner to the edge of the ever ready blade. and the people love to have it so for it be their right. 
it happen upon a day in kabul that the amir choose to do his day s work in the baber garden which lie a short distance from the city of kabul. a light table stand before him and round the table in the open air be group general and finance minister accord to their degree. the court and the long tail of feudal chief men of blood feed and cow by blood stand in an irregular semicircle round the table and the wind from the kabul orchard blow among them. all day long sweat courier dash in with letter from the outlying district with rumour of rebellion intrigue famine failure of payment or announcement of treasure on the road. and all day long the amir would read the docket and pas such of these a be le private to the official whom they directly concern or call up a wait chief for a word of explanation. it be well to speak clearly to the ruler of afghanistan. then the grim head under the black astrachan cap with the diamond star in front would nod gravely and that chief would return to his fellow. once that afternoon a woman clamour for divorce against her husband who be bald and the amir hear both side of the case bid her pour curd over the bare scalp and lick them off that the hair might grow again and she be content. here the court laugh and the woman withdraw curse her king under her breath. 
but when twilight be fall and the order of the court be a little relax there come before the king in custody a tremble haggard wretch sore with much buffet but of stout enough build who have steal three rupee of such small matter doe his highness take cognisance. 
why do you steal. say he. and when the king ask question they do themselves service who answer directly. 
i be poor and no one give. hungry and there be no food. 
why do you not work. 
i could find no work protector of the poor and i be starve. 
you lie. you steal for drink for lust for idleness for anything but hunger since any man who will may find work and daily bread. 
the prisoner drop his eye. he have attend the court before and he know the ring of the death tone. 
any man may get work. who know this so well a i do. for i too have be hunger not like you bastard scum but a any honest man may be by the turn of fate and the will of god. 
grow warm the amir turn to his noble all arow and thrust the hilt of his sabre aside with his elbow. 
you have hear this son of lie. hear me tell a true tale. i also be once starve and tighten my belt on the sharp belly pinch. nor be i alone for with me be another who do not fail me in my evil day when i be hunt before ever i come to this throne. and wander like a houseless dog by kandahar my money melt melt melt till he fling out a bare palm before the audience. and day upon day faint and sick i go back to that one who wait and god know how we live till on a day i take our best lihaf silk it be fine work of iran such a no needle now work warm and a coverlet for two and all that we have. i bring it to a money lender in a bylane and i ask for three rupee upon it. he say to me who be now the king you be a thief. this be worth three hundred. i be no thief i answer but a prince of good blood and i be hungry. prince of wander beggar say that money lender i have no money with me but go to my house with my clerk and he will give you two rupee eight anna for that be all i will lend. so i go with the clerk to the house and we talk on the way and he give me the money. we live on it till it be spend and we fare hard. and then that clerk say be a young man of a good heart surely the money lender will lend yet more on that lihaf and he offer me two rupee. these i refuse say nay. but get me some work. and he get me work and i even i abdur rahman amir of afghanistan work day by day a a coolie bear burden and labour of my hand receive four anna wage a day for my sweat and backache. but he this bastard son of naught must steal. for a year and four month i work and none dare say that i lie for i have a witness even that clerk who be now my friend. 
then there rise in his place among the sirdar and the noble one clothe in silk who fold his hand and say this be the truth of god for i who by the favour of god and the amir be such a you know be once clerk to that money lender. 
there be a pause and the amir cry hoarsely to the prisoner throw scorn upon him till he end with the dread dar arid which clinch justice. 
so they lead the thief away and the whole of him be see no more together. and the court rustle out of it silence whisper before god and the prophet but this be a man. 
jew in shushan [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
my newly purchase house furniture be at the least insecure. the leg part from the chair and the top from the table on the slight provocation. but such a it be it be to be pay for and ephraim agent and collector for the local auctioneer wait in the verandah with the receipt. he be announce by the mahomedan servant a ephraim yahudi ephraim the jew. he who belief in the brotherhood of man should hear my elahi bukhsh grind the second word through his white teeth with all the scorn he dare show before his master. ephraim be personally meek in manner so meek indeed that one could not understand how he have fall into the profession of bill collect. he resemble an over feed sheep and his voice suit his figure. there be a fix unvarying mask of childish wonder upon his face. if you pay him he be a one marvel at your wealth. if you send him away he seem puzzle at your hard heartedness. never be jew more unlike his dread breed. ephraim wear list slipper and coat of duster cloth so preposterously pattern that the most brazen of british subaltern would have shy from them in fear. very slow and deliberate be his speech and carefully guard to give offence to no one. after many week ephraim be induce to speak to me of his friend. 
there be eight of u in shushan and we be wait till there be ten. then we shall apply for a synagogue and get leave from calcutta. to day we have no synagogue. and i only i be priest and butch to our people. i be of the tribe of judah i think but i be not sure. my father be of the tribe of judah and we wish much to get our synagogue. i shall be a priest of that synagogue. 
shushan be a big city in the north of india count it dweller by the ten thousand. and these eight of the choose people be shut up in it midst wait till time or chance send them their full congregation. 
miriam the wife of ephraim two little child an orphan boy of their people epraim s uncle jackrael israel a white haired old man his wife hester a jew from cutch one hyem benjamin and ephraim priest and butch make up the list of the jew in shushan. they live in one house on the outskirt of the great city amid heap of saltpetre rotten brick herd of kine and a fix pillar of dust cause by the incessant pass of the beast to the river to drink. in the even the child of the city come to the waste place to fly their kite and ephraim s son hold aloof watch the sport from the roof but never descend to take part in them. at the back of the house stand a small brick enclosure in which ephraim prepare the daily meat for his people after the custom of the jew. once the rude door of the square be suddenly smash open by a struggle from inside and show the meek bill collector at his work nostril dilate lip draw back over his teeth and his hand upon a half madden sheep. he be attire in strange raiment have no relation whatever to duster coat or list slipper and a knife be in his mouth. a he struggle with the animal between the wall the breath come from him in thick sob and the nature of the man seem change. when the ordain slaughter be end he saw that the door be open and shut it hastily his hand leave a red mark on the timber while his child from the neighbour house top look down awe stricken and open eye. a glimpse of ephraim busy in one of his religious capacity be no thing to be desire twice. 
summer come upon shushan turn the tread waste grind to iron and bring sickness to the city. 
it will not touch u say ephraim confidently. before the winter we shall have our synagogue. my brother and his wife and child be come up from calcutta and then i shall be the priest of the synagogue. 
jackrael israel the old man would crawl out in the stifle evening to sit on the rubbish heap and watch the corps be bear down to the river. 
it will not come near u say jackrael israel feebly for we be the people of god and my nephew will be priest of our synagogue. let them die. he creep back to his house again and bar the door to shut himself off from the world of the gentile. 
but miriam the wife of ephraim look out of the window at the dead a the bier pass and say that she be afraid. ephraim comfort her with hope of the synagogue to be and collect bill a be his custom. 
in one night the two child die and be bury early in the morning by ephraim. the death never appear in the city return. the sorrow be my sorrow say ephraim. and this to him seem a sufficient reason for set at naught the sanitary regulation of a large flourish and remarkably well govern empire. 
the orphan boy dependent on the charity of ephraim and his wife could have felt no gratitude and must have be a ruffian. he beg for whatever money his protector would give him and with that flee down country for his life. a week after the death of her child miriam leave her bed at night and wander over the country to find them. she hear them cry behind every bush or drown in every pool of water in the field and she beg the cartmen on the grand trunk road not to steal her little one from her. in the morning the sun rise and beat upon her bare head and she turn into the cool wet crop to lie down and never come back. though hyem benjamin and ephraim seek her for two night. 
the look of patient wonder on ephraim s face deepen but he presently find an explanation. there be so few of u here and these people be so many say he that it may be our god ha forget u. 
in the house on the outskirt of the city old jackrael israel and hester grumble that there be no one to wait on them and that miriam have be untrue to her race. ephraim go out and collect bill and in the evening smoke with hyem benjamin till one dawn hyem benjamin die have first pay all his debt to ephraim. jackrael israel and hester sit alone in the empty house all day and when ephraim return weep the easy tear of age till they cry themselves asleep. 
a week late ephraim stagger under a huge bundle of clothe and cook pot lead the old man and woman to the railway station where the bustle and confusion make them whimper. 
we be go back to calcutta say ephraim to whose sleeve hester be cling. there be more of u there and here my house be empty. 
he help hester into the carriage and turn back say to me i should have be priest of the synagogue if there have be ten of u. surely we must have be forget by our god. 
the remnant of the break colony pass out of the station on their journey south. while a subaltern turn over the book on the bookstall be whistle to himself the ten little nigger boy. 
but the tune sound a solemn a the dead march. 
it be the dirge of the jew in shushan. 
the limitation of pambe serang [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
if you consider the circumstance of the case it be the only thing that he could do. but pambe serang ha be hang by the neck till he be dead and nurkeed be dead also. 
three year ago when the elsass lothringen steamer saarbruck be coal at aden and the weather be very hot indeed nurkeed the big fat zanzibar stoker who feed the second right furnace thirty foot down in the hold get leave to go ashore. he depart a seedee boy a they call the stoker. he return the full blood sultan of zanzibar his highness sayyid burgash with a bottle in each hand. then he sit on the fore hatch grate eat salt fish and onion and sing the song of a far country. the food belong to pambe the serang or head man of the lascar sailor. he have just cook it for himself turn to borrow some salt and when he come back nurkeed s dirty black finger be spade into the rice. 
a serang be a person of importance far above a stoker though the stoker draw good pay. he set the chorus of hya. hulla. hee ah. heh. when the captain s gig be pull up to the davit. he heave the lead too. and sometimes when all the ship be lazy he put on his white muslin and a big red sash and play with the passenger child on the quarter deck. then the passenger give him money and he save it all up for an orgie at bombay or calcutta or pulu penang. ho. you fat black barrel you re eat my food. say pambe in the other lingua franca that begin where the levant tongue stop and run from port say eastward till east be west and the seal brig of the kurile island gossip with the stray hakodate junk. 
son of eblis monkey face dry shark s liver pigman i be the sultan sayyid burgash and the commander of all this ship. take away your garbage. and nurkeed thrust the empty pewter rice plate into pambe s hand. 
pambe beat it into a basin over nurkeed s woolly head. nurkeed draw his sheath knife and stab pambe in the leg. pambe draw his sheath knife. but nurkeed drop down into the darkness of the hold and spat through the grate at pambe who be stain the clean fore deck with his blood. 
only the white moon saw these thing. for the officer be look after the coal and the passenger be toss in their close cabin. all right say pambe and go forward to tie up his leg we will settle the account late on. 
he be a malay bear in india. marry once in burma where his wife have a cigar shop on the shwe dagon road. once in singapore to a chinese girl. and once in madras to a mahomedan woman who sell fowl. the english sailor cannot owe to postal and telegraph facility marry a profusely a he use to do. but native sailor can be uninfluenced by the barbarous invention of the western savage. pambe be a good husband when he happen to remember the existence of a wife. but he be also a very good malay. and it be not wise to offend a malay because he doe not forget anything. moreover in pambe s case blood have be draw and food spoil. 
next morning nurkeed rise with a blank mind. he be no long sultan of zanzibar but a very hot stoker. so he go on deck and open his jacket to the morning breeze till a sheath knife come like a fly fish and stick into the woodwork of the cook s galley half an inch from his right armpit. he run down below before his time try to remember what he could have say to the owner of the weapon. at noon when all the ship s lascar be feed nurkeed advance into their midst and be a placid man with a large regard for his own skin he open negotiation say men of the ship last night i be drink and this morning i know that i behave unseemly to some one or another of you. who be that man that i may meet him face to face and say that i be drink. 
pambe measure the distance to nurkeed s naked breast. if he spring at him he might be trip up and a blind blow at the chest sometimes only mean a gash on the breast bone. rib be difficult to thrust between unless the subject be asleep. so he say nothing. nor do the other lascar. their face immediately drop all expression a be the custom of the oriental when there be kill on the carpet or any chance of trouble. nurkeed look long at the white eyeball. he be only an african and could not read character. a big sigh almost a groan break from him and he go back to the furnace. the lascar take up the conversation where he have interrupt it. they talk of the best method of cook rice. 
nurkeed suffer considerably from lack of fresh air during the run to bombay. he only come on deck to breathe when all the world be about. and even then a heavy block once drop from a derrick within a foot of his head and an apparently firm lash grate on which he set his foot begin to turn over with the intention of drop him on the case cargo fifteen foot below. and one insupportable night the sheath knife drop from the fo c s le and this time it draw blood. so nurkeed make complaint. and when the saarbruck reach bombay flee and bury himself among eight hundred thousand people and do not sign article till the ship have be a month go from the port. pambe wait too. but his bombay wife grow clamorous and he be force to sign in the spicheren to hongkong because he realise that all play and no work give jack a rag shirt. in the foggy china sea he think a great deal of nurkeed and when elsass lothringen steamer lay in port with the spicheren inquire after him and find he have go to england via the cape on the gravelotte. pambe come to england on the worth. the spicheren meet her by the nore light. nurkeed be go out with the spicheren to the calicut coast. 
want to find a friend my trap mouth coal scuttle. say a gentleman in the mercantile service. nothing easy. wait at the nyanza dock till he come. every one come to the nyanza dock. wait you poor heathen. the gentleman speak truth. there be three great door in the world where if you stand long enough you shall meet any one you wish. the head of the suez canal be one but there death come also. char cross station be the second for inland work. and the nyanza dock be the third. at each of these place be men and woman look eternally for those who will surely come. so pambe wait at the dock. time be no object to him. and the wife could wait a he do from day to day week to week and month to month by the blue diamond funnel the red dot smoke stack the yellow streak and the nameless dingy gypsy of the sea that load and unload jostle whistle and roar in the everlasting fog. when money fail a kind gentleman tell pambe to become a christian. and pambe become one with great speed get his religious teaching between ship and ship s arrival and six or seven shilling a week for distribute tract to mariner. what the faith be pambe do not in the least care. but he know if he say native ki li ti an sar to men with long black coat he might get a few copper. and the tract be vendible at a little public house that sell shag by the dottel which be even small weight than the half screw which be le than the half ounce and a most profitable retail trade. 
but after eight month pambe fell sick with pneumonia contract from long stand still in slush. and much against his will he be force to lie down in his two and sixpenny room rag against fate. 
the kind gentleman sit by his bedside and grieve to find that pambe talk in strange tongue instead of listen to good book and almost seem to become a benight heathen again till one day he be rouse from semi stupor by a voice in the street by the dock head. my friend he whisper pambe. call now call nurkeed. quick. god ha send him. 
he want one of his own race say the kind gentleman. and go out he call nurkeed. at the top of his voice. an excessively colour man in a rasp white shirt and brand new slop a shin hat and a breastpin turn round. many voyage have teach nurkeed how to spend his money and make him a citizen of the world. 
hi. yes. say he when the situation be explain. command him black nigger when i be in the saarbruck. ole pambe good ole pambe. dam lascar. show him up sar. and he follow into the room. one glance tell the stoker what the kind gentleman have overlook. pambe be desperately poor. nurkeed drive his hand deep into his pocket then advance with clench fist on the sick shout hya pambe. hya. hee ah. hulla. heh. takilo. takilo. make fast aft pambe. you know pambe. you know me. dekho jee. look. dam big fat lazy lascar. 
pambe beckon with his leave hand. his right be under his pillow. nurkeed remove his gorgeous hat and stoop over pambe till he could catch a faint whisper. how beautiful. say the kind gentleman. how these oriental love like child. 
spit him out say nurkeed lean over pambe yet more closely. 
touch the matter of that fish and onion say pambe and send the knife home under the edge of the rib bone upwards and forward. 
there be a thick sick cough and the body of the african slide slowly from the bed his clutch hand let fall a shower of silver piece that run across the room. 
now i can die. say pambe. 
but he do not die. he be nurse back to life with all the skill that money could buy for the law want him. and in the end he grow sufficiently healthy to be hang in due and proper form. 
pambe do not care particularly. but it be a sad blow to the kind gentleman. 
little tobrah [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
prisoner s head do not reach to the top of the dock a the english newspaper say. this case however be not report because nobody care by so much a a hempen rope for the life or death of little tobrah. the assessor in the red court house sit upon him all through the long hot afternoon and whenever they ask him a question he salaam and whine. their verdict be that the evidence be inconclusive and the judge concur. it be true that the dead body of little tobrah s sister have be find at the bottom of the well and little tobrah be the only human be within a half mile radius at the time. but the child might have fall in by accident. therefore little tobrah be acquit and tell to go where he please. this permission be not so generous a it sound for he have nowhere to go to nothing in particular to eat and nothing whatever to wear. 
he trot into the court compound and sit upon the well kerb wonder whether an unsuccessful dive into the black water below would end in a force voyage across the other black water. a groom put down an empty nose bag on the brick and little tobrah be hungry set himself to scrape out what wet grain the horse have overlook. 
o thief and but newly set free from the terror of the law. come along. say the groom and little tobrah be lead by the ear to a large and fat englishman who hear the tale of the theft. 
hah. say the englishman three time. only he say a strong word. put him into the net and take him home. so little tobrah be throw into the net of the cart and nothing doubt that he should be stick like a pig be drive to the englishman s house. hah. say the englishman a before. wet grain by jove. fee the little beggar some of you and we ll make a rid boy of him. see. wet grain good lord. 
give an account of yourself say the head of the groom to little tobrah after the meal have be eat and the servant lay at ease in their quarter behind the house. you be not of the groom caste unless it be for the stomach s sake. how come you into the court and why. answer little devil s spawn. 
there be not enough to eat say little tobrah calmly. this be a good place. 
talk straight talk say the head groom or i will make you clean out the stable of that large red stallion who bite like a camel. 
we be telis oil pressers say little tobrah scratch his toe in the dust. we be telis my father my mother my brother the elder by four year myself and the sister. 
she who be find dead in the well. say one who have hear something of the trial. 
even so say little tobrah gravely. she who be find dead in the well. it befel upon a time which be not in my memory that the sickness come to the village where our oil press stand and first my sister be smite a to her eye and go without sight for it be mata the smallpox. thereafter my father and my mother die of that same sickness so we be alone my brother who have twelve year i who have eight and the sister who could not see. yet be there the bullock and the oil press remain and we make shift to press the oil a before. but surjun das the grain seller cheat u in his dealing. and it be always a stubborn bullock to drive. we put marigold flower for the god upon the neck of the bullock and upon the great grind beam that rise through the roof. but we gain nothing thereby and surjun das be a hard man. 
bapri bap mutter the groom wife to cheat a child so. but we know what the bunnia folk be sister. 
the press be an old press and we be not strong men my brother and i. nor could we fix the neck of the beam firmly in the shackle. 
nay indeed say the gorgeously clothe wife of the head groom join the circle. that be a strong man s work. when i be a maid in my father s house. 
peace woman say the head groom. go on boy. 
it be nothing say little tobrah. the big beam tear down the roof upon a day which be not in my memory and with the roof fell much of the hind wall and both together upon our bullock whose back be break. thus we have neither home nor press nor bullock my brother myself and the sister who be blind. we go cry away from that place hand in hand across the field. and our money be seven anna and six pie. there be a famine in the land. i do not know the name of the land. so on a night when we be sleep my brother take the five anna that remain to u and run away. i do not know whither he go. the curse of my father be upon him. but i and the sister beg food in the village and there be none to give. only all men say go to the englishman and they will give. i do not know what the englishman be. but they say that they be white live in tent. i go forward. but i cannot say whither i go and there be no more food for myself or the sister. and upon a hot night she weep and call for food we come to a well and i bid her sit upon the kerb and thrust her in for in truth she could not see. and it be good to die than to starve. 
ai. ahi. wail the groom wife in chorus. he thrust her in for it be good to die than to starve. 
i would have throw myself in also but that she be not dead and call to me from the bottom of the well and i be afraid and run. and one come out of the crop say that i have kill her and defile the well and they take me before an englishman white and terrible live in a tent and me he send here. but there be no witness and it be good to die than to starve. she furthermore could not see with her eye and be but a little child. 
be but a little child echo the head groom s wife. but who art thou weak a a fowl and small a a day old colt what art thou. 
i who be empty be now full say little tobrah stretch himself upon the dust. and i would sleep. 
the groom s wife spread a cloth over him while little tobrah sleep the sleep of the just. 
bubble well road [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
look out on a large scale map the place where the chenab river fall into the indus fifteen mile or so above the hamlet of chachuran. five mile west of chachuran lie bubble well road and the house of the gosain or priest of arti goth. it be the priest who show me the road but it be no thank to him that i be able to tell this story. 
five mile west of chachuran be a patch of the plume jungle grass that turn over in silver when the wind blow from ten to twenty foot high and from three to four mile square. in the heart of the patch hide the gosain of bubble well road. the villager stone him when he peer into the daylight although he be a priest and he run back again a a stray wolf turn into tall crop. he be a one eye man and carry burn between his brow the impress of two copper coin. some say that he be torture by a native prince in the old day. for he be so old that he must have be capable of mischief in the day of runjit singh. his most press need at present be a halter and the care of the british government. 
these thing happen when the jungle grass be tall. and the villager of chachuran tell me that a sound of pig have go into the arti goth patch. to enter jungle grass be always an unwise proceed but i go partly because i know nothing of pig hunt and partly because the villager say that the big boar of the sound own foot long tush. therefore i wish to shoot him in order to produce the tush in after year and say that i have ride him down in fair chase. i take a gun and go into the hot close patch believe that it would be an easy thing to unearth one pig in ten square mile of jungle. mr. wardle the terrier go with me because he believe that i be incapable of exist for an hour without his advice and countenance. he manage to slip in and out between the grass clump but i have to force my way and in twenty minute be a completely lose a though i have be in the heart of central africa. i do not notice this at first till i have grow weary of stumble and push through the grass and mr. wardle be begin to sit down very often and hang out his tongue very far. there be nothing but grass everywhere and it be impossible to see two yard in any direction. the grass stem hold the heat exactly a boiler tube do. 
in half an hour when i be devoutly wish that i have leave the big boar alone i come to a narrow path which seem to be a compromise between a native foot path and a pig run. it be barely six inch wide but i could sidle along it in comfort. the grass be extremely thick here and where the path be ill define it be necessary to crush into the tussock either with both hand before the face or to back into it leave both hand free to manage the rifle. none the le it be a path and valuable because it might lead to a place. 
at the end of nearly fifty yard of fair way just when i be prepare to back into an unusually stiff tussock i miss mr. wardle who for his girth be an unusually frivolous dog and never keep to heel. i call him three time and say aloud where ha the little beast go to. then i step backwards several pace for almost under my foot a deep voice repeat where ha the little beast go. to appreciate an unseen voice thoroughly you should hear it when you be lose in stifle jungle grass. i call mr. wardle again and the underground echo assist me. at that i cease call and listen very attentively because i think i hear a man laugh in a peculiarly offensive manner. the heat make me sweat but the laughter make me shake. there be no earthly need for laughter in high grass. it be indecent a well a impolite. the chuckle stop and i take courage and continue to call till i think that i have locate the echo somewhere behind and below the tussock into which i be prepare to back just before i lose mr. wardle. i drive my rifle up to the trigger between the grass stem in a downward and forward direction. then i waggle it to and fro but it do not seem to touch grind on the far side of the tussock a it should have do. every time that i grunt with the exertion of drive a heavy rifle through thick grass the grunt be faithfully repeat from below and when i stop to wipe my face the sound of low laughter be distinct beyond doubt. 
i go into the tussock face first an inch at a time my mouth open and my eye fine full and prominent. when i have overcome the resistance of the grass i find that i be look straight across a black gap in the grind that i be actually lie on my chest lean over the mouth of a well so deep i could scarcely see the water in it. 
there be thing in the water black thing and the water be a black a pitch with blue scum atop. the laugh sound come from the noise of a little spring spout half way down one side of the well. sometimes a the black thing circle round the trickle from the spring fell upon their tightly stretch skin and then the laughter change into a sputter of mirth. one thing turn over on it back a i watch and drift round and round the circle of the mossy brickwork with a hand and half an arm hold clear of the water in a stiff and horrible flourish a though it be a very weary guide pay to exhibit the beauty of the place. 
i do not spend more than half an hour in creep round that well and find the path on the other side. the remainder of the journey i accomplish by feel every foot of grind in front of me and crawl like a snail through every tussock. i carry mr. wardle in my arm and he lick my nose. he be not frighten in the least nor be i but we wish to reach open grind in order to enjoy the view. my knee be loose and the apple in my throat refuse to slide up and down. the path on the far side of the well be a very good one though box in on all side by grass and it lead me in time to a priest s hut in the centre of a little clear. when that priest saw my very white face come through the grass he howl with terror and embrace my boot. but when i reach the bedstead set outside his door i sit down quickly and mr. wardle mount guard over me. i be not in a condition to take care of myself. 
when i awake i tell the priest to lead me into the open out of the arti goth patch and to walk slowly in front of me. mr. wardle hate native and the priest be more afraid of mr. wardle than of me though we be both angry. he walk very slowly down a narrow little path from his hut. that path cross three path such a the one i have come by in the first instance and every one of the three head towards the bubble well. once when we stop to draw breath i hear the well laugh to itself alone in the thick grass and only my need for his service prevent my fire both barrel into the priest s back. 
when we come to the open the priest crash back into cover and i go to the village of arti goth for a drink. it be pleasant to be able to see the horizon all round a well a the grind underfoot. 
the villager tell me that the patch of grass be full of devil and ghost all in the service of the priest and that men and woman and child have enter it and have never return. they say the priest use their liver for purpose of witchcraft. when i ask why they have not tell me of this at the outset they say that they be afraid they would lose their reward for bring news of the pig. 
before i leave i do my best to set the patch alight but the grass be too green. some fine summer day however if the wind be favourable a file of old newspaper and a box of match will make clear the mystery of bubble well road. 
the city of dreadful night [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ].
