the dense wet heat that hang over the face of land like a blanket prevent all hope of sleep in the first instance. the cicala help the heat. and the yell jackal the cicala. it be impossible to sit still in the dark empty echo house and watch the punkah beat the dead air. so at ten o clock of the night i set my walk stick on end in the middle of the garden and wait to see how it would fall. it point directly down the moonlit road that lead to the city of dreadful night. the sound of it fall disturb a hare. she limp from her form and run across to a disused mahomedan burial grind where the jawless skull and rough butt shank bone heartlessly expose by the july rain glimmer like mother o pearl on the rain channel soil. the heat air and the heavy earth have drive the very dead upward for coolness sake. the hare limp on. snuff curiously at a fragment of a smoke stain lamp shard and die out in the shadow of a clump of tamarisk tree. 
the mat weaver s hut under the lee of the hindu temple be full of sleep men who lay like sheet corps. overhead blaze the unwinking eye of the moon. darkness give at least a false impression of coolness. it be hard not to believe that the flood of light from above be warm. not so hot a the sun but still sickly warm and heat the heavy air beyond what be our due. straight a a bar of polish steel run the road to the city of dreadful night. and on either side of the road lay corps dispose on bed in fantastic attitude one hundred and seventy body of men. some shroud all in white with bind up mouth. some naked and black a ebony in the strong light. and one that lay face upwards with drop jaw far away from the others silvery white and ashen gray. 
a leper asleep. and the remainder weary cooly servant small shopkeeper and driver from the hackstand hard by. the scene a main approach to lahore city and the night a warm one in august. this be all that there be to be see. but by no mean all that one could see. the witchery of the moonlight be everywhere. and the world be horribly change. the long line of the naked dead flank by the rigid silver statue be not pleasant to look upon. it be make up of men alone. be the womenkind then force to sleep in the shelter of the stifle mud hut a best they might. the fretful wail of a child from a low mud roof answer the question. where the child be the mother must be also to look after them. they need care on these swelter night. a black little bullet head peep over the cop and a thin a painfully thin brown leg be slide over on to the gutter pipe. there be a sharp clink of glass bracelet. a woman s arm show for an instant above the parapet twin itself round the lean little neck and the child be drag back protest to the shelter of the bedstead. his thin high pitch shriek die out in the thick air almost a soon a it be raise. for even the child of the soil find it too hot to weep. 
more corps. more stretch of moonlit white road a string of sleep camel at rest by the wayside. a vision of scud jackal. ekka pony asleep the harness still on their back and the brass stud country cart wink in the moonlight and again more corps. wherever a grain cart atilt a tree trunk a saw log a couple of bamboo and a few handful of thatch cast a shadow the grind be cover with them. they lie some face downwards arm fold in the dust. some with clasp hand fling up above their head. some curl up dog wise. some throw like limp gunny bag over the side of the grain cart. and some bow with their brow on their knee in the full glare of the moon. it would be a comfort if they be only give to snore. but they be not and the liken to corps be unbroken in all respect save one. the lean dog snuff at them and turn away. here and there a tiny child lie on his father s bedstead and a protect arm be throw round it in every instance. but for the most part the child sleep with their mother on the house top. yellow skin white toothed pariah be not to be trust within reach of brown body. 
a stifle hot blast from the mouth of the delhi gate nearly end my resolution of enter the city of dreadful night at this hour. it be a compound of all evil savour animal and vegetable that a wall city can brew in a day and a night. the temperature within the motionless grove of plantain and orange tree outside the city wall seem chilly by comparison. heaven help all sick person and young child within the city to night. the high house wall be still radiate heat savagely and from obscure side gully fetid breeze eddy that ought to poison a buffalo. but the buffalo do not heed. a drive of them be parade the vacant main street. stop now and then to lay their ponderous muzzle against the close shutter of a grain dealer s shop and to blow thereon like grampus. 
then silence follow the silence that be full of the night noise of a great city. a string instrument of some kind be just and only just audible. high overhead some one throw open a window and the rattle of the wood work echo down the empty street. on one of the roof a hookah be in full blast. and the men be talk softly a the pipe gutter. a little farther on the noise of conversation be more distinct. a slit of light show itself between the slide shutter of a shop. inside a stubble beard weary eye trader be balance his account book among the bale of cotton print that surround him. three sheet figure bear him company and throw in a remark from time to time. first he make an entry then a remark. then pass the back of his hand across his stream forehead. the heat in the build in street be fearful. inside the shop it must be almost unendurable. but the work go on steadily. entry guttural growl and uplift hand stroke succeed each other with the precision of clock work. 
a policeman turbanless and fast asleep lie across the road on the way to the mosque of wazir khan. a bar of moonlight fall across the forehead and eye of the sleeper but he never stir. it be close upon midnight and the heat seem to be increase. the open square in front of the mosque be crowd with corps. and a man must pick his way carefully for fear of tread on them. the moonlight stripe the mosque s high front of colour enamel work in broad diagonal band. and each separate dream pigeon in the niche and corner of the masonry throw a squab little shadow. sheet ghost rise up wearily from their pallet and flit into the dark depth of the build. be it possible to climb to the top of the great minars and thence to look down on the city. at all event the attempt be worth make and the chance be that the door of the staircase will be unlock. unlock it be. but a deeply sleep janitor lie across the threshold face turn to the moon. a rat dash out of his turban at the sound of approach footstep. the man grunt open his eye for a minute turn round and go to sleep again. all the heat of a decade of fierce indian summer be store in the pitch black polish wall of the corkscrew staircase. half way up there be something alive warm and feathery. and it snore. drive from step to step a it catch the sound of my advance it flutter to the top and reveal itself a a yellow eye angry kite. dozen of kite be asleep on this and the other minars and on the dome below. there be the shadow of a cool or at least a le sultry breeze at this height. and refresh thereby turn to look on the city of dreadful night. 
dore might have draw it. zola could describe it this spectacle of sleep thousand in the moonlight and in the shadow of the moon. the roof top be cram with men woman and child. and the air be full of undistinguishable noise. they be restless in the city of dreadful night. and small wonder. the marvel be that they can even breathe. if you gaze intently at the multitude you can see that they be almost a uneasy a a daylight crowd. but the tumult be subdue. everywhere in the strong light you can watch the sleeper turn to and fro. shift their bed and again resettle them. in the pit like court yard of the house there be the same movement. 
the pitiless moon show it all. show too the plain outside the city and here and there a hand s breadth of the ravee without the wall. show lastly a splash of glitter silver on a house top almost directly below the mosque minar. some poor soul ha rise to throw a jar of water over his fevered body. the tinkle of the fall water strike faintly on the ear. two or three other men in far off corner of the city of dreadful night follow his example and the water flash like heliographic signal. a small cloud pass over the face of the moon and the city and it inhabitant clear draw in black and white before fade into mass of black and deep black. still the unrestful noise continue the sigh of a great city overwhelm with the heat and of a people seek in vain for rest. it be only the low class woman who sleep on the house top. what must the torment be in the latticed zenanas where a few lamp be still twinkle. there be footfall in the court below. it be the muezzin faithful minister. but he ought to have be here an hour ago to tell the faithful that prayer be good than sleep the sleep that will not come to the city. 
the muezzin fumble for a moment with the door of one of the minars disappear awhile and a bull like roar a magnificent bass thunder tell that he ha reach the top of the minar. they must hear the cry to the bank of the shrink ravee itself. even across the courtyard it be almost overpower. the cloud drift by and show him outline in black against the sky hand lay upon his ear and broad chest heave with the play of his lung allah ho akbar. then a pause while another muezzin somewhere in the direction of the golden temple take up the call allah ho akbar. again and again. four time in all. and from the bedstead a dozen men have rise up already. i bear witness that there be no god but god. what a splendid cry it be the proclamation of the creed that bring men out of their bed by score at midnight. once again he thunder through the same phrase shake with the vehemence of his own voice. and then far and near the night air ring with mahomed be the prophet of god. it be a though he be fling his defiance to the far off horizon where the summer lightning play and leap like a bar sword. every muezzin in the city be in full cry and some men on the roof top be begin to kneel. a long pause precede the last cry la ilaha illallah and the silence close up on it a the ram on the head of a cotton bale. 
the muezzin stumble down the dark stairway grumble in his beard. he pass the arch of the entrance and disappear. then the stifle silence settle down over the city of dreadful night. the kite on the minar sleep again snore more loudly the hot breeze come up in puff and lazy eddy and the moon slide down towards the horizon. seat with both elbow on the parapet of the tower one can watch and wonder over that heat torture hive till the dawn. how do they live down there. what do they think of. when will they awake. more tinkle of sluice water pot. faint jar of wooden bedstead move into or out of the shadow. uncouth music of string instrument soften by distance into a plaintive wail and one low grumble of far off thunder. in the courtyard of the mosque the janitor who lay across the threshold of the minar when i come up start wildly in his sleep throw his hand above his head mutter something and fall back again. lull by the snore of the kite they snore like over gorge human i drop off into an uneasy doze conscious that three o clock ha strike and that there be a slight a very slight coolness in the atmosphere. the city be absolutely quiet now but for some vagrant dog s love song. nothing save dead heavy sleep. 
several week of darkness pas after this. for the moon ha go out. the very dog be still and i watch for the first light of the dawn before make my way homeward. again the noise of shuffle foot. the morning call be about to begin and my night watch be over. allah ho akbar. allah ho akbar. the east grow gray and presently saffron. the dawn wind come up a though the muezzin have summon it. and a one man the city of dreadful night rise from it bed and turn it face towards the dawn day. with return of life come return of sound. first a low whisper then a deep bass hum. for it must be remember that the entire city be on the house top. my eyelid weigh down with the arrears of long defer sleep i escape from the minar through the courtyard and out into the square beyond where the sleeper have rise stow away the bedstead and be discuss the morning hookah. the minute s freshness of the air ha go and it be a hot a at first. 
will the sahib out of his kindness make room. what be it. something bear on men s shoulder come by in the half light and i stand back. a woman s corpse go down to the burn ghat and a bystander say she die at midnight from the heat. so the city be of death a well a night after all. 
georgie porgie [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
georgie porgie pudding and pie kiss the girl and make them cry. when the girl come out to play georgie porgie run away. 
if you will admit that a man ha no right to enter his draw room early in the morning when the housemaid be set thing right and clear away the dust you will concede that civilise people who eat out of china and own card case have no right to apply their standard of right and wrong to an unsettle land. when the place be make fit for their reception by those men who be tell off to the work they can come up bring in their trunk their own society and the decalogue and all the other apparatus. where the queen s law doe not carry it be irrational to expect an observance of other and weak rule. the men who run ahead of the car of decency and propriety and make the jungle way straight cannot be judge in the same manner a the stay at home folk of the rank of the regular tchin. 
not many month ago the queen s law stop a few mile north of thayetmyo on the irrawaddy. there be no very strong public opinion up to that limit but it exist to keep men in order. when the government say that the queen s law must carry up to bhamo and the chinese border the order be give and some men whose desire be to be ever a little in advance of the rush of respectability flock forward with the troop. these be the men who could never pas examination and would have be too pronounce in their idea for the administration of bureau work province. the supreme government step in a soon a might be with code and regulation and all but reduce new burma to the dead indian level. but there be a short time during which strong men be necessary and plough a field for themselves. 
among the fore runner of civilisation be georgie porgie reckon by all who know him a strong man. he hold an appointment in low burma when the order come to break the frontier and his friend call him georgie porgie because of the singularly burmese like manner in which he sing a song whose first line be something like the word georgie porgie. most men who have be in burma will know the song. it mean. puff puff puff puff great steamboat. georgie sing it to his banjo and his friend shout with delight so that you could hear them far away in the teak forest. 
when he go to upper burma he have no special regard for god or man but he know how to make himself respect and to carry out the mix military civil duty that fell to most men s share in those month. he do his office work and entertain now and again the detachment of fever shake soldier who blunder through his part of the world in search of a fly party of dacoit. sometimes he turn out and dress down dacoit on his own account. for the country be still smoulder and would blaze when least expect. he enjoy these charivari but the dacoit be not so amuse. all the official who come in contact with him depart with the idea that georgie porgie be a valuable person well able to take care of himself and on that belief he be leave to his own device. 
at the end of a few month he weary of his solitude and cast about for company and refinement. the queen s law have hardly begin to be felt in the country and public opinion which be more powerful than the queen s law have yet to come. also there be a custom in the country which allow a white man to take to himself a wife of the daughter of heth upon due payment. the marriage be not quite so bind a be the nikkah ceremony among mahomedans but the wife be very pleasant. 
when all our troop be back from burma there will be a proverb in their mouth a thrifty a a burmese wife and pretty english lady will wonder what in the world it mean. 
the headman of the village next to georgie porgie s post have a fair daughter who have see georgie porgie and love him from afar. when news go abroad that the englishman with the heavy hand who live in the stockade be look for a housekeeper the headman come in and explain that for five hundred rupee down he would entrust his daughter to georgie porgie s keep to be maintain in all honour respect and comfort with pretty dress accord to the custom of the country. this thing be do and georgie porgie never repent it. 
he find his rough and tumble house put straight and make comfortable his hitherto unchecked expense cut down by one half and himself pet and make much of by his new acquisition who sit at the head of his table and sing song to him and order his madrassee servant about and be in every way a sweet and merry and honest and win a little woman a the most exact of bachelor could have desire. no race men say who know produce such good wife and head of household a the burmese. when the next detachment tramp by on the war path the subaltern in command find at georgie porgie s table a host to be deferential to a woman to be treat in every way a one occupy an assure position. when he gather his men together next dawn and replunged into the jungle he think regretfully of the nice little dinner and the pretty face and envy georgie porgie from the bottom of his heart. yet he be engage to a girl at home and that be how some men be construct. 
the burmese girl s name be not a pretty one. but a she be promptly christen georgina by georgie porgie the blemish do not matter. georgie porgie think well of the pet and the general comfort and vow that he have never spend five hundred rupee to a good end. 
after three month of domestic life a great idea strike him. matrimony english matrimony could not be such a bad thing after all. if he be so thoroughly comfortable at the back of beyond with this burmese girl who smoke cheroot how much more comfortable would he be with a sweet english maiden who would not smoke cheroot and would play upon a piano instead of a banjo. also he have a desire to return to his kind to hear a band once more and to feel how it felt to wear a dress suit again. decidedly matrimony would be a very good thing. he think the matter out at length of evening while georgina sing to him or ask him why he be so silent and whether she have do anything to offend him. a he think he smoke and a he smoke he look at georgina and in his fancy turn her into a fair thrifty amuse merry little english girl with hair come low down on her forehead and perhaps a cigarette between her lip. certainly not a big thick burma cheroot of the brand that georgina smoke. he would wed a girl with georgina s eye and most of her way. but not all. she could be improve upon. then he blow thick smoke wreath through his nostril and stretch himself. he would taste marriage. georgina have help him to save money and there be six month leave due to him. 
see here little woman he say we must put by more money for these next three month. i want it. that be a direct slur on georgina s housekeep. for she pride herself on her thrift. but since her god want money she would do her best. 
you want money. she say with a little laugh. i have money. look. she run to her own room and fetch out a small bag of rupee. of all that you give me i keep back some. see. one hundred and seven rupee. can you want more money than that. take it. it be my pleasure if you use it. she spread out the money on the table and push it towards him with her quick little pale yellow finger. 
georgie porgie never refer to economy in the household again. 
three month late after the dispatch and receipt of several mysterious letter which georgina could not understand and hat for that reason georgie porgie say that he be go away and she must return to her father s house and stay there. 
georgina weep. she would go with her god from the world s end to the world s end. why should she leave him. she love him. 
i be only go to rangoon say georgie porgie. i shall be back in a month but it be safe to stay with your father. i will leave you two hundred rupee. 
if you go for a month what need of two hundred. fifty be more than enough. there be some evil here. do not go or at least let me go with you. 
georgie porgie doe not like to remember that scene even at this date. in the end he get rid of georgina by a compromise of seventy five rupee. she would not take more. then he go by steamer and rail to rangoon. 
the mysterious letter have grant him six month leave. the actual flight and an idea that he might have be treacherous hurt severely at the time but a soon a the big steamer be well out into the blue thing be easy and georgina s face and the queer little stockade house and the memory of the rush of shout dacoit by night the cry and struggle of the first man that he have ever kill with his own hand and a hundred other more intimate thing fade and fade out of georgie porgie s heart and the vision of approach england take it place. the steamer be full of men on leave all rampantly jovial soul who have shake off the dust and sweat of upper burma and be a merry a schoolboy. they help georgie porgie to forget. 
then come england with it luxury and decency and comfort and georgie porgie walk in a pleasant dream upon pavement of which he have nearly forget the ring wonder why men in their sens ever leave town. he accept his keen delight in his furlough a the reward of his service. providence further arrange for him another and great delight all the pleasure of a quiet english woo quite different from the brazen business of the east when half the community stand back and bet on the result and the other half wonder what mr. so and so will say to it. 
it be a pleasant girl and a perfect summer and a big country house near petworth where there be acre and acre of purple heather and high grass water meadow to wander through. georgie porgie felt that he have at last find something worth the live for and naturally assume that the next thing to do be to ask the girl to share his life in india. she in her ignorance be will to go. on this occasion there be no barter with a village headman. there be a fine middle class wed in the country with a stout papa and a weep mamma and a best man in purple and fine linen and six snub nose girl from the sunday school to throw rose on the path between the tombstone up to the church door. the local paper describe the affair at great length even down to give the hymn in full. but that be because the direction be starve for want of material. 
then come a honeymoon at arundel and the mamma weep copiously before she allow her one daughter to sail away to india under the care of georgie porgie the bridegroom. beyond any question georgie porgie be immensely fond of his wife and she be devote to him a the best and great man in the world. when he report himself at bombay he felt justify in demand a good station for his wife s sake. and because he have make a little mark in burma and be begin to be appreciate they allow him nearly all that he ask for and post him to a station which we will call sutrain. it stand upon several hill and be style officially a sanitarium for the good reason that the drainage be utterly neglect. here georgie porgie settle down and find marry life come very naturally to him. he do not rave a do many bridegroom over the strangeness and delight of see his own true love sit down to breakfast with him every morning a though it be the most natural thing in the world. 
he have be there before a the american say and check the merit of his own present grace by those of georgina he be more and more incline to think that he have do well. 
but there be no peace or comfort across the bay of bengal under the teak tree where georgina live with her father wait for georgie porgie to return. the headman be old and remember the war of. he have be to rangoon and know something of the way of the kullahs. sit in front of his door in the evening he teach georgina a dry philosophy which do not console her in the least. 
the trouble be that she love georgie porgie just a much a the french girl in the english history book love the priest whose head be break by the king s bully. one day she disappear from the village with all the rupee that georgie porgie have give her and a very small smatter of english also gain from georgie porgie. 
the headman be angry at first but light a fresh cheroot and say something uncomplimentary about the sex in general. georgina have start on a search for georgie porgie who might be in rangoon or across the black water or dead for aught that she know. chance favour her. an old sikh policeman tell her that georgie porgie have cross the black water. she take a steerage passage from rangoon and go to calcutta. keep the secret of her search to herself. 
in india every trace of her be lose for six week and no one know what trouble of heart she must have undergo. 
she reappear four hundred mile north of calcutta steadily head northward very wear and haggard but very fix in her determination to find georgie porgie. she could not understand the language of the people. but india be infinitely charitable and the woman folk along the grand trunk give her food. something make her believe that georgie porgie be to be find at the end of that pitiless road. she may have see a sepoy who know him in burma but of this no one can be certain. at last she find a regiment on the line of march and meet there one of the many subaltern whom georgie porgie have invite to dinner in the far off old day of the dacoit hunt. there be a certain amount of amusement among the tent when georgina throw herself at the man s foot and begin to cry. there be no amusement when her story be tell. but a collection be make and that be more to the point. one of the subaltern know of georgie porgie s whereabouts but not of his marriage. so he tell georgina and she go her way joyfully to the north in a railway carriage where there be rest for tire foot and shade for a dusty little head. the march from the train through the hill into sutrain be try but georgina have money and family journey in bullock cart give her help. it be an almost miraculous journey and georgina felt sure that the good spirit of burma be look after her. the hill road to sutrain be a chilly stretch and georgina catch a bad cold. still there be georgie porgie at the end of all the trouble to take her up in his arm and pet her a he use to do in the old day when the stockade be shut for the night and he have approve of the even meal. georgina go forward a fast a she could. and her good spirit do her one last favour. 
an englishman stop her in the twilight just at the turn of the road into sutrain say good heaven. what be you do here. 
he be gillis the man who have be georgie porgie s assistant in upper burma and who occupy the next post to georgie porgie s in the jungle. georgie porgie have apply to have him to work with at sutrain because he like him. 
i have come say georgina simply. it be such a long way and i have be month in come. where be his house. 
gillis gasp. he have see enough of georgina in the old time to know that explanation would be useless. you cannot explain thing to the oriental. you must show. 
i ll take you there say gillis and he lead georgina off the road up the cliff by a little pathway to the back of a house set on a platform cut into the hillside. 
the lamp be just light but the curtain be not draw. now look say gillis stop in front of the draw room window. georgina look and saw georgie porgie and the bride. 
she put her hand up to her hair which have come out of it top knot and be straggle about her face. she try to set her rag dress in order but the dress be past pull straight and she cough a queer little cough for she really have take a very bad cold. gillis look too but while georgina only look at the bride once turn her eye always on georgie porgie gillis look at the bride all the time. 
what be you go to do. say gillis who hold georgina by the wrist in case of any unexpected rush into the lamplight. will you go in and tell that english woman that you live with her husband. 
no say georgina faintly. let me go. i be go away. i swear that i be go away. she twist herself free and run off into the dark. 
poor little beast. say gillis drop on to the main road. i d ha give her something to get back to burma with. what a narrow shave though. and that angel would never have forgive it. 
this seem to prove that the devotion of gillis be not entirely due to his affection for georgie porgie. 
the bride and the bridegroom come out into the verandah after dinner in order that the smoke of georgie porgie s cheroot might not hang in the new draw room curtain. 
what be that noise down there. say the bride. both listen. 
oh say georgie porgie i suppose some brute of a hillman ha be beat his wife. 
beat his wife. how ghastly. say the bride. fancy your beat me. she slip an arm round her husband s waist and lean her head against his shoulder look out across the cloud fill valley in deep content and security. 
but it be georgina cry all by herself down the hillside among the stone of the water course where the washerman wash the clothe. 
naboth [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
this be how it happen. and the truth be also an allegory of empire. 
i meet him at the corner of my garden an empty basket on his head and an unclean cloth round his loin. that be all the property to which naboth have the shadow of a claim when i first saw him. he open our acquaintance by beg. he be very thin and show nearly a many rib a his basket. and he tell me a long story about fever and a lawsuit and an iron cauldron that have be seize by the court in execution of a decree. i put my hand into my pocket to help naboth a king of the east have help alien adventurer to the loss of their kingdom. a rupee have hide in my waistcoat line. i never know it be there and give the trove to naboth a a direct gift from heaven. he reply that i be the only legitimate protector of the poor he have ever know. 
next morning he reappear a little fat in the round and curl himself into knot in the front verandah. he say i be his father and his mother and the direct descendant of all the god in his pantheon besides control the destiny of the universe. he himself be but a sweetmeat seller and much le important than the dirt under my foot. i have hear this sort of thing before so i ask him what he want. my rupee quoth naboth have raise him to the ever last heaven and he wish to prefer a request. he wish to establish a sweetmeat pitch near the house of his benefactor to gaze on my revere countenance a i go to and fro illumine the world. i be graciously please to give permission and he go away with his head between his knee. 
now at the far end of my garden the grind slope toward the public road and the slope be crown with a thick shrubbery. there be a short carriage road from the house to the mall which pass close to the shrubbery. next afternoon i saw that naboth have seat himself at the bottom of the slope down in the dust of the public road and in the full glare of the sun with a starve basket of greasy sweet in front of him. he have go into trade once more on the strength of my munificent donation and the grind be a paradise by my honour favour. remember there be only naboth his basket the sunshine and the gray dust when the sap of my empire first begin. 
next day he have move himself up the slope near to my shrubbery and wave a palm leaf fan to keep the fly off the sweet. so i judge that he must have do a fair trade. 
four day late i notice that he have back himself and his basket under the shadow of the shrubbery and have tie an isabella colour rag between two branch in order to make more shade. there be plenty of sweet in his basket. i think that trade must certainly be look up. 
seven week late the government take up a plot of grind for a chief court close to the end of my compound and employ nearly four hundred cooly on the foundation. naboth buy a blue and white strip blanket a brass lamp stand and a small boy to cope with the rush of trade which be tremendous. 
five day late he buy a huge fat red back account book and a glass inkstand. thus i saw that the cooly have be get into his debt and that commerce be increase on legitimate line of credit. also i saw that the one basket have grow into three and that naboth have back and hack into the shrubbery and make himself a nice little clear for the proper display of the basket the blanket the book and the boy. 
one week and five day late he have build a mud fire place in the clear and the fat account book be overflow. he say that god create few englishman of my kind and that i be the incarnation of all human virtue. he offer me some of his sweet a tribute and by accept these i acknowledge him a my feudatory under the skirt of my protection. 
three week late i notice that the boy be in the habit of cook naboth s mid day meal for him and naboth be begin to grow a stomach. he have hack away more of my shrubbery and own another and a fat account book. 
eleven week late naboth have eat his way nearly through that shrubbery and there be a reed hut with a bedstead outside it stand in the little glade that he have erode. two dog and a baby sleep on the bedstead. so i fancy naboth have take a wife. he say that he have by my favour do this thing and that i be several time fine than krishna. six week and two day late a mud wall have grow up at the back of the hut. there be fowl in front and it smelt a little. the municipal secretary say that a ce pool be form in the public road from the drainage of my compound and that i must take step to clear it away. i speak to naboth. he say i be lord paramount of his earthly concern and the garden be all my own property and send me some more sweet in a second hand duster. 
two month late a coolie bricklayer be kill in a scuffle that take place opposite naboth s vineyard. the inspector of police say it be a serious case. go into my servant quarter. insult my butler s wife and want to arrest my butler. the curious thing about the murder be that most of the cooly be drink at the time. naboth point out that my name be a strong shield between him and his enemy and he expect that another baby would be bear to him shortly. 
four month late the hut be all mud wall very solidly build and naboth have use most of my shrubbery for his five goat. a silver watch and an aluminium chain shine upon his very round stomach. my servant be alarmingly drink several time and use to waste the day with naboth when they get the chance. i speak to naboth. he say by my favour and the glory of my countenance he would make all his woman folk lady and that if any one hint that he be run an illicit still under the shadow of the tamarisk why i his suzerain be to prosecute. 
a week late he hire a man to make several dozen square yard of trellis work to put around the back of his hut that his woman folk might be screen from the public gaze. the man go away in the even and leave his day s work to pave the short cut from the public road to my house. i be drive home in the dusk and turn the corner by naboth s vineyard quickly. the next thing i know be that the horse of the phaeton be stamp and plunge in the strong sort of bamboo net work. both beast come down. one rise with nothing more than chip knee. the other be so badly kick that i be force to shoot him. 
naboth be go now and his hut be plough into it native mud with sweetmeat instead of salt for a sign that the place be accurse. i have build a summer house to overlook the end of the garden and it be a a fort on my frontier whence i guard my empire. 
i know exactly how ahab felt. he ha be shamefully misrepresent in the scripture. 
the dream of duncan parrenness [footnote. copyright by macmillan & co. ]. 
like mr. bunyan of old i duncan parrenness writer to the most honourable the east india company in this god forget city of calcutta have dream a dream and never since that kitty my mare fell lame have i be so trouble. therefore l i should forget my dream i have make shift to set it down here. though heaven know how unhandy the pen be to me who be always ready with sword than ink horn when i leave london two long year since. 
when the governor general s great dance. that he give yearly at the latter end of november. be finisht i have go to mine own room which look over that sullen un english stream the hoogly scarce so sober a i might have be. now roar drink in the west be but fuddle in the east and i be drink nor nor easterly a mr. shakespeare might have say. yet in spite of my liquor the cool night wind. though i have hear that they breed chill and flux innumerable. sober me somewhat. and i remember that i have be but a little wring and waste by all the sickness of the past four month whereas those young blood that come eastward with me in the same ship have be all a month back plant to eternity in the foul soil north of writer building. so then i thank god mistily. though to my shame i never kneel down to do so. for license to live at least till march should be upon u again. 
indeed we that be alive. and our number be le by far than those who have go to their last account in the hot weather late past. have make very merry that even by the rampart of the fort over this kindness of providence. though our jest be neither witty nor such a i should have like my mother to hear. 
when i have lie down. or rather throw me on my bed. and the fume of my drink have a little clear away i find that i could get no sleep for think of a thousand thing that be good leave alone. first and it be a long time since i have think of her the sweet face of kitty somerset drift a it might have be draw in a picture across the foot of my bed so plainly that i almost think she have be present in the body. then i remember how she drive me to this accurse country to get rich that i might the more quickly marry her our parent on both side give their consent. and then how she think good. or bad may be. of her troth and wed tom sanderson but a short three month after i have sail. from kitty i fell a muse on mr. vansuythen a tall pale woman with violet eye that have come to calcutta from the dutch factory at chinsura and have set all our young men and not a few of the factor by the ear. some of our lady it be true say that she have never a husband or marriage line at all. but woman and specially those who have lead only indifferent good life themselves be cruel hard one on another. besides mr. vansuythen be far pretty than them all. she have be most gracious to me at the governor general s rout and indeed i be look upon by all a her preux chevalier which be french for a much bad word. now whether i care so much a the scratch of a pin for this same mr. vansuythen. albeit i have vow eternal love three day after we meet. i know not then nor do till late on. but mine own pride and a skill in the small sword that no man in calcutta could equal keep me in her affection. so that i believe i worshipt her. 
when i have dismist her violet eye from my thought my reason reproacht me for ever have follow her at all. and i saw how the one year that i have live in this land have so burn and sear my mind with the flame of a thousand bad passion and desire that i have age ten month for each one in the devil s school. whereat i think of my mother for a while and be very penitent. make in my sinful tipsy mood a thousand vow of reformation all since break i fear me again and again. to morrow say i to myself i will live cleanly for ever. and i smile dizzily. the liquor be still strong in me. to think of the danger i have escape. and build all manner of fine castle in spain whereof a shadowy kitty somerset that have the violet eye and the sweet slow speech of mr. vansuythen be always queen. 
lastly a very fine and magnificent courage. that doubtless have it birth in mr. hastings madeira. grow upon me till it seem that i could become governor general nawab prince ay even the great mogul himself by the mere wish of it. wherefore take my first step random and unstable enough towards my new kingdom i kickt my servant sleep without till they howl and run from me and call heaven and earth to witness that i duncan parrenness be a writer in the service of the company and afraid of no man. then see that neither the moon nor the great bear be mind to accept my challenge i lay down again and must have fall asleep. 
i be wake presently by my last word repeat two or three time and i saw that there have come into the room a drunken man a i think from mr. hastings rout. he sate down at the foot of my bed in all the world a it belong to him and i take note a well a i could that his face be somewhat like mine own grow old save when it change to the face of the governor general or my father dead these six month. but this seem to me only natural and the due result of too much wine. and i be so anger at his entry all unannounced that i tell him not over civilly to go. to all my word he make no answer whatever only say slowly a though it be some sweet morsel. writer in the company s service and afraid of no man. then he stop short and turn round sharp upon me say that one of my kidney need fear neither man nor devil. that i be a brave young man and like enough should i live so long to be governor general. but for all these thing. and i suppose that he mean thereby the change and chance of our shifty life in these part. i must pay my price. by this time i have sober somewhat and be well wake out of my first sleep be dispose to look upon the matter a a tipsy man s jest. so say i merrily. and what price shall i pay for this palace of mine which be but twelve foot square and my five poor pagoda a month. the devil take you and your jest. i have pay my price twice over in sickness. at that moment my man turn full towards me. so that by the moonlight i could see every line and wrinkle of his face. then my drunken mirth die out of me a i have see the water of our great river die away in one night. and i duncan parrenness who be afraid of no man be take with a more deadly terror than i hold it ha ever be the lot of mortal man to know. for i saw that his face be my very own but mark and though it be to be give in pagoda and sicca rupee. what price will you pay. say i very softly. for god s sake let me be whoever you be and i will mend my way from to night. say he laugh a little at my word but otherwise make no motion of have hear them. nay i would only rid so brave a young ruffler a yourself of much that will be a great hindrance to you on your way through life in the indie. for from me and that ere he go he would only ask me for a few other trifle such a no man or for matter of that boy either would keep about him in this country. and so it happen that he take from out of my for though lord help me i have travel far enough from all path of decent or godly live yet there be in me though i myself write it a certain goodness of heart which when i be sober. or sick. make me very sorry of all that i have do before the fit come on me. and this i lose wholly. have in place thereof another deadly coldness at the heart. i be not a i have before say ready with my pen so i fear that what i have just write may not be readily understand. yet there be certain time in a young man s life when through great sorrow or sin all the boy in him be burn and sear away so that he pass at one step to the more sorrowful state of manhood. a our star indian day change into night with never so much a the gray of twilight to temper the two extreme. this shall perhaps make my state more clear if it be remember that my torment be ten time a great a come in the natural course of nature to any man. at that time i dare not think of the change that have come over me and all in one night. though i have often think of it since. i have pay the price say i my teeth chatter for i be deadly cold and what be my return. at this time it be nearly dawn and myself have begin to grow pale and thin against the white light in the east a my mother use to tell me be the custom of ghost and devil and the like. he make a if he would go but my word stopt him and he laugh a i remember that i laugh when i run angus macalister through the sword arm last august because he say that mr. vansuythen be no good than she should be. what return. say he catch up my last word why strength to live a long a god or the devil plea and so long a you live my young master my gift. with that he put something into my hand though it be still too dark to see what it be and when next i lookt up he be go. 
when the light come i make shift to behold his gift and saw that it be a little piece of dry bread. 
the incarnation of krishna mulvaney. 
wohl auf my bully cavalier we ride to church to day the man that hasn t get a horse must steal one straight away. 
be reverent men remember this be a gottes haus. du conrad cut along d aisle and schenck d whiskey au. han breitmann s ride to church. 
once upon a time very far from england there live three men who love each other so greatly that neither man nor woman could come between them. they be in no sense refine nor to be admit to the out door mat of decent folk because they happen to be private soldier in her majesty s army. and private soldier of our service have small time for self culture. their duty be to keep themselves and their accoutrement specklessly clean to refrain from get drink more often than be necessary to obey their superior and to pray for a war. all these thing my friend accomplish. and of their own motion throw in some fight work for which the army regulation do not call. their fate send them to serve in india which be not a golden country though poet have sing otherwise. there men die with great swiftness and those who live suffer many and curious thing. i do not think that my friend concern themselves much with the social or political aspect of the east. they attend a not unimportant war on the northern frontier another one on our western boundary and a third in upper burma. then their regiment sit still to recruit and the boundless monotony of cantonment life be their portion. they be drill morning and even on the same dusty parade grind. they wander up and down the same stretch of dusty white road attend the same church and the same grog shop and sleep in the same lime wash barn of a barrack for two long year. there be mulvaney the father in the craft who have serve with various regiment from bermuda to halifax old in war scar reckless resourceful and in his pious hour an unequalled soldier. to him turn for help and comfort six and a half foot of slow move heavy foot yorkshireman bear on the wold breed in the dale and educate chiefly among the carrier cart at the back of york railway station. his name be learoyd and his chief virtue an unmitigated patience which help him to win fight. how ortheris a fox terrier of a cockney ever come to be one of the trio be a mystery which even to day i cannot explain. there be always three av u mulvaney use to say. an by the grace av god so long a our service last three av u they ll always be. ti betther so. 
they desire no companionship beyond their own and it be evil for any man of the regiment who attempt dispute with them. physical argument be out of the question a regard mulvaney and the yorkshireman. and assault on ortheris mean a combine attack from these twain a business which no five men be anxious to have on their hand. therefore they flourish share their drink their tobacco and their money. good luck and evil. battle and the chance of death. life and the chance of happiness from calicut in southern to peshawur in northern india. 
through no merit of my own it be my good fortune to be in a measure admit to their friendship frankly by mulvaney from the begin sullenly and with reluctance by learoyd and suspiciously by ortheris who hold to it that no man not in the army could fraternise with a red coat. like to like say he. i m a bloomin sodger he s a bloomin civilian. tain t natural that s all. 
but that be not all. they thaw progressively and in the thaw tell me more of their life and adventure than i be ever likely to write. 
omit all else this tale begin with the lamentable thirst that be at the begin of first cause. never be such a thirst mulvaney tell me so. they kick against their compulsory virtue but the attempt be only successful in the case of ortheris. he whose talent be many go forth into the highway and steal a dog from a civilian videlicet some one he know not who not in the army. now that civilian be but newly connect by marriage with the colonel of the regiment and outcry be make from quarter least anticipate by ortheris and in the end he be force l a bad thing should happen to dispose at ridiculously unremunerative rate of a promise a small terrier a ever grace one end of a lead string. the purchase money be barely sufficient for one small outbreak which lead him to the guard room. he escape however with nothing bad than a severe reprimand and a few hour of punishment drill. not for nothing have he acquire the reputation of be the best soldier of his inch in the regiment. mulvaney have teach personal cleanliness and efficiency a the first article of his companion creed. a dhirty man he be use to say in the speech of his kind go to clink for a weakness in the knee an be coort martialled for a pair av sock missin. but a clane man such a be an ornament to his service a man whose button be gold whose coat be wax upon him an whose coutrements be widout a speck that man may spakin in reason do fwhat he like an dhrink from day to divil. that s the pride av bein dacint. 
we sit together upon a day in the shade of a ravine far from the barrack where a watercourse use to run in rainy weather. behind u be the scrub jungle in which jackal peacock the gray wolf of the north western province and occasionally a tiger estrayed from central india be suppose to dwell. in front lay the cantonment glare white under a glare sun. and on either side run the broad road that lead to delhi. 
it be the scrub that suggest to my mind the wisdom of mulvaney take a day s leave and go upon a shoot tour. the peacock be a holy bird throughout india and he who slay one be in danger of be mob by the near villager. but on the last occasion that mulvaney have go forth he have contrive without in the least offend local religious susceptibility to return with six beautiful peacock skin which he sell to profit. it seem just possible then. 
but fwhat manner av use be ut to me goin out widout a dhrink. the grind s powdher dhry underfoot an ut get unto the throat fit to kill wail mulvaney look at me reproachfully. an a peacock be not a bird you can catch the tail av onless ye run. can a man run on wather an jungle wather too. 
ortheris have consider the question in all it bearing. he speak chew his pipe stem meditatively the while. 
go forth return in glory to clusium s royal ome. an round these bloomin temple ang the bloomin shield o rome. 
you good go. you ain t like to shoot yourself not while there s a chanst of liquor. me an learoyd ll stay at ome an keep shop case o anythin turnin up. but you go out with a gas pipe gun an ketch the little peacock or somethin. you kin get one day s leave easy a winkin. go along an get it an get peacock or somethin. 
jock say mulvaney turn to learoyd who be half asleep under the shadow of the bank. he rouse slowly. 
sitha mulvaaney go say he. 
and mulvaney go. curse his ally with irish fluency and barrack room point. 
take note say he when he have win his holiday and appear dress in his rough clothe with the only other regimental fowl piece in his hand. take note jock an you orth ri i be goin in the face av my own will all for to please you. i misdoubt anythin will come av permiscuous huntin afther peacock in a desolit lan. an i know that i will lie down an die wid thirrrst. me catch peacock for you ye lazy scutts an be sacrifice by the peasanthry ugh. 
he wave a huge paw and go away. 
at twilight long before the appoint hour he return empty hand much begrime with dirt. 
peacock. query ortheris from the safe rest of a barrack room table whereon he be smoke cross legged learoyd fast asleep on a bench. 
jock say mulvaney without answer a he stir up the sleeper. jock can ye fight. will ye fight. 
very slowly the mean of the word communicate itself to the half rouse man. he understand and again what might these thing mean. mulvaney be shake him savagely. meantime the men in the room howl with delight. there be war in the confederacy at last war and the break of bond. 
barrack room etiquette be stringent. on the direct challenge must follow the direct reply. this be more bind than the tie of try friendship. once again mulvaney repeat the question. learoyd answer by the only mean in his power and so swiftly that the irishman have barely time to avoid the blow. the laughter around increase. learoyd look bewilderedly at his friend himself a greatly bewilder. ortheris drop from the table because his world be fall. 
come outside say mulvaney and a the occupant of the barrack room prepare joyously to follow he turn and say furiously there will be no fight this night onless any wan av you be wishful to assist. the man that doe follow on. 
no man move. the three pass out into the moonlight learoyd fumble with the button of his coat. the parade grind be desert except for the scurry jackal. mulvaney s impetuous rush carry his companion far into the open ere learoyd attempt to turn round and continue the discussion. 
be still now. twas my fault for beginnin thing in the middle av an end jock. i should ha comminst wid an explanation. but jock dear on your sowl be ye fit think you for the fine fight that iv be betther than fightin me. considher before ye answer. 
more than ever puzzle learoyd turn round two or three time felt an arm kick tentatively and answer ah m fit. he be accustom to fight blindly at the bid of the superior mind. 
they sit them down the men look on from afar and mulvaney untangle himself in mighty word. 
followin your fool scheme i wint out into the thrackless desert beyond the barricks. an there i meet a pious hindu dhriving a bullock kyart. i tuk ut for grant he wud be delight for to convoy me a piece an i jump in. 
you long lazy black haired swine drawl ortheris who would have do the same thing under similar circumstance. 
twas the height av policy. that naygur man dhruv mile an mile a far a the new railway line they re buildin now back av the tavi river. ti a kyart for dhirt only say he now an again timoreously to get me out av ut. dhirt i be sez i an the dhryest that you iv kyarted. dhrive on me son an glory be wid you. at that i wint to slape an take no heed till he pull up on the embankmint av the line where the cooly be pilin mud. there be a matther av two thousand cooly on that line you remimber that. prisintly a bell ring an they throops off to a big pay shed. where s the white man in charge. sez i to my kyart dhriver. in the shed sez he engage on a riffle. a fwhat. sez i. riffle sez he. you take ticket. he take money. you get nothin. 
oho. sez i that s fwhat the shuperior an cultivate man call a raffle me misbeguided child av darkness an sin. lead on to that raffle though fwhat the mischief ti doin so far away from ut home which be the charity bazaar at christmas an the colonel s wife grinnin behind the tea table be more than i know. wid that i wint to the shed an find twas pay day among the cooly. their wage be on a table forninst a big fine red buck av a man sivun fut high four fut wide an three fut thick wid a fist on him like a corn sack. he be payin the cooly fair an easy but he wud ask each man if he wud raffle that month an each man sez. yes av course. thin he wud deduct from their wage accordin. whin all be pay he fill an ould cigar box full av gun wad an scatthered ut among the cooly. they do not take much joy av that performince an small wondher. a man close to me pick up a black gun wad an sing out i have ut. good may ut do you sez i. the coolie wint forward to this big fine red man who throw a cloth off av the most sumpshus jooled enamel an variously bedivilled sedan chair i iv saw. 
sedan chair. put your ead in a bag. that be a palanquin. don t yer know a palanquin when you see it. say ortheris with great scorn. 
i chuse to call ut sedan chair an chair ut shall be little man continue the irishman. twas a most amazin chair all line wid pink silk an fit wid red silk curtain. here ut be sez the red man. here ut be sez the coolie an he grin weakly way. be ut any use to you. sez the red man. no sez the coolie. i d like to make a presint av ut to you. i be graciously please to accept that same sez the red man. an at that all the cooly cry aloud in fwhat be mint for cheerful note an wint back to their diggin lavin me alone in the shed. the red man saw me an his face grow blue on his big fat neck. fwhat d you want here. sez he. standin room an no more sez i onless it may be fwhat ye niver have an that s manner ye rafflin ruffian for i be not goin to have the service throd upon. out of this sez he. i m in charge av this section av construction. i m in charge av mesilf sez i an it s like i will stay a while. d ye raffle much in these part. fwhat s that to you. sez he. nothin sez i but a great dale to you for begad i m thinkin you get the full half av your revenue from that sedan chair. be ut always raffle so. i sez an wid that i wint to a coolie to ask question. bhoys that man s name be dearsley an he s be rafflin that ould sedan chair monthly this matther av nine month. ivry coolie on the section take a ticket or he give em the go wanst a month on pay day. ivry coolie that win ut give ut back to him for ti too big to carry away an he d sack the man that thried to sell ut. that dearsley ha be makin the rowlin wealth av roshus by nefarious rafflin. think av the burnin shame to the sufferin coolie man that the army in injia be bind to protect an nourish in their bosom. two thousand cooly defraud wanst a month. 
dom t cooly. ha t get t cheer man. say learoyd. 
hould on. havin onearthed this amazin an stupenjus fraud commit by the man dearsley i hild a council av war. he thryin all the time to sejuce me into a fight with opprobrious language. that sedan chair niver belong by right to any foreman av cooly. ti a king s chair or a quane s. there s gold on ut an silk an all manner av trapesemints. bhoys ti not for me to countenance any sort av wrong doin me bein the ould man but anyway he ha have ut nine month an he dare not make throuble av ut be take from him. five mile away or ut may be six. 
there be a long pause and the jackal howl merrily. learoyd bar one arm and contemplate it in the moonlight. then he nod partly to himself and partly to his friend. ortheris wriggle with suppress emotion. 
i think ye wud see the reasonableness av ut say mulvaney. i make bould to say a much to the man before. he be for a direct front attack fut horse an gun an all for nothin seein that i have no thransport to convey the machine away. i will not argue wid you sez i this day but subsequently mister dearsley me rafflin jool we talk ut out lengthways. ti no good policy to swindle the naygur av his hard earn emolumints an by presint informashin twas the kyart man that tould me ye ve be perpethrating that same for nine month. but i m a just man sez i an overlookin the presumpshin that yondher settee wid the gild top be not come by honust at that he turn sky green so i know thing be more thrue than tellable not come by honust i m willin to compound the felony for this month s winnin s. 
ah. ho. from learoyd and ortheris. 
that man dearsley s rushin on his fate continue mulvaney solemnly wag his head. all hell have no name bad enough for me that tide. faith he call me a robber. me. that be savin him from continuin in his evil way widout a remonstrince an to a man av conscience a remonstrince may change the chune av his life. ti not for me to argue sez i fwhatever ye be mister dearsley but by my hand i ll take away the temptation for you that lie in that sedan chair. you will have to fight me for ut sez he for well i know you will never dare make report to any one. fight i will sez i but not this day for i m rejuced for want av nourishment. ye re an ould bould hand sez he sizin me up an down. an a jool av a fight we will have. eat now an dhrink an go your way. wid that he give me some hump an whisky good whisky an we talk av this an that the while. it go hard on me now sez i wipin my mouth to confiscate that piece av furniture but justice be justice. ye ve not get ut yet sez he. there s the fight between. there be sez i an a good fight. ye shall have the pick av the best quality in my rigimint for the dinner you have give this day. thin i come hot foot to you two. hould your tongue the both. ti this way. to morrow we three will go there an he shall have his pick betune me an jock. jock s a deceivin fighter for he be all fat to the eye an he move slow. now i m all beef to the look an i move quick. by my reckonin the dearsley man win t take me. so me an orth ri ll see fair play. jock i tell you twill be big fightin whip wid the cream above the jam. afther the business twill take a good three av u jock ll be very hurt to haul away that sedan chair. 
palanquin. this from ortheris. 
fwhatever ut be we must have ut. ti the only sellin piece av property widin reach that we can get so cheap. an fwhat s a fight afther all. he ha rob the naygur man dishonust. we rob him honust for the sake av the whisky he give me. 
but wot ll we do with the bloomin article when we ve get it. them palanquin be a big a ouse an uncommon ard to sell a mccleary say when ye steal the sentry box from the curragh. 
who s goin to do t fightin. say learoyd and ortheris subside. the three return to barrack without a word. mulvaney s last argument clinch the matter. this palanquin be property vendible and to be attain in the simple and least embarrass fashion. it would eventually become beer. great be mulvaney. 
next afternoon a procession of three form itself and disappear into the scrub in the direction of the new railway line. learoyd alone be without care for mulvaney dive darkly into the future and little ortheris fear the unknown. what befall at that interview in the lonely pay shed by the side of the half build embankment only a few hundred cooly know and their tale be confuse one run thus. 
we be at work. three men in red coat come. they saw the sahib dearsley sahib. they make oration. and noticeably the small man among the red coat. dearsley sahib also make oration and use many very strong word. upon this talk they depart together to an open space and there the fat man in the red coat fight with dearsley sahib after the custom of white men with his hand make no noise and never at all pull dearsley sahib s hair. such of u a be not afraid behold these thing for just so long a time a a man need to cook the mid day meal. the small man in the red coat have possess himself of dearsley sahib s watch. no he do not steal that watch. he hold it in his hand and at certain season make outcry and the twain cease their combat which be like the combat of young bull in spring. both men be soon all red but dearsley sahib be much more red than the other. see this and fear for his life because we greatly love him some fifty of u make shift to rush upon the red coat. but a certain man very black a to the hair and in no way to be confuse with the small man or the fat man who fight that man we affirm run upon u and of u he embrace some ten or fifty in both arm and beat our head together so that our liver turn to water and we run away. it be not good to interfere in the fighting of white men. after that dearsley sahib fell and do not rise these men jump upon his stomach and despoil him of all his money and attempt to fire the pay shed and depart. be it true that dearsley sahib make no complaint of these latter thing have be do. we be senseless with fear and do not at all remember. there be no palanquin near the pay shed. what do we know about palanquin. be it true that dearsley sahib doe not return to this place on account of his sickness for ten day. this be the fault of those bad men in the red coat who should be severely punish. for dearsley sahib be both our father and mother and we love him much. yet if dearsley sahib doe not return to this place at all we will speak the truth. there be a palanquin for the up keep of which we be force to pay nine tenth of our monthly wage. on such mulct dearsley sahib allow u to make obeisance to him before the palanquin. what could we do. we be poor men. he take a full half of our wage. will the government repay u those money. those three men in red coat bore the palanquin upon their shoulder and depart. all the money that dearsley sahib have take from u be in the cushion of that palanquin. therefore they steal it. thousand of rupee be there all our money. it be our bank box to fill which we cheerfully contribute to dearsley sahib three seventh of our monthly wage. why doe the white man look upon u with the eye of disfavour. before god there be a palanquin and now there be no palanquin. and if they send the police here to make inquisition we can only say that there never ha be any palanquin. why should a palanquin be near these work. we be poor men and we know nothing. 
such be the simple version of the simple story connect with the descent upon dearsley. from the lip of the cooly i receive it. dearsley himself be in no condition to say anything and mulvaney preserve a massive silence break only by the occasional lick of the lip. he have see a fight so gorgeous that even his power of speech be take from him. i respect that reserve until three day after the affair i discover in a disused stable in my quarter a palanquin of unchastened splendour evidently in past day the litter of a queen. the pole whereby it swing between the shoulder of the bearer be rich with the paint papier mache of cashmere. the shoulder pad be of yellow silk. the panel of the litter itself be ablaze with the love of all the god and goddess of the hindu pantheon lacquer on cedar. the cedar slide door be fit with hasp of translucent jaipur enamel and run in groove shoe with silver. the cushion be of brocade delhi silk and the curtain which once hide any glimpse of the beauty of the king s palace be stiff with gold. close investigation show that the entire fabric be everywhere rub and discolour by time and wear. but even thus it be sufficiently gorgeous to deserve house on the threshold of a royal zenana. i find no fault with it except that it be in my stable. then try to lift it by the silver shoe shoulder pole i laugh. the road from dearsley s pay shed to the cantonment be a narrow and uneven one and traverse by three very inexperienced palanquin bearer one of whom be sorely batter about the head must have be a path of torment. still i do not quite recognise the right of the three musketeer to turn me into a fence for steal property. 
i m askin you to warehouse ut say mulvaney when he be bring to consider the question. there s no steal in ut. dearsley tould u we cud have ut if we fight. jock fight an oh sorr when the throuble be at ut fine an jock be bleedin like a stick pig an little orth ri be shquealin on one leg chewin big bite out av dearsley s watch i wud ha give my place at the fight to have have you see wan round. he tuk jock a i suspicioned he would an jock be deceptive. nine roun s they be even match an at the tenth about that palanquin now. there s not the least throuble in the world or we wud not ha bring ut here. you will ondherstand that the queen god bless her. doe not reckon for a privit soldier to kape elephints an palanquin an sich in barricks. afther we have dhragged ut down from dearsley s through that cruel scrub that near break orth ri s heart we set ut in the ravine for a night. an a thief av a porcupine an a civet cat av a jackal roost in ut a well we know in the mornin. i put ut to you sorr be an elegint palanquin fit for the princess the natural abidin place av all the vermin in cantonmints. we bring ut to you afther dhark and put ut in your shtable. do not let your conscience prick. think av the rejoicin men in the pay shed yonder lookin at dearsley wid his head tie up in a towel an well knowin that they can dhraw their pay ivry month widout stoppage for riffle. indirectly sorr you have rescue from an onprincipled son av a night hawk the peasanthry av a numerous village. an besides will i let that sedan chair rot on our hand. not i. ti not every day a piece av pure joolry come into the market. there s not a king widin these forty mile he wave his hand round the dusty horizon not a king wud not be glad to buy ut. some day meself whin i have leisure i ll take ut up along the road an dishpose av ut. 
how. say i for i know the man be capable of anything. 
get into ut av coorse and keep wan eye open through the curtain. whin i see a likely man av the native persuasion i will descind blushin from my canopy and say buy a palanquin ye black scutt. i will have to hire four men to carry me first though. and that s impossible till next pay day. 
curiously enough learoyd who have fight for the prize and in the win secure the high pleasure life have to offer him be altogether dispose to undervalue it while ortheris openly say it would be good to break the thing up. dearsley he argue might be a many side man capable despite his magnificent fight quality of set in motion the machinery of the civil law a thing much abhor by the soldier. under any circumstance their fun have come and pass. the next pay day be close at hand when there would be beer for all. wherefore long conserve the paint palanquin. 
a first class rifle shoot an a good little man av your inch you be say mulvaney. but you niver have a head worth a soft boil egg. ti me ha to lie awake av night schamin an plottin for the three av u. orth ri me son ti no matther av a few gallon av beer no nor twenty gallon but tub an vat an firkin in that sedan chair. who ut be an what ut be an how ut get there we do not know. but i know in my bone that you an me an jock wid his sprain thumb will get a fortune thereby. lave me alone an let me think. 
meantime the palanquin stay in my stall the key of which be in mulvaney s hand. 
pay day come and with it beer. it be not in experience to hope that mulvaney dry by four week drought would avoid excess. next morning he and the palanquin have disappear. he have take the precaution of get three day leave to see a friend on the railway and the colonel well know that the seasonal outburst be near and hop it would spend it force beyond the limit of his jurisdiction cheerfully give him all he demand. at this point mulvaney s history a record in the mess room stop. 
ortheris carry it not much further. no e wasn t drink say the little man loyally the liquor be no more than feelin it way round inside of im. but e go an fill that ole bloomin palanquin with bottle fore e go off. e s go an ired six men to carry im an i ad to elp im into be nupshal couch cause e wouldn t ear reason. e s go off in be shirt an trousies swearin tremenjus go down the road in the palanquin wavin be leg out o windy.

now you arx me a question. e say e be goin to sell that palanquin but from observation what happen when i be stuffin im through the door i fancy e s go to the new embankment to mock at dearsley. soon a jock s off duty i m goin there to see if e s safe not mulvaney but t other man. my saint but i pity im a elps terence out o the palanquin when e s once fair drink.

reinforce by learoyd ortheris seek the foreman of the coolie gang. dearsley s head be still embellish with towel. mulvaney drink or sober would have strike no man in that condition and dearsley indignantly deny that he would have take advantage of the intoxicate brave. 
i have my pick o you two he explain to learoyd and you get my palanquin not before i d make my profit on it. why d i do harm when everything s settle. your man do come here drink a davy s sow on a frosty night come a purpose to mock me stick his head out of the door an call me a crucify hodman. i make him drunk an send him along. but i never touch him. 
to these thing learoyd slow to perceive the evidence of sincerity answer only if owt come to mulvaaney long o you i ll gripple you clout or no clout on your ugly head an i ll draw t throat twistyways man. see there now. 
the embassy remove itself and dearsley the batter laugh alone over his supper that even. 
three day pass a fourth and a fifth. the week draw to a close and mulvaney do not return. he his royal palanquin and his six attendant have vanish into air. a very large and very tipsy soldier his foot stick out of the litter of a reign princess be not a thing to travel along the way without comment. yet no man of all the country round have see any such wonder. he be and he be not. and learoyd suggest the immediate smashment of dearsley a a sacrifice to his ghost. ortheris insist that all be well and in the light of past experience his hope seem reasonable. 
when mulvaney go up the road say he e s like to go a very long way up specially when e s so blue drink a e be now. but what git me be be not bein eard of pullin wool off the nigger somewhere about. that don t look good. the drink must ha die out in im by this unless e s break a bank an then why don t e come back. e didn t ought to ha go off without u. 
even ortheris s heart sink at the end of the seventh day for half the regiment be out scour the country side and learoyd have be force to fight two men who hint openly that mulvaney have desert. to do him justice the colonel laugh at the notion even when it be put forward by his much trust adjutant. 
mulvaney would a soon think of desert a you would say he. no. he s either fall into a mischief among the villager and yet that isn t likely for he d blarney himself out of the pit. or else he be engage on urgent private affair some stupendous devilment that we shall hear of at mess after it ha be the round of the barrack room. the bad of it be that i shall have to give him twenty eight day confinement at least for be absent without leave just when i most want him to lick the new batch of recruit into shape. i never know a man who could put a polish on young soldier a quickly a mulvaney can. how doe he do it. 
with blarney and the buckle end of a belt sir say the adjutant. he be worth a couple of non commission officer when we be deal with an irish draft and the london lad seem to adore him. the bad of it be that if he go to the cell the other two be neither to hold nor to bind till he come out again. i believe ortheris preach mutiny on those occasion and i know that the mere presence of learoyd mourn for mulvaney kill all the cheerfulness of his room. the sergeant tell me that he allow no man to laugh when he feel unhappy. they be a queer gang. 
for all that i wish we have a few more of them. i like a well conduct regiment but these pasty face shifty eye mealy mouth young sloucher from the depot worry me sometimes with their offensive virtue. they don t seem to have backbone enough to do anything but play card and prowl round the marry quarter. i believe i d forgive that old villain on the spot if he turn up with any sort of explanation that i could in decency accept. 
not likely to be much difficulty about that sir say the adjutant. mulvaney s explanation be only one degree le wonderful than his performance. they say that when he be in the black tyrone before he come to u he be discover on the bank of the liffey try to sell his colonel s charger to a donegal dealer a a perfect lady s hack. shackbolt command the tyrone then. 
shackbolt must have have apoplexy at the think of his ramp war horse answer to that description. he use to buy unbacked devil and tame them on some pet theory of starvation. what do mulvaney say. 
that he be a member of the society for the prevention of cruelty to animal anxious to sell the poor baste where he would get something to fill out his dimple. shackbolt laugh but i fancy that be why mulvaney exchange to ours. 
i wish he be back say the colonel. for i like him and believe he like me. 
that even to cheer our soul learoyd ortheris and i go into the waste to smoke out a porcupine. all the dog attend but even their clamour and they begin to discus the shortcoming of porcupine before they leave cantonment could not take u out of ourselves. a large low moon turn the top of the plume grass to silver and the stunt camelthorn bush and sour tamarisk into the likeness of troop devil. the smell of the sun have not leave the earth and little aimless wind blow across the rise garden to the southward bring the scent of dry rose and water. our fire once start and the dog craftily dispose to wait the dash of the porcupine we climb to the top of a rain scar hillock of earth and look across the scrub seam with cattle path white with the long grass and dot with spot of level pond bottom where the snipe would gather in winter. 
this say ortheris with a sigh a he take in the unkempt desolation of it all this be sanguinary. this be unusually sanguinary. sort o mad country. like a grate when the fire s put out by the sun. he shade his eye against the moonlight. an there s a loony dancin in the middle of it all. quite right. i d dance too if i wasn t so downheart. 
there prance a portent in the face of the moon a huge and rag spirit of the waste that flap it wing from afar. it have rise out of the earth. it be come towards u and it outline be never twice the same. the toga table cloth or dress gown whatever the creature wear take a hundred shape. once it stop on a neighbour mound and fling all it leg and arm to the wind. 
my but that scarecrow a get em bad. say ortheris. seem like if e come any furder we ll ave to argify with im.

you damn fool. say they and severally pound him with their fist.

the latter part of the sentence destroy the suspicion raise by the former. any one would have be justify in regard mulvaney a mad. he be hatless and shoeless and his shirt and trouser be drop off him. but he wear one wondrous garment a gigantic cloak that fell from collar bone to heel of pale pink silk work all over in cunning needlework of hand long since dead with the love of the hindu god. the monstrous figure leap in and out of the light of the fire a he settle the fold round him.

i be say the irishman an by the same token the broidery be scrapin my hide off. i ve live in this sumpshus counterpane for four day. me son i begin to ondherstand why the naygur be no use. widout me boot an me trousies like an openwork stock on a gyurl s leg at a dance i begin to feel like a naygur man all fearful an timoreous. give me a pipe an i ll tell on.
