the man do not move. he be sit on a low red lacquer couch in a room furnish only with a blue and white floor cloth some rug and a very complete collection of native cushion. at his foot sit a woman of sixteen and she be all but all the world in his eye. by every rule and law she should have be otherwise for he be an englishman and she a mussulman s daughter buy two year before from her mother who be leave without money would have sell ameera shriek to the prince of darkness if the price have be sufficient. 
it be a contract enter into with a light heart. but even before the girl have reach her bloom she come to fill the great portion of john holden s life. for her and the wither hag her mother he have take a little house overlook the great red wall city and find when the marigold have spring up by the well in the courtyard and ameera have establish herself accord to her own idea of comfort and her mother have cease grumble at the inadequacy of the cook place the distance from the daily market and at matter of house keep in general that the house be to him his home. any one could enter his bachelor s bungalow by day or night and the life that he lead there be an unlovely one. in the house in the city his foot only could pas beyond the out courtyard to the woman s room. and when the big wooden gate be bolt behind him he be king in his own territory with ameera for queen. and there be go to be add to this kingdom a third person whose arrival holden felt incline to resent. it interfere with his perfect happiness. it disarrange the orderly peace of the house that be his own. but ameera be wild with delight at the think of it and her mother not le so. the love of a man and particularly a white man be at the best an inconstant affair but it might both woman argue be hold fast by a baby s hand. and then ameera would always say then he will never care for the white mem log. i hate them all i hate them all.

holden sit silent on the couch think of the future and his thought be not pleasant. the drawback of a double life be manifold. the government with singular care have order him out of the station for a fortnight on special duty in the place of a man who be watch by the bedside of a sick wife. the verbal notification of the transfer have be edge by a cheerful remark that holden ought to think himself lucky in be a bachelor and a free man. he come to break the news to ameera. 
it be not good she say slowly but it be not all bad. there be my mother here and no harm will come to me unless indeed i die of pure joy. go thou to thy work and think no troublesome thought. when the day be do i believe. nay i be sure. and and then i shall lay him in thy arm and thou wilt love me for ever. the train go to night at midnight be it not. go now and do not let thy heart be heavy by cause of me. but thou wilt not delay in return. thou wilt not stay on the road to talk to the bold white mem log. come back to me swiftly my life. 
a he leave the courtyard to reach his horse that be tether to the gate post holden speak to the white haired old watchman who guard the house and bid him under certain contingency despatch the fill up telegraph form that holden give him. it be all that could be do and with the sensation of a man who ha attend his own funeral holden go away by the night mail to his exile. every hour of the day he dread the arrival of the telegram and every hour of the night he picture to himself the death of ameera. in consequence his work for the state be not of first rate quality nor be his temper towards his colleague of the most amiable. the fortnight end without a sign from his home and tear to piece by his anxiety holden return to be swallow up for two precious hour by a dinner at the club wherein he hear a a man hear in a swoon voice tell him how execrably he have perform the other man s duty and how he have endear himself to all his associate. then he flee on horseback through the night with his heart in his mouth. there be no answer at first to his blow on the gate and he have just wheel his horse round to kick it in when pir khan appear with a lantern and hold his stirrup.

four men each entitle to life liberty and the pursuit of happiness sit at a table play whist. the thermometer mark for them one hundred and one degree of heat. the room be darken till it be only just possible to distinguish the pip of the card and the very white face of the player. a tattered rotten punkah of whitewash calico be puddle the hot air and whine dolefully at each stroke. outside lay gloom of a november day in london. there be neither sky sun nor horizon nothing but a brown purple haze of heat. it be a though the earth be die of apoplexy. 
from time to time cloud of tawny dust rise from the grind without wind or warn fling themselves tablecloth wise among the top of the parch tree and come down again. then a whirl dust devil would scutter across the plain for a couple of mile break and fall outward though there be nothing to check it flight save a long low line of pile railway sleeper white with the dust a cluster of hut make of mud condemn rail and canvas and the one squat four room bungalow that belong to the assistant engineer in charge of a section of the gaudhari state line then under construction. 
the four strip to the thin of sleep suit play whist crossly with wrangling a to lead and return. it be not the best kind of whist but they have take some trouble to arrive at it. mottram of the indian survey have ride thirty and rail one hundred mile from his lonely post in the desert since the night before. lowndes of the civil service on special duty in the political department have come a far to escape for an instant the miserable intrigue of an impoverish native state whose king alternately fawn and bluster for more money from the pitiful revenue contribute by hard wring peasant and despair camel breeder. spurstow the doctor of the line have leave a cholera stricken camp of cooly to look after itself for forty eight hour while he associate with white men once more. hummil the assistant engineer be the host. he stand fast and receive his friend thus every sunday if they could come in. when one of them fail to appear he would send a telegram to his last address in order that he might know whether the defaulter be dead or alive. there be very many place in the east where it be not good or kind to let your acquaintance drop out of sight even for one short week. 
the player be not conscious of any special regard for each other. they squabble whenever they meet. but they ardently desire to meet a men without water desire to drink. they be lonely folk who understand the dread mean of loneliness. they be all under thirty year of age which be too soon for any man to posse that knowledge.

the mutiny of the maverick.

when three obscure gentleman in san francisco argue on insufficient premise they condemn a fellow creature to a most unpleasant death in a far country which have nothing whatever to do with the unite state. they foregather at the top of a tenement house in tehama street an unsavoury quarter of the city and there call for certain drink they conspire because they be conspirator by trade officially know a the third three of the i. a. a. an institution for the propagation of pure light not to be confound with any others though it be affiliate to many. the second three live in montreal and work among the poor there. the first three have their home in new york not far from castle garden and write regularly once a week to a small house near one of the big hotel at boulogne. what happen after that a particular section of scotland yard know too well and laugh at. a conspirator detest ridicule. more men have be stab with lucrezia borgia dagger and drop into the thames for laugh at head centre and triangle than for betray secret. for this be human nature. 
the third three conspire over whisky cocktail and a clean sheet of notepaper against the british empire and all that lay therein. this work be very like what men without discernment call politics before a general election. you pick out and discus in the company of congenial friend all the weak point in your opponent organisation and unconsciously dwell upon and exaggerate all their mishap till it seem to you a miracle that the hat party hold together for an hour. 
our principle be not so much active demonstration that we leave to others a passive embarrassment to weaken and unnerve say the first man. wherever an organisation be cripple wherever a confusion be throw into any branch of any department we gain a step for those who take on the work. we be but the forerunner. he be a german enthusiast and editor of a newspaper from whose lead article he quote frequently. 
that curse empire make so many blunder of her own that unless we double the year s average i guess it wouldn t strike her anything special have occur say the second man. be you prepare to say that all our resource be equal to blow off the muzzle of a hundred ton gun or spike a ten thousand ton ship on a plain rock in clear daylight. they can beat u at our own game. good join hand with the practical branch. we re in fund now. try a direct scare in a crowd street. they value their greasy hide. he be the drag upon the wheel and an americanise irishman of the second generation despise his own race and hat the other. he have learn caution. 
the third man drink his cocktail and speak no word. he be the strategist but unfortunately his knowledge of life be limit. he pick a letter from his breast pocket and throw it across the table. that epistle to the heathen contain some very concise direction from the first three in new york. it say. 
the boom in black iron ha already affect the eastern market where our agent have be force down the english hold stock among the small buyer who watch the turn of share. any immediate operation such a western bear would increase their willingness to unload. this however cannot be expect till they see clearly that foreign iron master be witting to co operate. mulcahy should be dispatch to feel the pulse of the market and act accordingly. maverick be at present the best for our purpose. p. d. q.

already. surely they be in too great a hurry. all that dhulip singh could do in india he ha do down to the distribution of his photograph among the peasantry. ho. ho. the paris firm arrange that and he ha no substantial money back from the other power. even our agent in india know he hasn t. what be the use of our organisation waste men on work that be already do. of course the irish regiment in india be half mutinous a they stand. 
this show how near a lie may come to the truth. an irish regiment for just so long a it stand still be generally a hard handful to control be reckless and rough. when however it be move in the direction of musketry fire it become strangely and unpatriotically content with it lot. it ha even be hear to cheer the queen with enthusiasm on these occasion. 
but the notion of tamper with the army be from the point of view of tehama street an altogether sound one. there be no shadow of stability in the policy of an english government and the most sacred oath of england would even if engross on vellum find very few buyer among colony and dependency that have suffer from vain belief. but there remain to england always her army. that cannot change except in the matter of uniform and equipment. the officer may write to the paper demand the head of the horse guard in default of clean redress for grievance. the men may break loose across a country town and seriously startle the publican. but neither officer nor men have it in their composition to mutiny after the continental manner. the english people when they trouble to think about the army at all be and with justice absolutely assure that it be absolutely trustworthy. imagine for a moment their emotion on realise that such and such a regiment be in open revolt from cause directly due to england s management of ireland. they would probably send the regiment to the poll forthwith and examine their own conscience a to their duty to erin. but they would never be easy any more. and it be this vague unhappy mistrust that the i. a. a. be labour to produce. 
sheer waste of breath say the second man after a pause in the council i don t see the use of tamper with their fool army but it ha be try before and we must try it again. it look well in the report. if we send one man from here you may bet your life that other men be go too. order up mulcahy. 
they order him up a slim slight dark haired young man devour with that blind rancorous hatred of england that only reach it full growth across the atlantic. he have suck it from his mother s breast in the little cabin at the back of the northern avenue of new york. he have be teach his right and his wrong in german and irish on the canal front of chicago. and san francisco hold men who tell him strange and awful thing of the great blind power over the sea. once when business take him across the atlantic he have serve in an english regiment and be insubordinate have suffer extremely. he draw all his idea of england that be not breed by the cheap patriotic print from one iron fisted colonel and an unbend adjutant. he would go to the mine if need be to teach his gospel. and he go a his instruction advise p. d. q. which mean with speed to introduce embarrassment into an irish regiment already half mutinous quarter among sikh peasantry all wear miniature of his highness dhulip singh maharaja of the punjab next their heart and all eagerly expect his arrival. other information equally valuable be give him by his master. he be to be cautious but never to grudge expense in win the heart of the men in the regiment. his mother in new york would supply fund and he be to write to her once a month. life be pleasant for a man who ha a mother in new york to send him two hundred pound a year over and above his regimental pay. 
in process of time thank to his intimate knowledge of drill and musketry exercise the excellent mulcahy wear the corporal s stripe go out in a troopship and join her majesty s royal loyal musketeer commonly know a the maverick because they be masterless and unbranded cattle son of small farmer in county clare shoeless vagabond of kerry herder of bally vegan much want moonlighter from the bare rainy headland of the south coast officer by o more brady hill kilreas and the like. never to outward seem be there more promise material to work on. the first three have choose their regiment well. it fear nothing that move or talk save the colonel and the regimental roman catholic chaplain the fat father dennis who hold the key of heaven and hell and blare like an angry bull when he desire to be convince. him also it love because on occasion of stress he be use to tuck up his cassock and charge with the rest into the merry of the fray where he always find good man that the saint send him a revolver when there be a fall private to be protect or but this come a an afterthought his own gray head to be guard. 
cautiously a he have be instruct tenderly and with much beer mulcahy open his project to such a he deem fit to listen. and these be one and all of that quaint crook sweet profoundly irresponsible and profoundly lovable race that fight like fiend argue like child reason like woman obey like men and jest like their own goblin of the rath through rebellion loyalty want woe or war. the underground work of a conspiracy be always dull and very much the same the world over. at the end of six month the seed always fall on good grind mulcahy speak almost explicitly hint darkly in the approve fashion at dread power behind him and advise nothing more nor le than mutiny. be they not dog evilly treat. have they not all their own and their national revenge to satisfy. who in these day would do aught to nine hundred men in rebellion. who again could stay them if they break for the sea lick up on their way other regiment only too anxious to join. and afterwards. here follow windy promise of gold and preferment office and honour ever dear to a certain type of irishman.

from that day date the mutiny of the maverick to the joy of mulcahy and the pride of his mother in new york the good lady who send the money for the beer. never so far a word go be such a mutiny. the conspirator lead by dan grady and horse egan pour in daily. they be sound men men to be trust and they all want blood. but first they must have beer. they curse the queen they mourn over ireland they suggest hideous plunder of the indian country side and then ala some of the young men would go forth and wallow on the grind in spasm of wicked laughter. 
the genius of the irish for conspiracy be remarkable. none the le they would swear no oath but those of their own make which be rare and curious and they be always at pain to impress mulcahy with the risk they run. naturally the flood of beer work demoralisation. but mulcahy confuse the cause of thing and when a very muzzy maverick smite a sergeant on the nose or call his command officer a bald head old lard bladder and even bad name he fancy that rebellion and not liquor be at the bottom of the outbreak. other gentleman who have concern themselves in large conspiracy have make the same error. 
the hot season in which they protest no man could rebel come to an end and mulcahy suggest a visible return for his teaching. a to the actual upshot of the mutiny he care nothing. it would be enough if the english infatuatedly trust to the integrity of their army should be startle with news of an irish regiment revolt from political consideration. his persistent demand would have end at dan s instigation in a regimental belt which in all probability would have kill him and cut off the supply of beer have not he be send on special duty some fifty mile away from the cantonment to cool his heel in a mud fort and dismount obsolete artillery. then the colonel of the maverick read his newspaper diligently and scent frontier trouble from afar post to the army headquarter and plead with the commander in chief for certain privilege to be grant under certain contingency. which contingency come about only a week late when the annual little war on the border develop itself and the colonel return to carry the good news to the maverick. he hold the promise of the chief for active service and the men must get ready. 
on the even of the same day mulcahy an unconsidered corporal yet great in conspiracy return to cantonment and hear sound of strife and howling from afar off. the mutiny have break out and the barrack of the maverick be one white wash pandemonium. a private tear through the barrack square gasp in his ear service. active service. it s a burnin shame. oh joy the maverick have rise on the eve of battle. they would not noble and loyal son of ireland serve the queen long. the news would flash through the country side and over to england and he mulcahy the trust of the third three have bring about the crash. the private stand in the middle of the square and curse colonel regiment officer and doctor particularly the doctor by his god. an orderly of the native cavalry regiment clatter through the mob of soldier. he be half lift half drag from his horse beat on the back with mighty hand clap till his eye water and call all manner of endear name. yes the maverick have fraternise with the native troop. who then be the agent among the latter that have blindly work with mulcahy so well. 
an officer slink almost run from the mess to a barrack. he be mob by the infuriate soldiery who close round but do not kill him for he fight his way to shelter fly for the life. mulcahy could have weep with pure joy and thankfulness. the very prisoner in the guard room be shake the bar of their cell and howl like wild beast and from every barrack pour the boom a of a big war drum. 
mulcahy hasten to his own barrack. he could hardly hear himself speak. eighty men be pound with fist and heel the table and trestle eighty men flush with mutiny strip to their shirt sleeve their knapsack half pack for the march to the sea make the two inch board thunder again a they chant to a tune that mulcahy know well the sacred war song of the maverick.

mulcahy have not take into account the possibility of be send on active service. he have make up his mind that he would not go under any circumstance but fortune be against him. 
sick you. say the doctor who have serve an unholy apprenticeship to his trade in tralee poorhouse. you re only home sick and what you call varicose vein come from over eat. a little gentle exercise will cure that. and late mulcahy my man everybody be allow to apply for a sick certificate once. if he try it twice we call him by an ugly name. go back to your duty and let s hear no more of your disease. 
i be ashamed to say that horse egan enjoy the study of mulcahy s soul in those day and dan take an equal interest. together they would communicate to their corporal all the dark lore of death which be the portion of those who have see men die. egan have the large experience but dan the fine imagination. mulcahy shiver when the former speak of the knife a an intimate acquaintance or the latter dwell with love particularity on the fate of those who wound and helpless have be overlook by the ambulance and have fall into the hand of the afghan woman folk. 
mulcahy know that the mutiny for the present at least be dead. know too that a change have come over dan s usually respectful attitude towards him and horse egan s laughter and frequent allusion to abortive conspiracy emphasise all that the conspirator have guess. the horrible fascination of the death story however make him seek the men s society. he learn much more than he have bargain for. and in this manner. it be on the last night before the regiment entrain to the front. the barrack be strip of everything movable and the men be too excite to sleep. the bare wall give out a heavy hospital smell of chloride of lime.

mulcahy for some week understand very little of anything at all save that ever at his elbow in camp or at parade stand two big men with soft voice adjure him to commit hari kari l a bad thing should happen to die for the honour of the regiment in decency among the near knife. but mulcahy dread death. he remember certain thing that priest have say in his infancy and his mother not the one at new york start from her sleep with shriek to pray for a husband s soul in torment. it be well to be of a culture intelligence but in time of trouble the weak human mind return to the creed it suck in at the breast and if that creed be not a pretty one trouble follow. also the death he would have to face would be physically painful. most conspirator have large imagination. mulcahy could see himself a he lay on the earth in the night die by various cause. they be all horrible. the mother in new york be very far away and the regiment the engine that once you fall in it grip move you forward whether you will or win t be daily come close to the enemy. 
they be bring to the field of marzun katai and with the black boneens to aid they fight a fight that ha never be set down in the newspaper. in response many believe to the fervent prayer of father dennis the enemy not only elect to fight in the open but make a beautiful fight a many weep irish mother know late. they gather behind wall or flicker across the open in shout mass and be pot valiant in artillery. it be expedient to hold a large reserve and wait for the psychological moment that be be prepare by the shriek shrapnel. therefore the maverick lay down in open order on the brow of a hill to watch the play till their call should come. father dennis whose duty be in the rear to smooth the trouble of the wound have naturally manage to make his way to the foremost of his boy and lay like a black porpoise at length on the grass. to him crawl mulcahy ashen gray demand absolution.

this manoeuvre execute not for publication but a a guarantee of good faith to soothe men demand nerve. you must not hurry you must not look nervous though you know that you be a mark for every rifle within extreme range and above all if you be smite you must make a little noise a possible and roll inwards through the file. it be at this hour when the breeze bring the first salt whiff of the powder to nose rather cold at the tip and the eye can quietly take in the appearance of each red casualty that the strain on the nerve be strong. scotch regiment can endure for half a day and abate no whit of their zeal at the end. english regiment sometimes sulk under punishment while the irish like the french be apt to run forward by one and two which be just a bad a run back. the truly wise commandant of highly string troop allow them in season of wait to hear the sound of their own voice uplift in song. there be a legend of an english regiment that lay by it arm under fire chaunting sam hall to the horror of it newly appoint and pious colonel. the black boneens who be suffer more than the maverick on a hill half a mile away begin presently to explain to all who care to listen.

they should have sing it in the face of england not of the afghan whom it impress a much a do the wild irish yell. 
they come down sing say the unofficial report of the enemy bear from village to village the next day. they continue to sing and it be write that our men could not abide when they come. it be believe that there be magic in the aforesaid song. 
dan and horse egan keep themselves in the neighbourhood of mulcahy. twice the man would have bolt back in the confusion. twice he be heave kick and shoulder back again into the unpaintable inferno of a hotly contest charge. 
at the end the panic excess of his fear drive him into madness beyond all human courage. his eye star at nothing his mouth open and froth and breathe a one in a cold bath he go forward demented while dan toil after him. the charge check at a high mud wall. it be mulcahy who scramble up tooth and nail and hurl down among the bayonet the amaze afghan who bar his way. it be mulcahy keep to the straight line of the rabid dog who lead a collection of ardent soul at a newly unmask battery and fling himself on the muzzle of a gun a his companion dance among the gunner. it be mulcahy who run wildly on from that battery into the open plain where the enemy be retire in sullen group. his hand be empty he have lose helmet and belt and he be bleed from a wind in the neck. dan and horse egan pant and distress have throw themselves down on the grind by the capture gun when they notice mulcahy s charge. 
mad say horse egan critically. mad with fear. he s go straight to his death an shout s no use. 
let him go. watch now. if we fire we ll hit him maybe. 
the last of a hurry crowd of afghan turn at the noise of shoe foot behind him and shift his knife ready to hand. this he saw be no time to take prisoner. mulcahy tear on sob. the straight hold blade go home through the defenceless breast and the body pitch forward almost before a shoot from dan s rifle bring down the slayer and still further hurry the afghan retreat. the two irishman go out to bring in their dead. 
he be give the point and that be an easy death say horse egan view the corpse. but would you ha shoot him danny if he have live. 
he didn t live so there s no sayin. but i doubt i wud have bekase of the fun he give u let alone the beer. hike up his leg horse and we ll bring him in. perhaps ti good this way. 
they bore the poor limp body to the mass of the regiment loll open mouth on their rifle. and there be a general snigger when one of the young subaltern say that be a good man. 
phew say horse egan when a burial party have take over the burden. i m powerful dhry and this remind me there ll be no more beer at all. 
fwhy not. say dan with a twinkle in his eye a he stretch himself for rest. be we not conspirin all we can an while we conspire be we not entitle to free dhrinks. sure his ould mother in new york would not let her son s comrade perish of drouth if she can be reach at the end of a letter. 
you re a janius say horse egan. o coorse she will not. i wish this crool war be over an we d get back to canteen. faith the commander in chief ought to be hang in his own little sword belt for makin u work on wather. 
the maverick be generally of horse egan s opinion. so they make haste to get their work do a soon a possible and their industry be reward by unexpected peace. we can fight the son of adam say the tribesman but we cannot fight the son of eblis and this regiment never stay still in one place. let u therefore come in. they come in and this regiment withdraw to conspire under the leadership of dan grady. 
excellent a a subordinate dan fail altogether a a chief in command possibly because he be too much sway by the advice of the only man in the regiment who could manufacture more than one kind of handwrite. the same mail that bore to mulcahy s mother in new york a letter from the colonel tell her how valiantly her son have fight for the queen and how assuredly he would have be recommend for the victoria cross have he survive carry a communication sign i grieve to say by that same colonel and all the officer of the regiment explain their willingness to do anything which be contrary to the regulation and all kind of revolution if only a little money could be forward to cover incidental expense. daniel grady esquire would receive fund vice mulcahy who be unwell at this present time of write. 
both letter be forward from new york to tehama street san francisco with marginal comment a brief a they be bitter. the third three read and look at each other. then the second conspirator he who believe in join hand with the practical branch begin to laugh and on recover his gravity say gentleman i consider this will be a lesson to u. we re leave again. those curse irish have let u down. i know they would but here he laugh afresh i d give considerable to know what be at the back of it all. 
his curiosity would have be satisfy have he see dan grady discredit regimental conspirator try to explain to his thirsty comrade in india the non arrival of fund from new york. 
the mark of the beast. 
your god and my god do you or i know which be the strong. native proverb. 
east of suez some hold the direct control of providence cease. man be there hand over to the power of the god and devil of asia and the church of england providence only exercise an occasional and modify supervision in the case of englishman. 
this theory account for some of the more unnecessary horror of life in india. it may be stretch to explain my story. 
my friend strickland of the police who know a much of native of india a be good for any man can bear witness to the fact of the case. dumoise our doctor also saw what strickland and i saw. the inference which he draw from the evidence be entirely incorrect. he be dead now. he die in a rather curious manner which ha be elsewhere describe. 
when fleete come to india he own a little money and some land in the himalaya near a place call dharmsala. both property have be leave him by an uncle and he come out to finance them. he be a big heavy genial and inoffensive man. his knowledge of native be of course limit and he complain of the difficulty of the language. 
he ride in from his place in the hill to spend new year in the station and he stay with strickland. on new year s eve there be a big dinner at the club and the night be excusably wet. when men foregather from the uttermost end of the empire they have a right to be riotous. the frontier have send down a contingent o catch em alive o s who have not see twenty white face for a year and be use to ride fifteen mile to dinner at the next fort at the risk of a khyberee bullet where their drink should lie. they profit by their new security for they try to play pool with a curl up hedgehog find in the garden and one of them carry the marker round the room in his teeth. half a dozen planter have come in from the south and be talk horse to the big liar in asia who be try to cap all their story at once. everybody be there and there be a general close up of rank and take stock of our loss in dead or disable that have fall during the past year. it be a very wet night and i remember that we sing auld lang syne with our foot in the polo championship cup and our head among the star and swear that we be all dear friend. then some of u go away and annex burma and some try to open up the soudan and be open up by fuzzies in that cruel scrub outside suakim and some find star and medal and some be marry which be bad and some do other thing which be bad and the others of u stay in our chain and strive to make money on insufficient experience. 
fleete begin the night with sherry and bitter drink champagne steadily up to dessert then raw rasp capri with all the strength of whisky take benedictine with his coffee four or five whisky and soda to improve his pool stroke beer and bone at half past two wind up with old brandy. consequently when he come out at half past three in the morning into fourteen degree of frost he be very angry with his horse for cough and try to leapfrog into the saddle. the horse break away and go to his stable. so strickland and i form a guard of dishonour to take fleete home. 
our road lay through the bazaar close to a little temple of hanuman the monkey god who be a lead divinity worthy of respect. all god have good point just a have all priest. personally i attach much importance to hanuman and be kind to his people the great gray ape of the hill. one never know when one may want a friend. 
there be a light in the temple and a we pass we could hear voice of men chant hymn. in a native temple the priest rise at all hour of the night to do honour to their god. before we could stop him fleete dash up the step pat two priest on the back and be gravely grind the ash of his cigar butt into the forehead of the red stone image of hanuman. strickland try to drag him out but he sit down and say solemnly. 
shee that. mark of the b beasht. i make it. ishn t it fine. 
in half a minute the temple be alive and noisy and strickland who know what come of pollute god say that thing might occur. he by virtue of his official position long residence in the country and weakness for go among the native be know to the priest and he felt unhappy. fleete sit on the grind and refuse to move. he say that good old hanuman make a very soft pillow. 
then without any warn a silver man come out of a recess behind the image of the god. he be perfectly naked in that bitter bitter cold and his body shine like frost silver for he be what the bible call a leper a white a snow. also he have no face because he be a leper of some year stand and his disease be heavy upon him. we two stoop to haul fleete up and the temple be fill and fill with folk who seem to spring from the earth when the silver man run in under our arm make a noise exactly like the mew of an otter catch fleete round the body and drop his head on fleete s breast before we could wrench him away. then he retire to a corner and sit mew while the crowd block all the door. 
the priest be very angry until the silver man touch fleete. that nuzzle seem to sober them. 
at the end of a few minute silence one of the priest come to strickland and say in perfect english take your friend away. he ha do with hanuman but hanurnan ha not do with him. the crowd give room and we carry fleete into the road. 
strickland be very angry. he say that we might all three have be knife and that fleete should thank his star that he have escape without injury. 
fleete thank no one. he say that he want to go to bed. he be gorgeously drink. 
we move on strickland silent and wrathful until fleete be take with violent shiver fit and sweat. he say that the smell of the bazaar be overpower and he wonder why slaughter house be permit so near english residence. can t you smell the blood. say fleete. 
we put him to bed at last just a the dawn be break and strickland invite me to have another whisky and soda. while we be drink he talk of the trouble in the temple and admit that it baffle him completely. strickland hate be mystify by native because his business in life be to overmatch them with their own weapon. he ha not yet succeed in do this but in fifteen or twenty year he will have make some small progress. 
they should have maul u he say instead of mew at u. i wonder what they mean. i don t like it one little bite. 
i say that the manage committee of the temple would in all probability bring a criminal action against u for insult their religion. there be a section of the indian penal code which exactly meet fleete s offence. strickland say he only hop and pray that they would do this. before i leave i look into fleete s room and saw him lie on his right side scratch his leave breast. then. i go to bed cold depress and unhappy at seven o clock in the morning. 
at one o clock i ride over to strickland s house to inquire after fleete s head. i imagine that it would be a sore one. fleete be breakfast and seem unwell. his temper be go for he be abuse the cook for not supply him with an underdone chop. a man who can eat raw meat after a wet night be a curiosity. i tell fleete this and he laugh. 
you breed queer mosquito in these part he say. i ve be bite to piece but only in one place. 
let s have a look at the bite say strickland. it may have go down since this morning. 
while the chop be be cook fleete open his shirt and show u just over his leave breast a mark the perfect double of the black rosette the five or six irregular blotch arrange in a circle on a leopard s hide. strickland look and say it be only pink this morning. it s grow black now. 
fleete run to a glass. 
by jove. he say this be nasty. what be it. 
we could not answer. here the chop come in all red and juicy and fleete bolt three in a most offensive manner. he eat on his right grinder only and throw his head over his right shoulder a he snap the meat. when he have finish it strike him that he have be behave strangely for he say apologetically i don t think i ever felt so hungry in my life. i ve bolt like an ostrich. 
after breakfast strickland say to me don t go. stay here and stay for the night. 
see that my house be not three mile from strickland s this request be absurd. but strickland insist and be go to say something when fleete interrupt by declare in a shamefaced way that he felt hungry again. strickland send a man to my house to fetch over my bed and a horse and we three go down to strickland s stable to pas the hour until it be time to go out for a ride. the man who ha a weakness for horse never weary of inspect them. and when two men be kill time in this way they gather knowledge and lie the one from the other. 
there be five horse in the stable and i shall never forget the scene a we try to look them over. they seem to have go mad. they rear and scream and nearly tear up their picket. they sweat and shiver and lather and be distraught with fear. strickland s horse use to know him a well a his dog. which make the matter more curious. we leave the stable for fear of the brute throw themselves in their panic. then strickland turn back and call me. the horse be still frighten but they let u gentle and make much of them and put their head in our bosom. 
they aren t afraid of u say strickland. d you know i d give three month pay if outrage here could talk. 
but outrage be dumb and could only cuddle up to his master and blow out his nostril a be the custom of horse when they wish to explain thing but can t. fleete come up when we be in the stall and a soon a the horse saw him their fright break out afresh. it be all that we could do to escape from the place unkicked. strickland say they don t seem to love you fleete. 
nonsense say fleete. my mare will follow me like a dog. he go to her. she be in a loose box. but a he slip the bar she plunge knock him down and break away into the garden. i laugh but strickland be not amuse. he take his moustache in both fist and pull at it till it nearly come out. fleete instead of go off to chase his property yawn say that he felt sleepy. he go to the house to lie down which be a foolish way of spend new year s day. 
strickland sit with me in the stable and ask if i have notice anything peculiar in fleete s manner. i say that he eat his food like a beast. but that this might have be the result of live alone in the hill out of the reach of society a refine and elevate a ours for instance. strickland be not amuse. i do not think that he listen to me for his next sentence refer to the mark on fleete s breast and i say that it might have be cause by blister fly or that it be possibly a birth mark newly bear and now visible for the first time. we both agree that it be unpleasant to look at and strickland find occasion to say that i be a fool. 
i can t tell you what i think now say he because you would call me a madman. but you must stay with me for the next few day if you can. i want you to watch fleete but don t tell me what you think till i have make up my mind. 
but i be din out to night i say. so be i say strickland and so be fleete. at least if he doesn t change his mind. 
we walk about the garden smoke but say nothing because we be friend and talk spoil good tobacco till our pipe be out. then we go to wake up fleete. he be wide awake and fidget about his room. 
i say i want some more chop he say. can i get them. 
we laugh and say go and change. the pony will be round in a minute. 
all right say fleete. i ll go when i get the chop underdone one mind. 
he seem to be quite in earnest. it be four o clock and we have have breakfast at one. still for a long time he demand those underdone chop. then he change into rid clothe and go out into the verandah. his pony the mare have not be catch would not let him come near. all three horse be unmanageable mad with fear and finally fleete say that he would stay at home and get something to eat. strickland and i ride out wonder. a we pass the temple of hanuman the silver man come out and mew at u. 
he be not one of the regular priest of the temple say strickland. i think i should peculiarly like to lay my hand on him. 
there be no spring in our gallop on the racecourse that even. the horse be stale and move a though they have be ride out. 
the fright after breakfast ha be too much for them say strickland. 
that be the only remark he make through the remainder of the ride. once or twice i think he swear to himself. but that do not count. 
we come back in the dark at seven o clock and saw that there be no light in the bungalow. careless ruffian my servant be. say strickland. 
my horse rear at something on the carriage drive and fleete stand up under it nose. 
what be you do grovel about the garden. say strickland. 
but both horse bolt and nearly throw u. we dismount by the stable and return to fleete who be on his hand and knee under the orange bush. 
what the devil s wrong with you. say strickland. 
nothing nothing in the world say fleete speak very quickly and thickly. i ve be garden botanise you know. the smell of the earth be delightful. i think i m go for a walk a long walk all night. 
then i saw that there be something excessively out of order somewhere and i say to strickland i be not din out. 
bless you. say strickland. here fleete get up. you ll catch fever there. come in to dinner and let s have the lamp light. we ll all dine at home. 
fleete stand up unwillingly and say no lamp no lamp. it s much nice here. let s dine outside and have some more chop lot of em and underdone bloody one with gristle. 
now a december even in northern india be bitterly cold and fleete s suggestion be that of a maniac. 
come in say strickland sternly. come in at once. 
fleete come and when the lamp be bring we saw that he be literally plaster with dirt from head to foot. he must have be roll in the garden. he shrink from the light and go to his room. his eye be horrible to look at. there be a green light behind them not in them if you understand and the man s low lip hang down. 
strickland say there be go to be trouble big trouble to night. don t you change your rid thing. 
we wait and wait for fleete s reappearance and order dinner in the meantime. we could hear him move about his own room but there be no light there. presently from the room come the long draw howl of a wolf. 
people write and talk lightly of blood run cold and hair stand up and thing of that kind. both sensation be too horrible to be trifle with. my heart stop a though a knife have be drive through it and strickland turn a white a the tablecloth. 
the howl be repeat and be answer by another howl far across the field. 
that set the gild roof on the horror. strickland dash into fleete s room. i follow and we saw fleete get out of the window. he make beast noise in the back of his throat. he could not answer u when we shout at him. he spat. 
i don t quite remember what follow but i think that strickland must have stun him with the long boot jack or else i should never have be able to sit on his chest. fleete could not speak he could only snarl and his snarl be those of a wolf not of a man. the human spirit must have be give way all day and have die out with the twilight. we be deal with a beast that have once be fleete. 
the affair be beyond any human and rational experience. i try to say hydrophobia but the word wouldn t come because i know that i be lie. 
we bind this beast with leather thong of the punkah rope and tie it thumb and big toe together and gag it with a shoe horn which make a very efficient gag if you know how to arrange it. then we carry it into the din room and send a man to dumoise the doctor tell him to come over at once. after we have despatch the messenger and be draw breath strickland say it s no good. this isn t any doctor s work. i also know that he speak the truth. 
the beast s head be free and it throw it about from side to side. any one enter the room would have believe that we be cure a wolf s pelt. that be the most loathsome accessory of all. 
strickland sit with his chin in the heel of his fist watch the beast a it wriggle on the grind but say nothing. the shirt have be tear open in the scuffle and show the black rosette mark on the leave breast. it stand out like a blister. 
in the silence of the watch we hear something without mew like a she otter. we both rise to our foot and i answer for myself not strickland felt sick actually and physically sick. we tell each other a do the men in pinafore that it be the cat. 
dumoise arrive and i never saw a little man so unprofessionally shock. he say that it be a heart rend case of hydrophobia and that nothing could be do. at least any palliative measure would only prolong the agony. the beast be foam at the mouth. fleete a we tell dumoise have be bite by dog once or twice. any man who keep half a dozen terrier must expect a nip now and again. dumoise could offer no help. he could only certify that fleete be die of hydrophobia. the beast be then howl for it have manage to spit out the shoe horn. dumoise say that he would be ready to certify to the cause of death and that the end be certain. he be a good little man and he offer to remain with u. but strickland refuse the kindness. he do not wish to poison dumoise s new year. he would only ask him not to give the real cause of fleete s death to the public. 
so dumoise leave deeply agitate. and a soon a the noise of the cart wheel have die away strickland tell me in a whisper his suspicion. they be so wildly improbable that he dare not say them out aloud. and i who entertain all strickland s belief be so ashamed of own to them that i pretend to disbelieve. 
even if the silver man have bewtiched fleete for pollute the image of hanuman the punishment could not have fall so quickly. 
a i be whisper this the cry outside the house rise again and the beast fell into a fresh paroxysm of struggle till we be afraid that the thong that hold it would give way. 
watch. say strickland. if this happen six time i shall take the law into my own hand. i order you to help me. 
he go into his room and come out in a few minute with the barrel of an old shoot gun a piece of fish line some thick cord and his heavy wooden bedstead. i report that the convulsion have follow the cry by two second in each case and the beast seem perceptibly weak. 
strickland mutter but he can t take away the life. he can t take away the life. 
i say though i know that i be argue against myself it may be a cat. it must be a cat. if the silver man be responsible why doe he dare to come here. 
strickland arrange the wood on the hearth put the gun barrel into the glow of the fire spread the twine on the table and break a walk stick in two. there be one yard of fish line gut lap with wire such a be use for mahseer fish and he tie the two end together in a loop. 
then he say how can we catch him. he must be take alive and unhurt. 
i say that we must trust in providence and go out softly with polo stick into the shrubbery at the front of the house. the man or animal that make the cry be evidently move round the house a regularly a a night watchman. we could wait in the bush till he come by and knock him over. 
strickland accept this suggestion and we slip out from a bath room window into the front verandah and then across the carriage drive into the bush. 
in the moonlight we could see the leper come round the corner of the house. he be perfectly naked and from time to time he mew and stop to dance with his shadow. it be an unattractive sight and think of poor fleete bring to such degradation by so foul a creature i put away all my doubt and resolve to help strickland from the heat gun barrel to the loop of twine from the loin to the head and back again with all torture that might be needful. 
the leper halt in the front porch for a moment and we jump out on him with the stick. he be wonderfully strong and we be afraid that he might escape or be fatally injure before we catch him. we have an idea that leper be frail creature but this prove to be incorrect. strickland knock his leg from under him and i put my foot on his neck. he mew hideously and even through my rid boot i could feel that his flesh be not the flesh of a clean man. 
he strike at u with his hand and foot stump. we loop the lash of a dog whip round him under the armpit and drag him backwards into the hall and so into the din room where the beast lay. there we tie him with trunk strap. he make no attempt to escape but mew. 
when we confront him with the beast the scene be beyond description. the beast double backwards into a bow a though he have be poison with strychnine and moan in the most pitiable fashion. several other thing happen also but they cannot be put down here. 
i think i be right say strickland. now we will ask him to cure this case. 
but the leper only mew. strickland wrap a towel round his hand and take the gun barrel out of the fire. i put the half of the break walk stick through the loop of fish line and buckle the leper comfortably to strickland s bedstead. i understand then how men and woman and little child can endure to see a witch burn alive. for the beast be moan on the floor and though the silver man have no face you could see horrible feeling pass through the slab that take it place exactly a wave of heat play across red hot iron gun barrel for instance. 
strickland shade his eye with his hand for a moment and we get to work. this part be not to be print. 
the dawn be begin to break when the leper speak. his mew have not be satisfactory up to that point. the beast have faint from exhaustion and the house be very still. we unstrapped the leper and tell him to take away the evil spirit. he crawl to the beast and lay his hand upon the leave breast. that be all. then he fell face down and whine draw in his breath a he do so. 
we watch the face of the beast and saw the soul of fleete come back into the eye. then a sweat break out on the forehead and the eye they be human eye close. we wait for an hour but fleete still sleep. we carry him to his room and bid the leper go give him the bedstead and the sheet on the bedstead to cover his nakedness the glove and the towel with which we have touch him and the whip that have be hook round his body. he put the sheet about him and go out into the early morning without speak or mew. 
strickland wipe his face and sit down. a night gong far away in the city make seven o clock. 
exactly four and twenty hour. say strickland. and i ve do enough to ensure my dismissal from the service besides permanent quarter in a lunatic asylum. do you believe that we be awake. 
the red hot gun barrel have fall on the floor and be singe the carpet. the smell be entirely real. 
that morning at eleven we two together go to wake up fleete. we look and saw that the black leopard rosette on his chest have disappear. he be very drowsy and tire but a soon a he saw u he say oh. confound you fellow. happy new year to you. never mix your liquor. i m nearly dead. 
thank for your kindness but you re over time say strickland. to day be the morning of the second. you ve sleep the clock round with a vengeance. 
the door open and little dumoise put his head in. he have come on foot and fancy that we be lave out fleete. 
i ve bring a nurse say dumoise. i suppose that she can come in for. what be necessary. 
by all mean say fleete cheerily sit up in bed. bring on your nurse. 
dumoise be dumb. strickland lead him out and explain that there must have be a mistake in the diagnosis. dumoise remain dumb and leave the house hastily. he consider that his professional reputation have be injure and be incline to make a personal matter of the recovery. strickland go out too. when he come back he say that he have be to call on the temple of hanuman to offer redress for the pollution of the god and have be solemnly assure that no white man have ever touch the idol and that he be an incarnation of all the virtue labour under a delusion. 
what do you think. say strickland. 
i say there be more thing. 
but strickland hate that quotation. he say that i have wear it threadbare. 
one other curious thing happen which frighten me a much a anything in all the night s work. when fleete be dress he come into the din room and sniff. he have a quaint trick of move his nose when he sniff. horrid doggy smell here say he. you should really keep those terrier of yours in good order. try sulphur strick. 
but strickland do not answer. he catch hold of the back of a chair and without warn go into an amaze fit of hysteric. it be terrible to see a strong man overtake with hysteria. then it strike me that we have fight for fleete s soul with the silver man in that room and have disgrace ourselves a englishman for ever and i laugh and gasp and gurgle just a shamefully a strickland while fleete think that we have both go mad. we never tell him what we have do. 
some year late when strickland have marry and be a church go member of society for his wife s sake we review the incident dispassionately and strickland suggest that i should put it before the public. 
i cannot myself see that this step be likely to clear up the mystery. because in the first place no one will believe a rather unpleasant story and in the second it be well know to every right mind man that the god of the heathen be stone and brass and any attempt to deal with them otherwise be justly condemn. 
the return of imray. 
the door be wide the story saith out of the night come the patient wraith he might not speak and he could not stir a hair of the baron s minniver speechless and strengthless a shadow thin he rove the castle to seek his kin. and oh twas a piteous thing to see the dumb ghost follow his enemy. the baron. 
imray achieve the impossible. without warn for no conceivable motive in his youth at the threshold of his career he choose to disappear from the world which be to say the little indian station where he live. 
upon a day he be alive well happy and in great evidence among the billiard table at his club. upon a morning he be not and no manner of search could make sure where he might be. he have step out of his place. he have not appear at his office at the proper time and his dogcart be not upon the public road. for these reason and because he be hamper in a microscopical degree the administration of the indian empire that empire pause for one microscopical moment to make inquiry into the fate of imray. pond be drag well be plumb telegram be despatch down the line of railway and to the near seaport town twelve hundred mile away. but imray be not at the end of the drag rope nor the telegraph wire. he be go and his place know him no more. 
then the work of the great indian empire sweep forward because it could not be delay and imray from be a man become a mystery such a thing a men talk over at their table in the club for a month and then forget utterly. his gun horse and cart be sell to the high bidder. his superior officer write an altogether absurd letter to his mother say that imray have unaccountably disappear and his bungalow stand empty. 
after three or four month of the scorch hot weather have go by my friend strickland of the police saw fit to rent the bungalow from the native landlord. this be before he be engage to miss youghal an affair which ha be describe in another place and while he be pursue his investigation into native life. his own life be sufficiently peculiar and men complain of his manner and custom. there be always food in his house but there be no regular time for meal. he eat stand up and walk about whatever he might find at the sideboard and this be not good for human being. his domestic equipment be limit to six rifle three shoot gun five saddle and a collection of stiff joint mahseer rod big and strong than the large salmon rod. these occupy one half of his bungalow and the other half be give up to strickland and his dog tietjens an enormous rampur slut who devour daily the ration of two men. she speak to strickland in a language of her own. and whenever walk abroad she saw thing calculate to destroy the peace of her majesty the queen empress she return to her master and lay information. strickland would take step at once and the end of his labour be trouble and fine and imprisonment for other people. the native believe that tietjens be a familiar spirit and treat her with the great reverence that be bear of hate and fear. one room in the bungalow be set apart for her special use. she own a bedstead a blanket and a drink trough and if any one come into strickland s room at night her custom be to knock down the invader and give tongue till some one come with a light. strickland owe his life to her when he be on the frontier in search of a local murderer who come in the gray dawn to send strickland much farther than the andaman island. tietjens catch the man a he be crawl into strickland s tent with a dagger between his teeth. and after his record of iniquity be establish in the eye of the law he be hang. from that date tietjens wear a collar of rough silver and employ a monogram on her night blanket. and the blanket be of double weave kashmir cloth for she be a delicate dog. 
under no circumstance would she be separate from strickland. and once when he be ill with fever make great trouble for the doctor because she do not know how to help her master and would not allow another creature to attempt aid. macarnaght of the indian medical service beat her over her head with a gun butt before she could understand that she must give room for those who could give quinine. 
a short time after strickland have take imray s bungalow my business take me through that station and naturally the club quarter be full i quarter myself upon strickland. it be a desirable bungalow eight room and heavily thatch against any chance of leakage from rain. under the pitch of the roof run a ceiling cloth which look just a neat a a white wash ceiling. the landlord have repaint it when strickland take the bungalow. unless you know how indian bungalow be build you would never have suspect that above the cloth lay the dark three corner cavern of the roof where the beam and the underside of the thatch harbour all manner of rat bat ant and foul thing. 
tietjens meet me in the verandah with a bay like the boom of the bell of st. paul s put her paw on my shoulder to show she be glad to see me. strickland have contrive to claw together a sort of meal which he call lunch and immediately after it be finish go out about his business. i be leave alone with tietjens and my own affair. the heat of the summer have break up and turn to the warm damp of the rain. there be no motion in the heat air but the rain fell like ramrod on the earth and fling up a blue mist when it splash back. the bamboo and the custard apple the poinsettia and the mango tree in the garden stand still while the warm water lash through them and the frog begin to sing among the aloe hedge. a little before the light fail and when the rain be at it bad i sit in the back verandah and hear the water roar from the eaves and scratch myself because i be cover with the thing call prickly heat. tietjens come out with me and put her head in my lap and be very sorrowful. so i give her biscuit when tea be ready and i take tea in the back verandah on account of the little coolness find there. the room of the house be dark behind me. i could smell strickland s saddlery and the oil on his gun and i have no desire to sit among these thing. my own servant come to me in the twilight the muslin of his clothe cling tightly to his drench body and tell me that a gentleman have call and wish to see some one. very much against my will but only because of the darkness of the room i go into the naked draw room tell my man to bring the light. there might or might not have be a caller wait it seem to me that i saw a figure by one of the window but when the light come there be nothing save the spike of the rain without and the smell of the drink earth in my nostril. i explain to my servant that he be no wise than he ought to be and go back to the verandah to talk to tietjens. she have go out into the wet and i could hardly coax her back to me. even with biscuit with sugar top. strickland come home drip wet just before dinner and the first thing he say be. 
ha any one call. 
i explain with apology that my servant have summon me into the draw room on a false alarm. or that some loafer have try to call on strickland and think good of it have flee after give his name. strickiand order dinner without comment and since it be a real dinner with a white tablecloth attach we sit down. 
at nine o clock strickland want to go to bed and i be tire too. tietjens who have be lie underneath the table rise up and swing into the least expose verandah a soon a her master move to his own room which be next to the stately chamber set apart for tietjens. if a mere wife have wish to sleep out of door in that pelt rain it would not have matter. but tietjens be a dog and therefore the good animal. i look at strickland expect to see him flay her with a whip. he smile queerly a a man would smile after tell some unpleasant domestic tragedy. she ha do this ever since i move in here say he. let her go. 
the dog be strickland s dog so i say nothing but i felt all that strickland felt in be thus make light of. tietjens encamp outside my bedroom window and storm after storm come up thunder on the thatch and die away. the lightning spatter the sky a a throw egg spatter a barn door but the light be pale blue not yellow. and look through my split bamboo blind i could see the great dog stand not sleep in the verandah the hackle alift on her back and her foot anchor a tensely a the draw wire rope of a suspension bridge. in the very short pause of the thunder i try to sleep but it seem that some one want me very urgently. he whoever he be be try to call me by name but his voice be no more than a husky whisper. the thunder cease and tietjens go into the garden and howl at the low moon. somebody try to open my door walk about and about through the house and stand breathe heavily in the verandah and just when i be fall asleep i fancy that i hear a wild hammer and clamour above my head or on the door. 
i run into strickland s room and ask him whether he be ill and have be call for me. he be lie on his bed half dress a pipe in his mouth. i think you d come he say. have i be walk round the house recently. 
i explain that he have be tramp in the din room and the smoke room and two or three other place and he laugh and tell me to go back to bed. i go back to bed and sleep till the morning but through all my mix dream i be sure i be do some one an injustice in not attend to his want. what those want be i could not tell. but a flutter whisper bolt fumble lurk loiter someone be reproach me for my slackness and half awake i hear the howl of tietjens in the garden and the thresh of the rain. 
i live in that house for two day. strickland go to his office daily leave me alone for eight or ten hour with tietjens for my only companion. a long a the full light last i be comfortable and so be tietjens. but in the twilight she and i move into the back verandah and cuddle each other for company. we be alone in the house but none the le it be much too fully occupy by a tenant with whom i do not wish to interfere. i never saw him but i could see the curtain between the room quiver where he have just pass through. i could hear the chair creak a the bamboo spring under a weight that have just quit them. and i could feel when i go to get a book from the din room that somebody be wait in the shadow of the front verandah till i should have go away. tietjens make the twilight more interest by glare into the darken room with every hair erect and follow the motion of something that i could not see. she never enter the room but her eye move interestedly. that be quite sufficient. only when my servant come to trim the lamp and make all light and habitable she would come in with me and spend her time sit on her haunch watch an invisible extra man a he move about behind my shoulder. dog be cheerful companion. 
i explain to strickland gently a might be that i would go over to the club and find for myself quarter there. i admire his hospitality be please with his gun and rod but i do not much care for his house and it atmosphere. he hear me out to the end and then smile very wearily but without contempt for he be a man who understand thing. stay on he say and see what this thing mean. all you have talk about i have know since i take the bungalow. stay on and wait. tietjens ha leave me. be you go too. 
i have see him through one little affair connect with a heathen idol that have bring me to the door of a lunatic asylum and i have no desire to help him through further experience. he be a man to whom unpleasantness arrive a do dinner to ordinary people. 
therefore i explain more clearly than ever that i like him immensely and would be happy to see him in the daytime. but that i do not care to sleep under his roof. this be after dinner when tietjens have go out to lie in the verandah. 
pon my soul i don t wonder say strickland with his eye on the ceiling cloth. look at that. 
the tail of two brown snake be hang between the cloth and the cornice of the wall. they throw long shadow in the lamplight. 
if you be afraid of snake of course say strickland. 
i hate and fear snake because if you look into the eye of any snake you will see that it know all and more of the mystery of man s fall and that it feel all the contempt that the devil felt when adam be evict from eden. besides which it bite be generally fatal and it twist up trouser leg. 
you ought to get your thatch overhaul i say. 
give me a mahseer rod and we ll poke em down. 
they ll hide among the roof beam say strickland. i can t stand snake overhead. i m go up into the roof. if i shake em down stand by with a clean rod and break their back. 
i be not anxious to assist strickland in his work but i take the clean rod and wait in the din room while strickland bring a gardener s ladder from the verandah and set it against the side of the room. 
the snake tail draw themselves up and disappear. we could hear the dry rush scuttle of long body run over the baggy ceiling cloth. strickland take a lamp with him while i try to make clear to him the danger of hunt roof snake between a ceiling cloth and a thatch apart from the deterioration of property cause by rip out ceiling cloth. 
nonsense. say strickland. they re sure to hide near the wall by the cloth. the brick be too cold for em and the heat of the room be just what they like. he put his hand to the corner of the stuff and rip it from the cornice. it give with a great sound of tear and strickland put his head through the open into the dark of the angle of the roof beam. i set my teeth and lift the rod for i have not the least knowledge of what might descend. 
h m. say strickland and his voice roll and rumble in the roof. there s room for another set of room up here and by jove some one be occupy em. 
snake. i say from below. 
no. it s a buffalo. hand me up the two last joint of a mahseer rod and i ll prod it. it s lie on the main roof beam. 
i hand up the rod. 
what a nest for owl and serpent. no wonder the snake live here say strickland climb farther into the roof. i could see his elbow thrust with the rod. come out of that whoever you be. head below there. it s fall. 
i saw the ceiling cloth nearly in the centre of the room bag with a shape that be press it downwards and downwards towards the light lamp on the table. i snatch the lamp out of danger and stand back. then the cloth rip out from the wall tear split sway and shoot down upon the table something that i dare not look at till strickland have slide down the ladder and be stand by my side. 
he do not say much be a man of few word. but he pick up the loose end of the tablecloth and throw it over the remnant on the table. 
it strike me say he put down the lamp our friend imray ha come back. oh. you would would you. 
there be a movement under the cloth and a little snake wriggle out to be back break by the butt of the mahseer rod. i be sufficiently sick to make no remark worth record. 
strickland meditate and help himself to drink. the arrangement under the cloth make no more sign of life. 
be it imray. i say. 
strickland turn back the cloth for a moment and look. 
it be imray he say. and his throat be cut from ear to ear. 
then we speak both together and to ourselves. that s why he whisper about the house. 
tietjens in the garden begin to bay furiously. a little late her great nose heave open the din room door. 
she sniff and be still. the tattered ceiling cloth hang down almost to the level of the table and there be hardly room to move away from the discovery. 
tietjens come in and sit down. her teeth bar under her lip and her forepaw plant. she look at strickland. 
it s a bad business old lady say he. men don t climb up into the roof of their bungalow to die and they don t fasten up the ceiling cloth behind em. let s think it out. 
let s think it out somewhere else i say. 
excellent idea. turn the lamp out. we ll get into my room. 
i do not turn the lamp out. i go into strickland s room first and allow him to make the darkness. then he follow me and we light tobacco and think. strickland think. i smoke furiously because i be afraid. 
imray be back say strickland. the question be who kill imray. don t talk i ve a notion of my own. when i take this bungalow i take over most of imray s servant. imray be guileless and inoffensive wasn t he. 
i agree. though the heap under the cloth have look neither one thing nor the other. 
if i call in all the servant they will stand fast in a crowd and lie like aryan. what do you suggest. 
call em in one by one i say. 
they ll run away and give the news to all their fellow say strickland. we must segregate em. do you suppose your servant know anything about it. 
he may for aught i know. but i don t think it s likely. he ha only be here two or three day i answer. what s your notion. 
i can t quite tell. how the dickens do the man get the wrong side of the ceiling cloth. 
there be a heavy cough outside strickland s bedroom door. this show that bahadur khan his body servant have wake from sleep and wish to put strickland to bed. 
come in say strickland. it s a very warm night isn t it. 
bahadur khan a great green turbaned six foot mahomedan say that it be a very warm night. but that there be more rain pending which by his honour s favour would bring relief to the country. 
it will be so if god plea say strickland tug off his boot. it be in my mind bahadur khan that i have work thee remorselessly for many day ever since that time when thou first earnest into my service. what time be that. 
ha the heaven bear forget. it be when imray sahib go secretly to europe without warn give. and i even i come into the honour service of the protector of the poor. 
and imray sahib go to europe. 
it be so say among those who be his servant. 
and thou wilt take service with him when he return. 
assuredly sahib. he be a good master and cherish his dependant. 
that be true. i be very tire but i go buck shoot to morrow. give me the little sharp rifle that i use for black buck. it be in the case yonder. 
the man stoop over the case. hand barrel stock and fore end to strickland who fit all together yawn dolefully. then he reach down to the gun case take a solid draw cartridge and slip it into the breech of the express. 
and imray sahib ha go to europe secretly. that be very strange bahadur khan be it not. 
what do i know of the way of the white man. heaven bear. 
very little truly. but thou shalt know more anon. it ha reach me that imray sahib ha return from his so long journeying and that even now he lie in the next room wait his servant. 
sahib. 
the lamplight slide along the barrel of the rifle a they level themselves at bahadur khan s broad breast.

the man pick up a lamp and go into the din room strickland follow and almost push him with the muzzle of the rifle. he look for a moment at the black depth behind the ceiling cloth. at the writhe snake under foot. and last a gray glaze settle on his face at the thing under the tablecloth. 
hast thou see. say strickland after a pause. 
i have see. i be clay in the white man s hand. what doe the presence do. 
hang thee within the month. what else. 
for kill him. nay sahib consider. walk among u his servant he cast his eye upon my child who be four year old. him he bewitch and in ten day he die of the fever my child. 
what say imray sahib. 
he say he be a handsome child and pat him on the head. wherefore my child die. wherefore i kill imray sahib in the twilight when he have come back from office and be sleep. wherefore i drag him up into the roof beam and make all fast behind him. the heaven bear know all thing. i be the servant of the heaven bear. 
strickland look at me above the rifle and say in the vernacular thou art witness to this say. he ha kill. 
bahadur khan stand ashen gray in the light of the one lamp. the need for justification come upon him very swiftly. i be trap he say but the offence be that man s. he cast an evil eye upon my child and i kill and hide him. only such a be serve by devil he glare at tietjens couch stolidly before him only such could know what i do. 
it be clever. but thou shouldst have lash him to the beam with a rope. now thou thyself wilt hang by a rope. orderly. 
a drowsy policeman answer strickland s call. he be follow by another and tietjens sit wondrous still.

do i hang then. say bahadur khan make no attempt to escape and keep his eye on the grind. 
if the sun shine or the water run yes. say strickland.

go. say strickland. 
nay. but i go very swiftly say bahadur khan. look. i be even now a dead man. 
he lift his foot and to the little toe there cling the head of the half kill snake firm fix in the agony of death. 
i come of land hold stock say bahadur khan rock where he stand. it be a disgrace to me to go to the public scaffold. therefore i take this way. be it remember that the sahib s shirt be correctly enumerate and that there be an extra piece of soap in his washbasin. my child be bewitch and i slew the wizard. why should you seek to slay me with the rope. my honour be save and and i die. 
at the end of an hour he die a they die who be bite by the little brown karait and the policeman bore him and the thing under the tablecloth to their appoint place. all be need to make clear the disappearance of imray. 
this say strickland very calmly a he climb into bed be call the nineteenth century. do you hear what that man say. 
i hear i answer. imray make a mistake. 
simply and solely through not know the nature of the oriental and the coincidence of a little seasonal fever. bahadur khan have be with him for four year. 
i shudder. my own servant have be with me for exactly that length of time. when i go over to my own room i find my man wait impassive a the copper head on a penny to pull off my boot. 
what ha befall bahadur khan. say i. 
he be bite by a snake and die. the rest the sahib know be the answer. 
and how much of this matter hast thou know. 
a much a might be gather from one come in in the twilight to seek satisfaction. gently sahib. let me pull off those boot.
