tietjens ha come back to her place. 
and so she have. the great deerhound be couch statelily on her own bedstead on her own blanket while in the next room the idle empty ceiling cloth waggle a it trail on the table. 
namgay doola. 
there come to the beach a poor exile of erin the dew on his wet robe hang heavy and chill. ere the steamer that bring him have pass out of hearin he be alderman mike inthrojuicin a bill. american song. 
once upon a time there be a king who live on the road to thibet very many mile in the himalaya. his kingdom be eleven thousand foot above the sea and exactly four mile square. but most of the mile stand on end owe to the nature of the country. his revenue be rather le than four hundred pound yearly and they be expend in the maintenance of one elephant and a stand army of five men. he be tributary to the indian government who allow him certain sum for keep a section of the himalaya thibet road in repair. he further increase his revenue by sell timber to the railway company. for he would cut the great deodar tree in his one forest and they fell thunder into the sutlej river and be sweep down to the plain three hundred mile away and become railway tie. now and again this king whose name doe not matter would mount a ringstraked horse and ride score of mile to simla town to confer with the lieutenant governor on matter of state or to assure the viceroy that his sword be at the service of the queen empress. then the viceroy would cause a ruffle of drum to be sound and the ringstraked horse and the cavalry of the state two men in tatter and the herald who bore the silver stick before the king would trot back to their own place which lay between the tail of a heaven climb glacier and a dark birch forest. 
now from such a king always remember that he possess one veritable elephant and could count his descent for twelve hundred year i expect when it be my fate to wander through his dominion no more than mere license to live. 
the night have close in rain and roll cloud blot out the light of the village in the valley. forty mile away untouched by cloud or storm the white shoulder of donga pa the mountain of the council of the god uphold the even star. the monkey sing sorrowfully to each other a they hunt for dry roost in the fern wreathe tree and the last puff of the day wind bring from the unseen village the scent of damp wood smoke hot cake drip undergrowth and rot pine cone. that be the true smell of the himalaya and if once it creep into the blood of a man that man will at the last forget all else return to the hill to die. the cloud close and the smell go away and there remain nothing in all the world except chill white mist and the boom of the sutlej river race through the valley below. a fat tail sheep who do not want to die bleat piteously at my tent door. he be scuffle with the prime minister and the director general of public education and he be a royal gift to me and my camp servant. i express my thank suitably and ask if i might have audience of the king. the prime minister readjust his turban which have fall off in the struggle and assure me that the king would be very please to see me. therefore i despatch two bottle a a foretaste and when the sheep have enter upon another incarnation go to the king s palace through the wet. he have send his army to escort me but the army stay to talk with my cook. soldier be very much alike all the world over. 
the palace be a four room and whitewash mud and timber house the fine in all the hill for a day s journey. the king be dress in a purple velvet jacket white muslin trouser and a saffron yellow turban of price. he give me audience in a little carpet room open off the palace courtyard which be occupy by the elephant of state. the great beast be sheet and anchor from trunk to tail and the curve of his back stand out grandly against the mist. 
the prime minister and the director general of public education be present to introduce me but all the court have be dismiss l the two bottle aforesaid should corrupt their moral. the king cast a wreath of heavy scent flower round my neck a i bow and inquire how my honour presence have the felicity to be. i say that through see his auspicious countenance the mist of the night have turn into sunshine and that by reason of his beneficent sheep his good deed would be remember by the god. he say that since i have set my magnificent foot in his kingdom the crop would probably yield seventy per cent more than the average. i say that the fame of the king have reach to the four corner of the earth and that the nation gnash their teeth when they hear daily of the glory of his realm and the wisdom of his moon like prime minister and lotus like director general of public education. 
then we sit down on clean white cushion and i be at the king s right hand. three minute late he be tell me that the state of the maize crop be something disgraceful and that the railway company would not pay him enough for his timber. the talk shift to and fro with the bottle and we discuss very many stately thing and the king become confidential on the subject of government generally. most of all he dwell on the shortcoming of one of his subject who from all i could gather have be paralyze the executive. 
in the old day say the king i could have order the elephant yonder to trample him to death. now i must e en send him seventy mile across the hill to be try and his keep would be upon the state. the elephant eat everything. 
what be the man s crime rajah sahib. say i. 
firstly he be an outlander and no man of mine own people. secondly since of my favour i give him land upon his first come he refuse to pay revenue. be i not the lord of the earth above and below entitle by right and custom to one eighth of the crop. yet this devil establish himself refuse to pay a single tax. and he bring a poisonous spawn of babe. 
cast him into jail i say. 
sahib the king answer shift a little on the cushion once and only once in these forty year sickness come upon me so that i be not able to go abroad. in that hour i make a vow to my god that i would never again cut man or woman from the light of the sun and the air of god. for i perceive the nature of the punishment. how can i break my vow. be it only the lop of a hand or a foot i should not delay. but even that be impossible now that the english have rule. one or another of my people he look obliquely at the director general of public education would at once write a letter to the viceroy and perhaps i should be deprive of my ruffle of drum. 
he unscrew the mouthpiece of his silver water pipe fit a plain amber mouthpiece and pass his pipe to me. not content with refuse revenue he continue this outlander refuse also the begar. this be the corvee or force labour on the road. and stir my people up to the like treason. yet he be when he will an expert log snatcher. there be none good or bold among my people to clear a block of the river when the log stick fast. 
but he worship strange god say the prime minister deferentially. 
for that i have no concern say the king who be a tolerant a akbar in matter of belief. to each man his own god and the fire or mother earth for u all at last. it be the rebellion that offend me. 
the king ha an army i suggest. ha not the king burn the man s house and leave him naked to the night dew. 
nay a hut be a hut and it hold the life of a man. but once i send my army against him when his excuse become wearisome. of their head he brake three across the top with a stick. the other two men run away. also the gun would not shoot. 
i have see the equipment of the infantry. one third of it be an old muzzle load fowl piece with a rag rust hole where the nipple should have be one third a wire bind matchlock with a worm eat stock and one third a four bore flint duck gun without a flint. 
but it be to be remember say the king reach out for the bottle that he be a very expert log snatcher and a man of a merry face. what shall i do to him sahib. 
this be interest. the timid hill folk would a soon have refuse tax to their king a revenue to their god. 
if it be the king s permission i say i will not strike my tent till the third day and i will see this man. the mercy of the king be god like and rebellion be like unto the sin of witchcraft. moreover both the bottle and another be empty. 
you have my leave to go say the king. 
next morning a crier go through the state proclaim that there be a log jam on the river and that it behove all loyal subject to remove it. the people pour down from their village to the moist warm valley of poppy field. and the king and i go with them. hundred of dress deodar log have catch on a snag of rock and the river be bring down more log every minute to complete the blockade. the water snarl and wrench and worry at the timber and the population of the state begin prod the near log with a pole in the hope of start a general movement. then there go up a shout of namgay doola. namgay doola. and a large red haired villager hurry up strip off his clothe a he run. 
that be he. that be the rebel say the king. now will the dam be clear. 
but why ha he red hair. i ask since red hair among hill folk be a common a blue or green. 
he be an outlander say the king. well do. oh well do. 
namgay doola have scramble out on the jam and be claw out the butt of a log with a rude sort of boat hook. it slide forward slowly a an alligator move three or four others follow it and the green water spout through the gap they have make. then the villager howl and shout and scramble across the log pull and push the obstinate timber and the red head of namgay doola be chief among them all. the log sway and chafe and groan a fresh consignment from upstream batter the now weaken dam. all give way at last in a smother of foam race log bob black head and confusion indescribable. the river toss everything before it. i saw the red head go down with the last remnant of the jam and disappear between the great grind tree trunk. it rise close to the bank and blow like a grampus. namgay doola wring the water out of his eye and make obeisance to the king. i have time to observe him closely. the virulent redness of his shock head and beard be most startle. and in the thicket of hair wrinkle above high cheek bone shine two very merry blue eye. he be indeed an outlander but yet a thibetan in language habit and attire. he speak the lepcha dialect with an indescribable soften of the guttural. it be not so much a lisp a an accent. 
whence comest thou. i ask. 
from thibet. he point across the hill and grin. that grin go straight to my heart. mechanically i hold out my hand and namgay doola shake it. no pure thibetan would have understand the mean of the gesture. he go away to look for his clothe and a he climb back to his village i hear a joyous yell that seem unaccountably familiar. it be the whoop of namgay doola. 
you see now say the king why i would not kill him. he be a bold man among my log but and he shake his head like a schoolmaster i know that before long there will be complaint of him in the court. let u return to the palace and do justice. it be that king s custom to judge his subject every day between eleven and three o clock. i saw him decide equitably in weighty matter of trespass slander and a little wife steal. then his brow cloud and he summon me. 
again it be namgay doola he say despairingly. not content with refuse revenue on his own part he ha bind half his village by an oath to the like treason. never before ha such a thing befall me. nor be my tax heavy. 
a rabbit face villager with a blush rise stick behind his ear advance tremble. he have be in the conspiracy but have tell everything and hop for the king s favour. 
o king say i if it be the king s will let this matter stand over till the morning. only the god can do right swiftly and it may be that yonder villager ha lie. 
nay for i know the nature of namgay doola. but since a guest ask let the matter remain. wilt thou speak harshly to this red head outlander. he may listen to thee. 
i make an attempt that very even but for the life of me i could not keep my countenance. namgay doola grin persuasively and begin to tell me about a big brown bear in a poppy field by the river. would i care to shoot it. i speak austerely on the sin of conspiracy and the certainty of punishment. namgay doola s face cloud for a moment. shortly afterwards he withdraw from my tent and i hear him sing to himself softly among the pine. the word be unintelligible to me but the tune like his liquid insinuate speech seem the ghost of something strangely familiar. 
dir hane mard i yemen dir to weeree ala gee. 
sing namgay doola again and again and i rack my brain for that lose tune. it be not till after dinner that i discover some one have cut a square foot of velvet from the centre of my best camera cloth. this make me so angry that i wander down the valley in the hope of meet the big brown bear. i could hear him grunt like a discontent pig in the poppy field and i wait shoulder deep in the dew drip indian corn to catch him after his meal. the moon be at full and draw out the rich scent of the tasselled crop. then i hear the anguish bellow of a himalayan cow one of the little black crummies no big than newfoundland dog. two shadow that look like a bear and her cub hurry past me. i be in act to fire when i saw that they have each a brilliant red head. the less animal be trail some rope behind it that leave a dark track on the path. they pass within six foot of me and the shadow of the moonlight lay velvet black on their face. velvet black be exactly the word for by all the power of moonlight they be mask in the velvet of my camera cloth. i marvel and go to bed. 
next morning the kingdom be in uproar. namgay doola men say have go forth in the night and with a sharp knife have cut off the tail of a cow belong to the rabbit face villager who have betray him. it be sacrilege unspeakable against the holy cow. the state desire his blood but he have retreat into his hut barricade the door and window with big stone and defy the world. 
the king and i and the populace approach the hut cautiously. there be no hope of capture the man without loss of life for from a hole in the wall project the muzzle of an extremely well care for gun the only gun in the state that could shoot. namgay doola have narrowly miss a villager just before we come up. the stand army stand. it could do no more for when it advance piece of sharp shale fly from the window. to these be add from time to time shower of scald water. we saw red head bob up and down in the hut. the family of namgay doola be aid their sire and blood curdle yell of defiance be the only answer to our prayer. 
never say the king puff ha such a thing befall my state. next year i will certainly buy a little cannon. he look at me imploringly. 
be there any priest in the kingdom to whom he will listen. say i for a light be begin to break upon me. 
he worship his own god say the prime minister. we can starve him out. 
let the white man approach say namgay doola from within. all others i will kill. send me the white man. 
the door be throw open and i enter the smoky interior of a thibetan hut cram with child. and every child have flame red hair. a raw cow s tail lay on the floor and by it side two piece of black velvet my black velvet rudely hack into the semblance of mask. 
and what be this shame namgay doola. say i. 
he grin more winningly than ever. there be no shame say he. i do but cut off the tail of that man s cow. he betray me. i be mind to shoot him sahib. but not to death. indeed not to death. only in the leg. 
and why at all since it be the custom to pay revenue to the king. why at all. 
by the god of my father i cannot tell say namgay doola. 
and who be thy father. 
the same that have this gun. he show me his weapon a tower musket bear date and the stamp of the honourable east india company. 
and thy father s name. say i. 
timlay doola say he. at the first i be then a little child it be in my mind that he wear a red coat. 
of that i have no doubt. but repeat the name of thy father thrice or four time. 
he obey and i understand whence the puzzle accent in his speech come. thimla dhula say he excitedly. to this hour i worship his god. 
may i see that god. 
in a little while at twilight time. 
rememberest thou aught of thy father s speech. 
it be long ago. but there be one word which he say often. thus shun. then i and my brother stand upon our foot our hand to our side. thus. 
even so. and what be thy mother. 
a woman of the hill. we be lepchas of darjeeling but me they call an outlander because my hair be a thou seest. 
the thibetan woman his wife touch him on the arm gently. the long parley outside the fort have last far into the day. it be now close upon twilight the hour of the angelus. very solemnly the red head brat rise from the floor and form a semicircle. namgay doola lay his gun against the wall light a little oil lamp and set it before a recess in the wall. pull aside a curtain of dirty cloth he reveal a wear brass crucifix lean against the helmet badge of a long forget east india regiment. thus do my father he say cross himself clumsily. the wife and child follow suit. then all together they strike up the wail chant that i hear on the hillside. 
dir bane mard i yemen dir to weeree ala gee. 
i be puzzle no long. again and again they croon a if their heart would break their version of the chorus of the wear of the green. 
they re hang men and woman too for the wear of the green. 
a diabolical inspiration come to me. one of the brat a boy about eight year old be watch me a he sing. i pull out a rupee hold the coin between finger and thumb and look only look at the gun against the wall. a grin of brilliant and perfect comprehension overspread the face of the child. never for an instant stop the song he hold out his hand for the money and then slide the gun to my hand. i might have shoot namgay doola a he chant. but i be satisfy. the blood instinct of the race hold true. namgay doola draw the curtain across the recess. angelus be over. 
thus my father sing. there be much more but i have forget and i do not know the purport of these word but it may be that the god will understand. i be not of this people and i will not pay revenue. 
and why. 
again that soul compel grin. what occupation would be to me between crop and crop. it be good than scar bear. but these people do not understand. he pick the mask from the floor and look in my face a simply a a child. 
by what road didst thou attain knowledge to make these devilry. i say point. 
i cannot tell. i be but a lepcha of darjeeling and yet the stuff. 
which thou hast steal. 
nay surely. do i steal. i desire it so. the stuff the stuff what else should i have do with the stuff. he twist the velvet between his finger. 
but the sin of maim the cow consider that. 
that be true. but oh sahib that man betray me and i have no think but the heifer s tail wave in the moonlight and i have my knife. what else should i have do. the tail come off ere i be aware. sahib thou knowest more than i. 
that be true say i. stay within the door. i go to speak to the king. 
the population of the state be range on the hillside. i go forth and speak to the king. 
o king say i. touch this man there be two course open to thy wisdom. thou canst either hang him from a tree he and his brood till there remain no hair that be red within the land. 
nay say the king. why should i hurt the little child. 
they have pour out of the hut door and be make plump obeisance to everybody. namgay doola wait with his gun across his arm. 
or thou canst discard the impiety of the cow maim raise him to honour in thy army. he come of a race that will not pay revenue. a red flame be in his blood which come out at the top of his head in that glow hair. make him chief of the army. give him honour a may befall and full allowance of work but look to it o king that neither he nor his hold a foot of earth from thee henceforward. fee him with word and favour and also liquor from certain bottle that thou knowest of and he will be a bulwark of defence. but deny him even a tuft of grass for his own. this be the nature that god ha give him. moreover he ha brother. 
the state groan unanimously. 
but if his brother come they will surely fight with each other till they die. or else the one will always give information concern the other. shall he be of thy army o king. choose. 
the king bow his head and i say come forth namgay doola and command the king s army. thy name shall no more be namgay in the mouth of men but patsay doola for a thou hast say i know. 
then namgay doola new christen patsay doola son of timlay doola which be tim doolan go very wrong indeed clasp the king s foot cuff the stand army and hurry in an agony of contrition from temple to temple make offering for the sin of cattle maim. 
and the king be so please with my perspicacity that he offer to sell me a village for twenty pound sterling. but i buy no village in the himalaya so long a one red head flare between the tail of the heaven climb glacier and the dark birch forest. 
i know that breed. 
burtran and bimi. 
the orang outang in the big iron cage lash to the sheep pen begin the discussion. the night be stiflingly hot and a i and han breitmann the big beam german pass him drag our bed to the fore peak of the steamer he rouse himself and chatter obscenely. he have be catch somewhere in the malayan archipelago and be go to england to be exhibit at a shill a head. for four day he have struggle yell and wrench at the heavy bar of his prison without cease and have nearly slay a lascar incautious enough to come within reach of the great hairy paw. 
it would be well for you mine friend if you be a liddle seasick say han breitmann pause by the cage. you haf too much ego in your cosmos. 
the orang outang s arm slide out negligently from between the bar. no one would have believe that it would make a sudden snakelike rush at the german s breast. the thin silk of the sleep suit tear out. han step back unconcernedly to pluck a banana from a bunch hang close to one of the boat. 
too much ego say he peel the fruit and offer it to the cage devil who be rend the silk to tatter. 
then we lay out our bed in the bow among the sleep lascar to catch any breeze that the pace of the ship might give u. the sea be like smoky oil except where it turn to fire under our forefoot and whirl back into the dark in smear of dull flame. there be a thunderstorm some mile away. we could see the glimmer of the lightning. the ship s cow distress by the heat and the smell of the ape beast in the cage low unhappily from time to time in exactly the same key a that in which the look out man answer the hourly call from the bridge. the trample tune of the engine be very distinct and the jar of the ash lift a it be tip into the sea hurt the procession of hush noise. han lay down by my side and light a good night cigar. this be naturally the begin of conversation. he own a voice a soothe a the wash of the sea and store of experience a vast a the sea itself. for his business in life be to wander up and down the world collect orchid and wild beast and ethnological specimen for german and american dealer. i watch the glow end of his cigar wax and wane in the gloom a the sentence rise and fell till i be nearly asleep. the orang outang trouble by some dream of the forest of his freedom begin to yell like a soul in purgatory and to pluck madly at the bar of the cage. 
if he be out now dere would not be much of u leave hereabout say han lazily. he scream goot. see now how i shall tame him when he stop himself. 
there be a pause in the outcry and from han mouth come an imitation of a snake s hiss so perfect that i almost spring to my foot. the sustain murderous sound run along the deck and the wrench at the bar cease. the orang outang be quake in an ecstasy of pure terror. 
dot stop him say han. i learn dot trick in mogoung tanjong when i be collect liddle monkey for some people in berlin. efery one in d world be afraid of d monkey except d snake. so i blay snake against monkey and he keep quite still. dere be too much ego in his cosmos. dot be d soul custom of monkey. be you asleep or will you listen and i will tell a dale dot you shall not pelief. 
there s no tale in the wide world that i can t believe i say. 
if you haf learn pelief you haf learn somedings. now i shall try your pelief. goot. when i be collect dose liddle monkey it be in or und i be in d island of d archipelago over dere in d dark he point southward to new guinea generally mein gott. i would sooner collect life red devil than liddle monkey. when dey do not bite off your thumb dey be always die from nostalgia home sick for dey haf d imperfect soul which be midway arrest in defelopment und too much ego. i be dere for nearly a year und dere i find a man dot be call bertran. he be a frenchman und he be goot man naturalist to his bone. dey say he be an escape convict but he be naturalist und dot be enough for me. he would call all d life beast from d forest und dey would come. i say he be st. francis of assizi in a new dransmigration produce und he laugh und say he haf never preach to d fish. he sell dem for tripang beche de m. 
und dot man who be king of beast tame men he have in d house shust such anoder a dot devil animal in d cage a great orang outang dot think he be a man. he haf find him when he be a child d orang outang und he be child und brother und opera comique all round to betran. he have his room in dot house not a cage but a room mit a bed und sheet und he would go to bed und get up in d morning und smoke his cigar und eat his dinner mit bertran und walk mit him hand in hand which be most horrible. herr gott. i haf see dot beast throw himself back in his chair und laugh when bertran haf make fun of me. he be not a beast. he be a man und he talk to bertran und bertran comprehend for i have see dem. und he be always politeful to me except when i talk too long to bertran und say nod at all to him. den he would pull me away dis great dark devil mit his enormous paw shust a if i be a child. he be not a beast. he be a man. dis i saw pefore i know him three month und bertran he haf saw the same. and bimi d orang outang haf understand u both mit his cigar between his big dog teeth und d blue gum. 
i be dere a year dere und at dere oder island somedimes for monkey und somedimes for butterfly und orchits. one time bertran say to me dot he will be marry because he haf find a girl dot be goot und he enquire if this marry idee be right. i would not say pecause it be not me dot be go to be marry. den he go off court d girl she be a half caste french girl very pretty. haf you get a new light for my cigar. ouf. very pretty. only i say haf you think of bimi. if he pull me away when i talk to you what will he do to your wife. he will pull her in piece. if i be you bertran i would gif my wife for wed present d stuff figure of bimi. by dot time i have learn some ding about d monkey people. shoot him. say bertran. he be your beast i say. if he be mine he would be shoot now. 
den i felt at d back of my neck d finger of bimi. mein gott. i tell you dot he talk through dose finger. it be d deaf and dumb alphabet all gomplete. he slide his hairy arm round my neck und he tilt up my chin und look into my face shust to see if i understand his talk so well a he understand mine. 
see now dere. say bertran und you would shoot him while he be cuddlin you. dot be d teuton ingrate. 
but i know dot i have make bimi a life s enemy pecause his finger haf talk murder through the back of my neck. next dime i see bimi dere be a pistol in my belt und he touch it once und i open d breech to show him it be load. he haf see d liddle monkey kill in d wood. he understand. 
so bertran he be marry and he forget clean about bimi dot be skippin alone on d beach mit d half of a human soul in his belly. i be see him skip und he take a big bough und thrash d sand till he haf make a great hole like a grave. so i say to bertran for any sake kill bimi. he be mad mit d jealousy. 
bertran haf say he be not mad at all. he haf obey und lofe my wife und if she speak he will get her slipper und he look at his wife agross d room. she be a very pretty girl. 
den i say to him dost dou pretend to know monkey und dis beast dot be lash himself mad upon d sand pecause you do not talk to him. shoot him when he come to d house for he haf d light in his eye dot mean kill und kill. bimi come to d house but dere be no light in his eye. it be all put away cunning so cunning und he fetch d girl her slipper und bertran turn to me und say dost dou know him in nine month more dan i haf know him in twelve year. shall a child stab his fader. i haf feed him und he be my child. do not speak this nonsense to my wife or to me any more. 
dot next day bertran come to my house to help me make some wood case for d specimen und he tell me dot he haf leave his wife a liddle while mit bimi in d garden. den i finish my case quick und i say let u go to your house und get a trink. he laugh and say come along dry man. 
his wife be not in d garden und bimi do not come when bertran call. und his wife do not come when he call und he knock at her bedroom door und dot be shut tight lock. den he look at me und his face be white. i break down d door mit my shoulder und d thatch of d roof be tear into a great hole und d sun come in upon d floor. haf you ever see paper in d waste basket or card at whist on d table scatter. dere be no wife dot could be see. i tell you dere be nod in dot room dot might be a woman. dere be stuff on d floor und dot be all. i look at dese thing und i be very sick. but bertran look a liddle long at what be upon the floor und d wall und d hole in d thatch. den he pegan to laugh soft und low und i know und thank gott dot he be mad. he nefer cry he nefer pray. he stand all still in d doorway und laugh to himself. den he say she haf lock herself in dis room and he haf tear up d thatch. fi donc. dot be so. we will mend d thatch und wait for bimi. he will surely come. 
i tell you we wait ten day in dot house after d room be make into a room again und once or twice we saw bimi comin a liddle way from d wood. he be afraid pecause he haf do wrong. bertran call him when he be come to look on the tenth day und bimi come skip along d beach und make noise mit a long piece of black hair in his hand. den bertran laugh and say fi donc. shust a if it be a glass break upon d table. und bimi come near und bertran be honey sweet in his voice und laugh to himself. for three day he make love to bimi pecause bimi would not let himself be touch. den bimi come to dinner at d same table mit u und the hair on his hand be all black und thick mit mit what have dry on d hand. bertran give him sangaree till bimi be drink and stupid und den. 
han pause to puff at his cigar. 
and then. say i. 
und den bertran he kill him mit his hand und i go for a walk upon d beach. it be bertran s own piziness. when i come back d ape he be dead und bertran he be die abofe him. but still he laugh liddle und low und he be quite content. now you know d formula of d strength of d orang outang it be more a seven to one in relation to man. but bertran he haf kill bimi mit sooch ding a gott gif him. dot be d miracle. 
the infernal clamour in the cage recommence. aha. dot friend of ours haf still too much ego in his cosmos. be quiet dou. 
han hiss long and venomously. we could hear the great beast quake in his cage. 
but why in the world didn t you help bertran instead of let him be kill. i ask. 
my friend say han composedly stretch himself to slumber it be not nice even to mineself dot i should live after i haf see dot room mit d hole in d thatch. und bertran he be her husband. goot night und sleep well. 
moti guj mutineer. 
once upon a time there be a coffee planter in india who wish to clear some forest land for coffee plant. when he have cut down all the tree and burn the under wood the stump still remain. dynamite be expensive and slow fire slow. the happy medium for stump clear be the lord of all beat who be the elephant. he will either push the stump out of the grind with his tusk if he ha any or drag it out with rope. the planter therefore hire elephant by one and two and three and fell to work. the very best of all the elephant belong to the very bad of all the driver or mahout. and the superior beast s name be moti guj. he be the absolute property of his mahout which would never have be the case under native rule for moti guj be a creature to be desire by king. and his name be translate mean the pearl elephant. because the british government be in the land deesa the mahout enjoy his property undisturbed. he be dissipate. when he have make much money through the strength of his elephant he would get extremely drink and give moti guj a beat with a tent peg over the tender nail of the forefoot. moti guj never trample the life out of deesa on these occasion for he know that after the beat be over deesa would embrace his trunk and weep and call him his love and his life and the liver of his soul and give him some liquor. moti guj be very fond of liquor arrack for choice though he would drink palm tree toddy if nothing good offer. then deesa would go to sleep between moti guj s forefoot and a deesa generally choose the middle of the public road and a moti guj mount guard over him and would not permit horse foot or cart to pas by traffic be congest till deesa saw fit to wake up. 
there be no sleep in the daytime on the planter s clear. the wage be too high to risk. deesa sit on moti guj s neck and give him order while moti guj root up the stump for he own a magnificent pair of tusk. or pull at the end of a rope for he have a magnificent pair of shoulder while deesa kick him behind the ear and say he be the king of elephant. at even time moti guj would wash down his three hundred pound weight of green food with a quart of arrack and deesa would take a share and sing song between moti guj s leg till it be time to go to bed. once a week deesa lead moti guj down to the river and moti guj lay on his side luxuriously in the shallow while deesa go over him with a coir swab and a brick. moti guj never mistake the pound blow of the latter for the smack of the former that warn him to get up and turn over on the other side. then deesa would look at his foot and examine his eye and turn up the fringe of his mighty ear in case of sore or bud ophthalmia. after inspection the two would come up with a song from the sea moti guj all black and shin wave a tear tree branch twelve foot long in his trunk and deesa knot up his own long wet hair. 
it be a peaceful well pay life till deesa felt the return of the desire to drink deep. he wish for an orgie. the little draught that lead nowhere be take the manhood out of him. 
he go to the planter and my mother s dead say he weep. 
she die on the last plantation two month ago. and she die once before that when you be work for me last year say the planter who know something of the way of nativedom. 
then it s my aunt and she be just the same a a mother to me say deesa weep more than ever. she ha leave eighteen small child entirely without bread and it be i who must fill their little stomach say deesa beat his head on the floor. 
who bring you the news. say the planter. 
the post say deesa. 
there hasn t be a post here for the past week. get back to your line. 
a devastate sickness ha fall on my village and all my wife be die yell deesa really in tear this time. 
call chihun who come from deesa s village say the planter. chihun ha this man a wife. 
he. say chihun. no. not a woman of our village would look at him. they d sooner marry the elephant. chihun snort. deesa weep and bellow. 
you will get into a difficulty in a minute say the planter. go back to your work. 
now i will speak heaven s truth gulp deesa with an inspiration. i haven t be drink for two month. i desire to depart in order to get properly drink afar off and distant from this heavenly plantation. thus i shall cause no trouble. 
a flicker smile cross the planter s face. deesa say he you ve speak the truth and i d give you leave on the spot if anything could be do with moti guj while you re away. you know that he will only obey your order. 
may the light of the heaven live forty thousand year. i shall be absent but ten little day. after that upon my faith and honour and soul i return. a to the inconsiderable interval have i the gracious permission of the heaven bear to call up moti guj. 
permission be grant and in answer to deesa s shrill yell the lordly tusker swing out of the shade of a clump of tree where he have be squirt dust over himself till his master should return. 
light of my heart protector of the drunken mountain of might give ear say deesa stand in front of him. 
moti guj give ear and salute with his trunk. i be go away say deesa. 
moti guj s eye twinkle. he like jaunt a well a his master. one could snatch all manner of nice thing from the roadside then. 
but you you fubsy old pig must stay behind and work. 
the twinkle die out a moti guj try to look delight. he hat stump haul on the plantation. it hurt his teeth. 
i shall be go for ten day o delectable one. hold up your near forefoot and i ll impress the fact upon it warty toad of a dry mud puddle. deesa take a tent peg and bang moti guj ten time on the nail. moti guj grunt and shuffle from foot to foot. 
ten day say deesa you must work and haul and root tree a chihun here shall order you. take up chihun and set him on your neck. moti guj curl the tip of his trunk chihun put his foot there and be swing on to the neck. deesa hand chihun the heavy ankus the iron elephant goad. 
chihun thump moti guj s bald head a a paviour thump a kerbstone. 
moti guj trumpet. 
be still hog of the backwoods. chihun s your mahout for ten day. and now bid me good bye beast after mine own heart. oh my lord my king. jewel of all create elephant lily of the herd preserve your honour health. be virtuous. adieu. 
moti guj lap his trunk round deesa and swing him into the air twice. that be his way of bid the man good bye. 
he ll work now say dessa to the planter. have i leave to go. 
the planter nod and deesa dive into the wood. moti guj go back to haul stump. 
chihun be very kind to him but he felt unhappy and forlorn notwithstanding. chihun give him ball of spice and tickle him under the chin and chihun s little baby coo to him after work be over and chihun s wife call him a darling. but moti guj be a bachelor by instinct a deesa be. he do not understand the domestic emotion. he want the light of his universe back again the drink and the drunken slumber the savage beating and the savage caress. 
none the le he work well and the planter wonder. deesa have vagabond along the road till he meet a marriage procession of his own caste and drink dance and tipple have drift past all knowledge of the lapse of time. 
the morning of the eleventh day dawn and there return no deesa. moti guj be loose from his rope for the daily stint. he swing clear look round shrug his shoulder and begin to walk away a one have business elsewhere. 
hi. ho. come back you shout chihun. come back and put me on your neck misborn mountain. return splendour of the hillside. adornment of all india heave to or i ll bang every toe off your fat fore foot. 
moti guj gurgle gently but do not obey. chihun run after him with a rope and catch him up. moti guj put his ear forward and chihun know what that mean though he try to carry it off with high word. 
none of your nonsense with me say he. to your picket devil son. 
hrrump. say moti guj and that be all that and the forebent ear. 
moti guj put his hand in his pocket chew a branch for a toothpick and stroll about the clear make jest of the other elephant who have just set to work. 
chihun report the state of affair to the planter who come out with a dog whip and crack it furiously. moti guj pay the white man the compliment of charge him nearly a quarter of a mile across the clear and hrrumping him into the verandah. then he stand outside the house chuckle to himself and shake all over with the fun of it a an elephant will. 
we ll thrash him say the planter. he shall have the fine thrash that ever elephant receive. give kala nag and nazim twelve foot of chain apiece and tell them to lay on twenty blow. 
kala nag which mean black snake and nazim be two of the big elephant in the line and one of their duty be to administer the grave punishment since no man can beat an elephant properly. 
they take the whip chain and rattle them in their trunk a they sidle up to moti guj mean to hustle him between them. moti guj have never in all his life of thirty nine year be whip and he do not intend to open new experience. so he wait weave his head from right to leave and measure the precise spot in kala nag s fat side where a blunt tusk would sink deep. kala nag have no tusk. the chain be his badge of authority. but he judge it good to swing wide of moti guj at the last minute and seem to appear a if he have bring out the chain for amusement. nazim turn round and go home early. he do not feel fight fit that morning and so moti guj be leave stand alone with his ear cock. 
that decide the planter to argue no more and moti guj roll back to his inspection of the clear. an elephant who will not work and be not tie up be not quite so manageable a an eighty one ton gun loose in a heavy sea way. he slap old friend on the back and ask them if the stump be come away easily. he talk nonsense concern labour and the inalienable right of elephant to a long nooning. and wander to and fro thoroughly demoralize the garden till sundown when he return to his picket for food. 
if you win t work you shan t eat say chihun angrily. you re a wild elephant and no educate animal at all. go back to your jungle. 
chihun s little brown baby roll on the floor of the hut stretch it fat arm to the huge shadow in the doorway. moti guj know well that it be the dear thing on earth to chihun. he swing out his trunk with a fascinate crook at the end and the brown baby throw itself shout upon it. moti guj make fast and pull up till the brown baby be crow in the air twelve foot above his father s head. 
great chief. say chihun. flour cake of the best twelve in number two foot across and soak in rum shall be yours on the instant and two hundred pound weight of fresh cut young sugar cane therewith. deign only to put down safely that insignificant brat who be my heart and my life to me. 
moti guj tuck the brown baby comfortably between his forefoot that could have knock into toothpick all chihun s hut and wait for his food. he eat it and the brown baby crawl away. moti guj doze and think of deesa. one of many mystery connect with the elephant be that his huge body need le sleep than anything else that life. four or five hour in the night suffice two just before midnight lie down on one side. two just after one o clock lie down on the other. the rest of the silent hour be fill with eat and fidget and long grumble soliloquy. 
at midnight therefore moti guj stride out of his picket for a think have come to him that deesa might be lie drink somewhere in the dark forest with none to look after him. so all that night he chase through the undergrowth blow and trumpet and shake his ear. he go down to the river and blare across the shallow where deesa use to wash him but there be no answer. he could not find deesa but he disturb all the elephant in the line and nearly frighten to death some gypsy in the wood. 
at dawn deesa return to the plantation. he have be very drink indeed and he expect to fall into trouble for outstay his leave. he draw a long breath when he saw that the bungalow and the plantation be still uninjured. for he know something of moti guj s temper. and report himself with many lie and salaam. moti guj have go to his picket for breakfast. his night exercise have make him hungry. 
call up your beast say the planter and deesa shout in the mysterious elephant language that some mahout believe come from china at the birth of the world when elephant and not men be master. moti guj hear and come. elephant do not gallop. they move from spot at vary rate of speed. if an elephant wish to catch an express train he could not gallop but he could catch the train. thus moti guj be at the planter s door almost before chihun notice that he have leave his picket. he fell into deesa s arm trumpet with joy and the man and beast weep and slobber over each other and handle each other from head to heel to see that no harm have befall. 
now we will get to work say deesa. lift me up my son and my joy. 
moti guj swing him up and the two go to the coffee clear to look for irksome stump. 
the planter be too astonish to be very angry. 
l envoi. 
my new cut ashlar take the light where crimson blank the window flare. by my own work before the night great overseer i make my prayer. 
if there be good in that i work thy hand compel it master thine. where i have fail to meet thy think i know through thee the blame be mine. 
one instant s toil to thee deny stand all eternity s offence of that i do with thee to guide to thee through thee be excellence. 
who l all think of eden fade bring st eden to the craftsman s brain godlike to muse o er his own trade and manlike stand with god again. 
the depth and dream of my desire the bitter path wherein i stray thou knowest who hast make the fire thou knowest who hast make the clay. 
one stone the more swing to her place in that dread temple of thy worth it be enough that through thy grace i saw naught common on thy earth. 
take not that vision from my ken. oh whatso er may spoil or speed help me to need no aid from men that i may help such men a need.
